Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Legal Nature of Mudaraba
Definition and legal nature of mudaraba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of mudaraba, identify the three legal statuses of the mudarib, and list the essential conditions for a valid mudaraba contract.

Core Idea
Mudaraba is a partnership of capital and labor where the mudarib is a trustee, agent, and profit-sharer.

Mudaraba (commenda partnership) is a foundational contract in Islamic finance. This lesson unpacks its definition, the legal roles of the working partner (mudarib), and the conditions required for its validity. Understanding these basics ensures you can distinguish a valid mudaraba from similar but invalid arrangements.

Guided Path
1
Define mudaraba and its linguistic origin
Read the definition: mudaraba is a partnership with capital from one side and labor from the other. Note its Quranic basis from 'darb fi al-ard' (traveling for trade).
The term is derived from Surah al-Muzzammil 73:20.
2
Identify the three legal statuses of the mudarib
The text states the mudarib is amin (trustee), wakil (agent) in transactions, and sharik (partner) in profit. Understand why each status matters: amin for liability, wakil for authority, sharik for profit entitlement.
These statuses determine the mudarib's rights and responsibilities.
3
List the conditions for a valid mudaraba
Extract conditions: capital must be in currency (thaman), known, profit share must be specified, contract must be expressed with proper wording. Note that stipulating all profit for one party invalidates the contract.
Mudaraba on a debt of the mudarib is invalid; on a debt of a third party is permissible but disliked.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a case where someone says 'Take this 1000 and buy a garment in halves.' The text explains this is not mudaraba but a void ijarah. Practice distinguishing valid and invalid formulations.
The key is that the mudarib must have freedom to trade, not be restricted to a specific purchase.

كتاب المضاربة إلخ المضاربة كالمصالحة من حيث إنها تقتضي وجود البدل من جانب، ثم هي الضرب في الأرض، وهو السير، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَآخَرُونَ يَضْرِبُونَ ﴾ (المزمل: ۲۰ ) يعني الذين يسافرون في الأرض في التجارة، وسمي هذا العقد بها؛ لأن المضارب يسير في الأرض غالباً لطلب الربح، وأهل الحجاز يسمون هذا العقد مقارضة وقراضاً من القرض؛ لأن صاحب المال يقطع قدراً من ماله ويسلمه للعامل، وأصحابنا اختاروا لفظة المضاربة؛ لكونها موافقة للنص. رمز الحقائق ۲۳٩/٢] (ملا مسكين) هي شركة إلخ : فلو شرط كل الربح لأحدهما لا يكون مضاربة، ويجوز التفاوت في الربح، وإذا كان المال من اثنين، فلابد من تساويهما فيما فضل من الربح حتى لو شرط لأحدهما الثلثان وللآخر الثلث فيما فضل، فهو بينهما نصفين؛ لاستوائهما في رأس المال وركنها اللفظ الدال عليها كقوله: دفعت إليك هذا المال مضاربة أو مفاوضة أو معاملة أو خذ هذا المال واعمل به على أن لك من الربح نصفه أو ثلثه، أو قال: ابتع به متاعاً، فما من فضل فلك كذا، أو خذ ذلك بالنصف، بخلاف خذ هذه الألف واشتر بها هروياً بالنصف، ولم يزد عليه، فليس بمضاربة بل إجارة فاسدة له أجر مثله إن اشترى، وليس له البيع إلا بأمر. وشرطها: أن يكون رأس المال . الأثمان وهو معلوم، ويكفي الإعلام بالإشارة فإن اختلفا في مقدار رأس المال عند
كان
من
قسمة الربح فالقول للمضارب مع يمينه والبينة لرب المال، وأما المضاربة ،بدين فإن كان على المضارب فلا يصح، وما اشتراه له والدين في ذمته وإن كان على غيره بأن قال: اقبض مالي على فلان ثم اعمل به مضاربة، فهو جائز وإن كان مكروها؛ لأنه شرط لنفسه منفعة قبل العقد كما في "المبسوط"، ولو قال اقبض ديني على فلان، ثم اعمل به مضاربة فعمل قبل أن يقبض كله يضمن ولو قال: فاعمل به لا يضمن البحر الرائق: ۳۷۸/۷] أمين إلخ: هذا بيان حكم المضاربة أي المضارب أمين بعد قبض رأس المال قبل التصرف فيه؛ لأنه قبضه بإذن مالكه لا على وجه البدل والوثيقة. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۹/۲] واحترز بقوله: "لا" على وجه البدل" عن المقبوض
على سوم الشراء، وبقوله: "والوثيقة" عن المقبوض بحكم الرهن كما في "الدرر". (فتح، ملا مسكين) وكيل: لأنه يتصرف فيه له بأمره، حتى يرجع بما لحقه من العهدة على رب المال، "درر". (فتح) شريك: أي لرب المال في الربح؛ لأنه هو المقصود من عقد المضاربة رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٩/٢] وقال في "الفتح": لأنه حصل بالمال والعمل.
The Book of Mudaraba: Definition of Mudaraba and Its Ruling. Mudaraba is a partnership with capital from one side and work from the other. The mudarib is a trustee (amin), an agent (wakil) in transactions, and a partner (sharik) in profit. (Explanation): After receipt of capital before acting upon it. It is a verbal noun from 'daraba'. (Commentary from Mulla Miskin): Mudaraba is like a compromise in that it requires a consideration from one side. Then it is striking in the land, i.e., travel. Allah says: 'And others striking in the land' meaning those who travel for trade. The contract is named thus because the mudarib frequently travels for profit. The Hijazis call it muqarada or qirad. Our scholars chose 'mudaraba' because it agrees with the text. If profit is stipulated entirely for one party, it is not mudaraba. Disparity in profit is permissible. If capital is from two, they must be equal in the surplus profit; even if one is given two-thirds and the other one-third of the surplus, it is half each because they are equal in capital. Its pillar (rukn) is the word indicating it, such as 'I give you this capital as mudaraba, muqawada, or mu'amala' or 'take this capital and work with it on condition that you have half or a third of the profit' or 'buy goods with it, and whatever surplus is yours to such amount' or 'take it in halves'. But if he says 'take this thousand and buy a Herawi garment in halves' without more, it is not mudaraba but a void ijarah; he gets the equivalent wage if he buys, and he may not sell without permission. Its condition: capital must be in currency (thaman) and known; notification by gesture suffices. If they differ about the amount at division of profit, the mudarib's word with his oath is taken, and the evidence is for the owner of capital. As for mudaraba with a debt: if the debt is on the mudarib, it is not valid, and what he buys is for him with the debt in his liability. If the debt is on another, e.g., 'collect my money from so-and-so then work with it as mudaraba', it is permissible though disliked, because he stipulated a benefit for himself before the contract as in al-Mabsut. If he says 'collect my debt from so-and-so then work with it as mudaraba' and he works before collecting it all, he is liable. If he says 'then work with it', he is not liable. (from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq). Amin etc.: This is a statement of the ruling of mudaraba, i.e., the mudarib is a trustee after receiving the capital before acting upon it, because he took it with the owner's permission not as a substitute or pledge. (Commentary): He distinguishes 'not as a substitute' from what is taken for the purpose of purchase, and 'pledge' from what is taken as a pledge, as in al-Durar. He is an agent because he acts upon it by his order, so that any liability incurred reverts to the owner of the capital. He is a partner for the owner of capital in profit, because that is the purpose of the mudaraba contract, as in al-Fath: because it is achieved by capital and work.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq defines mudaraba (a commenda partnership) and its legal effects. The author begins by identifying the text as the Book of Mudaraba. He defines mudaraba as a partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor. The mudarib (working partner) has three legal statuses: as amin (trustee) regarding the capital, as wakil (agent) in transactions, and as sharik (partner) in profit. The commentary by Mulla Miskin expands: The term 'mudaraba' is derived from 'darb fi al-ard' (traveling), supported by Quran 73:20. The Hijazis call it 'qirad'. The Hanafi scholars prefer 'mudaraba' because it matches the Quranic usage. The commentary then lists conditions: profit cannot be entirely for one party; disparity in profit shares is allowed; if two people provide capital, they must share the surplus profit equally even if they stipulate unequal shares, because they are equal in capital. The pillar (rukn) is the verbal offer. It gives examples of valid and invalid formulations. A condition is that capital must be in known currency (thaman), and notification by indication suffices. In case of dispute over the capital amount, the mudarib's statement with oath is accepted, but the capital owner can provide evidence. The passage then discusses mudaraba with a debt: if the debt is on the mudarib himself, the contract is invalid; if the debt is owed by someone else, it is permissible but makruh (disliked). Finally, it explains why the mudarib is a trustee: he receives the capital with permission, not as a substitute or pledge, distinguishing it from other forms of possession.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-mudaraba): A contract of partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit shared according to agreement.
المضارب (al-mudarib): The working partner who manages the capital in a mudaraba contract.
الأثمان (al-athman): Currency; specifically gold, silver, or their equivalents that serve as money.
الربح (al-ribh): Surplus profit generated from the mudaraba after return of capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of the mudarib in a valid mudaraba contract?
A) A debtor
B) A trustee, agent, and partner in profit
C) A guarantor of the capital
D) An employee with fixed wage

Key Takeaway
Mudaraba is a permissible partnership contract where the mudarib is a trustee of capital, an agent in trade, and a partner in profit, subject to conditions including known currency capital and specified profit share.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Understanding Mudarabah: Definition and the Mudarib's Legal Status
Defining mudarabah and clarifying the mudarib's legal roles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of mudarabah, identify its essential conditions, and explain the three legal roles of the mudarib (amin, wakil, sharik).

Core Idea
Mudarabah: a partnership of capital and work; the mudarib is a trustee, agent, and profit-sharer.

This lesson unpacks the classical Hanafi definition of mudarabah — a foundational contract in Islamic finance. You will learn not only what mudarabah is, but why the mudarib occupies three distinct legal positions: trustee (amin) for the capital, agent (wakil) in transactions, and partner (sharik) in profit. Understanding these roles is key to determining liability and profit distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract's core elements
Examine the definition: 'partnership with capital from one side and work from the other'. Note that both capital and labour are essential; if both sides provide capital, it becomes a different contract (inan partnership).
The term 'sharika' (partnership) indicates shared profit.
2
Derive the mudarib's status as amin
The mudarib is a trustee (amin) after receiving capital but before disposing of it. This means he is not liable for loss unless he breaches the trust. Contrast with a borrower (damin) or hired worker (ajir).
Amin status protects the mudarib from liability for accidental loss.
3
Derive the mudarib's status as wakil
When transacting, the mudarib acts as an agent (wakil) of the capital owner. His actions bind the owner, and any debts from trade are the owner's responsibility.
As wakil, the mudarib does not personally guarantee the capital.
4
Derive the mudarib's status as sharik
In profit, the mudarib is a partner (sharik). He receives an agreed share (e.g., half or one-third), not a fixed wage. This distinguishes mudarabah from an invalid hire contract.
If all profit is stipulated for one party, the contract is not mudarabah.
5
Identify the conditions and pillars
The capital must be in monetary form (gold/silver dirhams/dinars) and known. The pillar (rukn) is the verbal expression indicating the contract. Note that if the capital is a debt owed by the mudarib himself, the contract is invalid.
Knowledge of the capital amount avoids gharar (uncertainty).

Source Text

كتاب المضاربة
تعريف المضاربة وحكمها
كتاب المضاربة
هي شركة بمال من جانب وعمل من جانب والمضارب أمين، وبالتصرف وكيل، أي في الربح وبالربح شريك، أي إذا ربح فهو أي رب المال أي المضارب بعد القبض قبل التصرف أي فيه مفاعلة من كتاب المضاربة إلخ المضاربة كالمصالحة من حيث إنها تقتضي وجود البدل من جانب، ثم هي الضرب في الأرض، وهو السير، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَآخَرُونَ يَضْرِبُونَ ﴾ (المزمل: 20 ) يعني الذين يسافرون في الأرض في التجارة، وسمي هذا العقد بها؛ لأن المضارب يسير في الأرض غالباً لطلب الربح، وأهل الحجاز يسمون هذا العقد مقارضة وقراضاً من القرض؛ لأن صاحب المال يقطع قدراً من ماله ويسلمه للعامل، وأصحابنا اختاروا لفظة المضاربة؛ لكونها موافقة للنص. رمز الحقائق 239/2] (ملا مسكين) هي شركة إلخ : فلو شرط كل الربح لأحدهما لا يكون مضاربة، ويجوز التفاوت في الربح، وإذا كان المال من اثنين، فلابد من تساويهما فيما فضل من الربح حتى لو شرط لأحدهما الثلثان وللآخر الثلث فيما فضل، فهو بينهما نصفين؛ لاستوائهما في رأس المال وركنها اللفظ الدال عليها كقوله: دفعت إليك هذا المال مضاربة أو مفاوضة أو معاملة أو خذ هذا المال واعمل به على أن لك من الربح نصفه أو ثلثه، أو قال: ابتع به متاعاً، فما من فضل فلك كذا، أو خذ ذلك بالنصف، بخلاف خذ هذه الألف واشتر بها هروياً بالنصف، ولم يزد عليه، فليس بمضاربة بل إجارة فاسدة له أجر مثله إن اشترى، وليس له البيع إلا بأمر. وشرطها: أن يكون رأس المال الأثمان وهو معلوم، ويكفي الإعلام بالإشارة فإن اختلفا في مقدار رأس المال عند قسمة الربح فالقول للمضارب مع يمينه والبينة لرب المال، وأما المضاربة بدين فإن كان على المضارب فلا يصح، وما اشتراه له والدين في ذمته وإن كان على غيره بأن قال: اقبض مالي على فلان ثم اعمل به مضاربة، فهو جائز وإن كان مكروها؛ لأنه شرط لنفسه منفعة قبل العقد كما في المبسوط، ولو قال اقبض ديني على فلان، ثم اعمل به مضاربة فعمل قبل أن يقبض كله يضمن ولو قال: فاعمل به لا يضمن البحر الرائق: 378/7] أمين إلخ: هذا بيان حكم المضاربة أي المضارب أمين بعد قبض رأس المال قبل التصرف فيه؛ لأنه قبضه بإذن مالكه لا على وجه البدل والوثيقة. [رمز الحقائق: 239/2] واحترز بقوله: لا على وجه البدل عن المقبوض على سوم الشراء، وبقوله: والوثيقة عن المقبوض بحكم الرهن كما في الدرر. (فتح، ملا مسكين) وكيل: لأنه يتصرف فيه له بأمره، حتى يرجع بما لحقه من العهدة على رب المال، درر. (فتح) شريك: أي لرب المال في الربح؛ لأنه هو المقصود من عقد المضاربة رمز الحقائق: 239/2] وقال في الفتح: لأنه حصل بالمال والعمل.
Book of Mudarabah. Definition of Mudarabah and its ruling. Book of Mudarabah: It is a partnership with capital from one side and work from the other. The mudarib is a trustee (amin), and with respect to disposition he is an agent (wakil), and with respect to profit he is a partner (sharik). ... And their condition [of validity] is that the capital be monetary (al-athman) and known...
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage defines mudarabah (a partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor) and explains the legal status of the mudarib (the working partner). The passage begins by noting that mudarabah, like a compromise (musalaha), involves consideration from one side. It then discusses the linguistic and legal origin of the term, citing the Quranic verse (73:20) using the word yadribun (traveling). The Hanafis preferred the term mudarabah because it aligns with the Quranic text, while the Hijazis use muqaradah or qirad. The passage then explains that if all profit is stipulated for one party, it is not mudarabah. Profit may be shared unequally, but if two people contribute capital, they must share the surplus profit equally because they are equal in capital. The pillar (rukn) of mudarabah is the verbal offer and acceptance. The condition for validity is that the capital be in monetary form (dirhams and dinars) and known. The mudarib is a trustee (amin) after taking possession but before acting, an agent (wakil) when acting, and a partner (sharik) in profit. The commentary from various sources clarifies these definitions and gives examples.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudarabah): A contract of partnership in profit where one party provides capital (rabb al-mal) and the other provides work (mudarib).
المضارب (al-mudarib): The working partner who manages the capital and receives a share of the profit.
أمين (amin): Trustee; the mudarib is not liable for loss of the capital unless he transgresses.
وكيل (wakil): Agent; the mudarib acts on behalf of the capital owner in transactions.
شريك (sharik): Partner; the mudarib shares in the profit according to the agreed ratio.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mudarib's status after receiving the capital but before beginning any transactions?
A) Guarantor (damin)
B) Trustee (amin)
C) Agent (wakil)
D) Partner (sharik)

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is a partnership of capital and labour; the mudarib is an amin, wakil, and sharik, and the capital must be monetary and known.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Rulings on Invalid Mudarabah and Valid Capital Types
Fiqh passage listing legal consequences of invalid mudarabah and conditions for validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal consequences of a fasid mudarabah and identify the conditions for a valid mudarabah capital according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In fasid mudarabah, the mudarib is an ajir entitled to ajr al-mithl; valid mudarabah requires gold/silver coins, not commodities.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the ahkam of mudarabah: the legal effects when the contract is corrupt and the essential conditions for validity. The Hanafi school treats a fasid mudarabah not as void but as creating a quasi-employment relationship, while valid mudarabah requires capital in dirhams/dinars. We will unpack each consequence and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios of invalid mudarabah
From the text (بالفساد أجير، وبالخلاف غاصب، وباشتراط كل الربح له مستقرض، وباشتراطه لرب المال مستبضع), list the four cases: corrupt contract, contravention, mudarib stipulates all profit, rabb al-mal stipulates all profit.
2
Understand the ruling for each scenario
For each, the mudarib is classified as ajir (hired worker), ghasib (usurper), mustaqrid (borrower), or mustabdi' (volunteer). Explain the legal consequence: e.g., in fasid, he gets ajr al-mithl; in contravention, he is liable even if owner later approves.
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on ajr al-mithl between Abu Yusuf (limited to agreed profit) and Muhammad (unlimited).
3
Analyze the condition for valid mudarabah: capital type
The text states that mudarabah is valid only with what partnership is valid with – dirhams and dinars (gold/silver coins). Muhammad adds current fulus (copper coins). This is based on the hadith 'no profit without liability'.
The prohibition of commodities is tied to the risk of profit without guarantee.
4
Examine the cross-madhhab dispute on capital type
Ibn Abi Layla and Malik allow mudarabah with weighed/measured goods. The Hanafi response: commodities are 'urud; their value may fluctuate, leading to profit without liability, which is prohibited.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): In Hanafi, such a contract is fasid; in Maliki, it may be valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام المضاربة
وبالفساد أجير، وبالخلاف غاصب وباشتراط كل الربح له مستقرض، وباشتراطه أي فساد المضاربة لرب المال مستبضع، وإنما تصح بما تصح به الشركة. أي بمال من الدراهم والدنانير أي للمضارب كل الربح

بالفساد أجير: أي بفساد المضاربة أجير؛ لأن الواجب في المضاربة الفاسدة أجر المثل، فيكون هو أجيراً، كما في الإجارة الفاسدة. [رمز الحقائق: 239/2] وقال في الفتح: حتى يستوجب أجر المثل كالإجارة الفاسدة مطلقاً، سواء ربح أو لا، بلا زيادة على المشروط كالإجارة الفاسدة، ولا ضمان فيها كالصحيحة؛ لأنه أمين، فلا يكون ضميناً، درر وقوله: بلا زيادة على المشروط هو مذهب أبي يوسف وعند محمد والثلاثة: يجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ. واستثنى في الأشباه من لزوم أجر المثل في المضاربة الفاسدة ما إذا أخذ الوصي مال اليتيم مضاربة فاسدة كشرطه لنفسه عشرة دراهم، فلا شيء له في مال اليتيم إذا عمل، وجرى عليه في التنوير، وظاهره أن أن يضارب في مال اليتيم بجزء من الربح، وكلام الزيلعي فيه أظهر، وأفاد الزيلعي أيضاً أن للوصي دفع المال إلى من يعمل فيه مضاربة بطريق النيابة عن التسليم كأبيه. للوصي

وبالخلاف غاصب : أي إذا خالف المضارب لرب المال فيما فوضه إليه، فهو غاصب ضامن؛ لأنه إذا خالف فقد تعدى فصار غاصباً فيضمن وإن أجاز بعد ذلك حتى لو اشترى ما نهي عنه، ثم باعه، وتصرف، ثم أجاز المال، رب فإنه لا أثر لإجازته خلافاً لمالك ملا مسكين وباشتراط إلخ أي باشتراط المضارب بأن يكون كل الربح له مستقرض أي طالب قرض يقال : استقرض من فلان إذا طلب منه القرض؛ لأنه لا يستحق الربح كله إلا إذا صار المال كله ملكاً له؛ لأن الربح فرع المال كالثمر للشجر، فإذا شرط أن يكون جميع الربح له، فقد ملك جميع رأس المال، فلا يكون هذا إلا بطريق القرض رمز الحقائق: 239/2]

مستبضع أي طالب بضاعة، وهي أن يعمل له متبرعاً؛ لأنه لم يطلب لعمله بدلاً فكان متبرعاً، فهذا معنى البضاعة، فكأنه نص عليها. رمز الحقائق: 239/2] وإنما تصح إلخ : أي وإنما تصح المضاربة بما تصح به الشركة الدراهم والدنانير عندهما، وعند محمد بهما وبالفلوس الرائجة، ولو دفع إليه عرضاً، وقال له: بعه واعمل به مضاربة في ثمنه، فباع بدراهم أو بدنانير فتصرف صح (ملا مسكين) وقال في الفتح: لا يصح؛ لنهيه عليه عن ربح ما لم يضمن، والمضاربة بغير النقود تؤدي إليه؛ لأنها أمانة في يد المضارب، وربما زادت قيمتها بعد العقد، فإذا باعها شركه في الربح فحصل ربح ما لم يضمن؛ إذ المضارب يستحق نصيبه من غير أن يدخل شيء في ضمانه؛ بخلاف النقود؛ فإنه عند الشراء بها يجب الثمن في ذمته؛ لأنها لا تتعين بالتعيين، فما يحصل له بذلك فهو ربح ما ضمن والمكيل والموزون عروض. (زيلعي)

بما تصح به الشركة إلخ وهي الدراهم والدنانير لا غير عندهما، والفلوس النافقة عند محمد مثلهما، وقد مر في الشركة، وقال ابن أبي ليلى تصح المضاربة في المكيل والموزون؛ لأنهما من ذوات الأمثال، فيمكن تقدير
Rulings of Mudarabah. And with corruption [of the contract] he is a hired worker (ajir), and with contravention [of instructions] he is a usurper (ghasib), and with stipulation of all profit for himself he is a borrower (mustaqrid), and with stipulation of all profit for the capital owner he is a party to a commenda (mustabdi'). And it is valid only with what partnership is valid with, i.e., wealth of dirhams and dinars. ...
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents the rulings (ahkam) of mudarabah, specifically the legal consequences when the contract becomes invalid (fasid) and the conditions for its validity. The passage enumerates four scenarios: (1) If the mudarabah is corrupt (fasid), the mudarib is considered a hired worker (ajir) and is entitled to the like wage (ajr al-mithl). (2) If the mudarib contravenes the capital owner's instructions, he becomes a usurper (ghasib) and is liable, and subsequent approval by the owner does not remove liability, contrary to the Maliki school. (3) If the mudarib stipulates all profit for himself, it is effectively a loan (qard), making him a borrower. (4) If the capital owner stipulates all profit for himself, it is a commenda (bida'ah), making the mudarib a volunteer. Then the passage discusses the conditions for a valid mudarabah: it requires capital in the form of dirhams and dinars (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; Imam Muhammad also accepts current fulus). There is a discussion about whether mudarabah can be with commodities ('urud) – the preferred Hanafi view is that it is not valid because it leads to profit without guarantee (ribh ma lam yudman). The passage ends with a note that Ibn Abi Layla allowed mudarabah with weighed and measured goods.

Key Terms
أجير (ajir): Hired worker; in a fasid mudarabah, the mudarib is treated as an ajir entitled to ajr al-mithl (like wage).
غاصب (ghasib): Usurper; the mudarib becomes a usurper if he contravenes instructions, making him liable for loss.
مستقرض (mustaqrid): Borrower; if the mudarib stipulates all profit for himself, it is effectively a loan (qard).
مستبضع (mustabdi'): One who gives bida'ah; if the capital owner stipulates all profit for himself, the mudarib is a volunteer (mutabarri').
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The like wage; in a fasid mudarabah, the mudarib receives the standard wage for similar work.
الدراهم والدنانير (al-darahim wa al-dananir): Dirhams and dinars (silver and gold coins) — the only types of capital allowed for valid mudarabah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the consequence if a mudarabah contract is concluded with a commodity ('ard) as capital?
A) The contract is valid and the profit is shared as agreed
B) The contract is fasid and the mudarib receives ajr al-mithl
C) The contract is batil (void) and no compensation is due
D) The mudarib becomes a borrower (mustaqrid)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a fasid mudarabah treats the mudarib as an employed worker, and valid mudarabah requires capital in dirhams or dinars, not commodities.

8 min
Ruling on Invalid Mudaraba: Mudarib as Ajir
Ruling on mudarib being ajir in invalid mudaraba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mudarib in a fasid mudaraba and explain the analogy to invalid ijara.

Core Idea
In an invalid mudaraba, the mudarib becomes an ajir entitled to ajr al-mithl and remains an amin.

When a mudaraba contract contains a condition that renders it fasid (invalid), the mudarib is not without compensation. The Hanafi school treats him as a hired worker (ajir) who deserves the equivalent market wage (ajr al-mithl). This lesson explores the ruling and the analogical reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the legal effect: the mudarib becomes an ajir and gets ajr al-mithl.
2
Understand the analogy
Recognize that this ruling is based on qiyas to invalid ijara.
3
Note the trustee status
The mudarib remains amin, so no daman (liability) for loss of capital.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالفساد أجير: أي بفساد المضاربة أجير؛ لأن الواجب في المضاربة الفاسدة أجر المثل، فيكون هو أجيراً، كما في الإجارة الفاسدة. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۹/۲] وقال في "الفتح": حتى يستوجب أجر المثل كالإجارة الفاسدة مطلقاً، سواء ربح أو لا، بلا زيادة على المشروط كالإجارة الفاسدة، ولا ضمان فيها كالصحيحة؛ لأنه أمين، فلا يكون ضميناً، درر" وقوله: "بلا" زيادة على المشروط" هو مذهب أبي يوسف وعند محمد والثلاثة: يجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ. واستثنى في "الأشباه" من لزوم أجر المثل في المضاربة الفاسدة ما إذا أخذ الوصي مال اليتيم مضاربة فاسدة كشرطه لنفسه عشرة دراهم، فلا شيء له في مال اليتيم إذا عمل، وجرى عليه في "التنوير"، وظاهره أن أن يضارب في مال اليتيم بجزء من الربح، وكلام الزيلعي فيه أظهر، وأفاد الزيلعي أيضاً أن للوصي دفع المال إلى من يعمل فيه مضاربة بطريق النيابة عن التسليم كأبيه.
And with the fasid (invalid) [mudaraba, the mudarib is] an ajir: meaning, due to the invalidity of the mudaraba, he is an ajir; because what is obligatory in an invalid mudaraba is ajr al-mithl (equivalent wage), so he becomes an ajir, just as in an invalid ijara. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/239] And it is said in al-Fath: until he is entitled to ajr al-mithl like an invalid ijara absolutely, whether there is profit or not, without increase over the stipulated [amount] like invalid ijara, and there is no guarantee (daman) in it, like the valid [mudaraba]; because he is an amin (trustee), so he is not a guarantor. Durar. And his statement: "without increase over the stipulated" is the Madhhab of Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad and the Three, the ajr al-mithl is obligatory, whatever it may amount to. And in al-Ashbah an exception is made from the obligation of ajr al-mithl in invalid mudaraba for the case where a guardian takes the property of an orphan in an invalid mudaraba, such as stipulating ten dirhams for himself; then he gets nothing from the orphan's property when he works, and this was followed in al-Tanwir. Its apparent meaning is that he makes a mudaraba on the orphan's property for a share of the profit. The statement of al-Zayla'i on this is clearer, and al-Zayla'i also stated that the guardian may hand over the property to someone to work with it as a mudaraba by way of deputation for delivery, like a father.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn phrase 'وبالفساد أجير' which states the ruling for an invalid mudaraba. The commentary explains that when a mudaraba is fasid (invalid due to a defective condition), the mudarib is treated as an ajir (hireling) because the obligation is ajr al-mithl (equivalent market wage). This is analogous to an invalid ijara contact. The mudarib remains an amin (trustee) and is not a guarantor, so there is no liability for loss of capital. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf, the ajr al-mithl cannot exceed the conditionally stipulated amount; according to Imam Muhammad and the three (likely Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar? Actually the text says 'Muhammad and the Three', which typically refers to the three main students of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar, but here it may mean the other two besides Muhammad? The tarjih is not given), the ajr al-mithl must be paid in full whatever it may be, even if it exceeds the stipulated amount. Finally, an exception is cited from Al-Ashbah: if a guardian (wasi) makes an invalid mudaraba with an orphan's property, such as stipulating a fixed amount for himself, he gets nothing from the orphan's property for his work, because he is not entitled to profit from the orphan's property. The guardian may, however, delegate the mudaraba to another person as a deputy.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The equivalent or market wage for the work performed, not the contractually agreed amount.
أمين (amin): A trustee who holds property with permission and is not liable for loss unless negligent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid mudaraba, what is the mudarib entitled to?
A) The stipulated profit share
B) Ajr al-mithl (equivalent wage)
C) Nothing
D) Guarantee of capital

Key Takeaway
In a fasid mudaraba, the mudarib is an ajir entitled to ajr al-mithl and remains an amin.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Limits of Ajr al-Mithl and Exception for Orphan's Property
Intra-Hanafi dispute and exception for wasi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding ajr al-mithl in fasid mudaraba and explain the exception for a guardian's mudaraba with orphan's property.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf limits ajr al-mithl to the stipulated amount; Muhammad does not; a guardian cannot profit from orphan's property.

The Hanafi school internally differs on whether the mudarib's ajr al-mithl in a fasid mudaraba can exceed the amount he contractually stipulated. Additionally, a special exception arises when the mudarib is a guardian (wasi) of an orphan who makes an invalid mudaraba with the orphan's property. This lesson unpacks these nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Abu Yusuf holds ajr al-mithl cannot exceed stipulated amount; Muhammad and the three hold it can be any amount.
2
Understand the qiyas difference
Abu Yusuf analogizes to invalid ijara where ajr cannot exceed named wage; Muhammad emphasizes the work value.
3
Analyze the exception
A guardian who makes invalid mudaraba with orphan's property by stipulating a fixed amount gets nothing because he cannot profit from the orphan.
4
Note the delegation possibility
The guardian may delegate the mudaraba to a third party as a deputy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالفساد أجير: أي بفساد المضاربة أجير؛ لأن الواجب في المضاربة الفاسدة أجر المثل، فيكون هو أجيراً، كما في الإجارة الفاسدة. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۹/۲] وقال في "الفتح": حتى يستوجب أجر المثل كالإجارة الفاسدة مطلقاً، سواء ربح أو لا، بلا زيادة على المشروط كالإجارة الفاسدة، ولا ضمان فيها كالصحيحة؛ لأنه أمين، فلا يكون ضميناً، درر" وقوله: "بلا" زيادة على المشروط" هو مذهب أبي يوسف وعند محمد والثلاثة: يجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ. واستثنى في "الأشباه" من لزوم أجر المثل في المضاربة الفاسدة ما إذا أخذ الوصي مال اليتيم مضاربة فاسدة كشرطه لنفسه عشرة دراهم، فلا شيء له في مال اليتيم إذا عمل، وجرى عليه في "التنوير"، وظاهره أن أن يضارب في مال اليتيم بجزء من الربح، وكلام الزيلعي فيه أظهر، وأفاد الزيلعي أيضاً أن للوصي دفع المال إلى من يعمل فيه مضاربة بطريق النيابة عن التسليم كأبيه.
And with the fasid (invalid) [mudaraba, the mudarib is] an ajir: meaning, due to the invalidity of the mudaraba, he is an ajir; because what is obligatory in an invalid mudaraba is ajr al-mithl (equivalent wage), so he becomes an ajir, just as in an invalid ijara. The statement of al-Zayla'i on this is clearer, and al-Zayla'i also stated that the guardian may hand over the property to someone to work with it as a mudaraba by way of deputation for delivery, like a father.
Source pages p. 91

The guardian may, however, delegate the mudaraba to another person as a deputy.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The equivalent or market wage for the work performed, not the contractually agreed amount.
مضاربة فاسدة (mudaraba fasida): A mudaraba contract that is invalid due to a condition that violates the principles of the contract, such as unequal profit shares or fixed amounts.
وصي (wasi): A guardian appointed to manage the property of an orphan or minor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad and the Three, the ajr al-mithl in fasid mudaraba is:
A) Limited to the stipulated amount
B) Unlimited, based on the market value
C) Not obligatory
D) Capped at the profit

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf caps ajr al-mithl at the stipulated amount; Muhammad does not; a guardian gets nothing from orphan's property in invalid mudaraba.

Mudarib Breaching Instructions Becomes Ghasib and Dhamin
Ruling on mudarib violating instructions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudarib who violates instructions and explain why ratification does not remove liability.

Core Idea
Violating instructions makes the mudarib a ghasib; liability is not undone by later approval.

In mudarabah, the mudarib is a trustee (amin) with limited authority. If he oversteps that authority by violating the rabb al-mal's instructions, he crosses into the realm of usurpation (ghasb) and becomes strictly liable. This lesson examines the Hanafi position that liability is fixed at the moment of violation and is not erased by subsequent ratification—a point of divergence from the Maliki school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the mudarib who acts contrary to explicit instructions. Determine that this act makes him a ghasib and dhamin.
The mudarib is not simply a trustee; with violation he becomes a usurper.
2
Locate the basis of the ruling
The ruling rests on the principle that violation of instructions constitutes ta'addi (transgression), which triggers liability. No specific proof text is cited; the inference is from the general rules of agency and trust.
This is a ruling derived from legal maxims rather than a direct text.
3
Note the ikhtilaf with Malik
The Hanafi position is contrasted with the Maliki school, which holds that subsequent ratification retroactively validates the action and removes liability.
The disagreement is over the effect of ratification.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, if the mudarib's violation causes a loss, under Hanafi he must compensate even if the rabb al-mal later approves; under Maliki, approval cancels liability.
This is the practical consequence of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالخلاف غاصب : أي إذا خالف المضارب لرب المال فيما فوضه إليه، فهو غاصب ضامن؛ لأنه إذا خالف فقد تعدى فصار غاصباً فيضمن وإن أجاز بعد ذلك حتى لو اشترى ما نهي عنه، ثم باعه، وتصرف، ثم أجاز المال، رب فإنه لا أثر لإجازته خلافاً لمالك
And with violation (al-khilaf) [he is a] ghasib: meaning, if the mudarib violates [the instructions of] the owner of the capital with respect to what was delegated to him, then he is a ghasib (usurper) and dhamin (liable); because if he violates, he has transgressed and thus becomes a usurper, so he is liable, even if he later ratifies [the violation?]. So if he buys what he was forbidden from, then sells it, and transacts, then the owner ratifies, his ratification has no effect, contrary to Malik.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage expands on the matn phrase 'وبالخلاف غاصب'. The ruling is that if the mudarib acts contrary to the specific instructions of the rabb al-mal (e.g., buying a type of goods he was told not to buy), he becomes a ghasib (wrongful usurper) and is liable (dhamin) for any loss. This liability applies even if the rabb al-mal later ratifies the transaction; the ratification does not remove the liability, because the mudarib's action was a transgression at the time. This is in contrast to the Maliki school, which holds that subsequent ratification can invalidate the claim of usurpation. The passage does not provide a specific proof text but derives the ruling from the principle that violation of instructions is a form of transgression (ta'addi), which triggers liability.

Key Terms
غاصب (ghasib): A person who wrongfully takes or uses another's property without right; here, the mudarib who violates instructions.
ضامن (dhamin): Liable or responsible for compensation; the mudarib must make good any loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mudarib buys goods he was forbidden to buy, and later the rabb al-mal approves, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The mudarib is no longer liable
B) The mudarib remains liable for any loss
C) The contract becomes valid
D) The profit is shared differently

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a mudarib who violates instructions becomes a ghasib and remains dhamin even if the investor later ratifies the action.

beginner
6 min
Stipulating All Profit for Mudarib Makes Contract a Loan
Ruling when mudarib stipulates all profit for himself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mudarib stipulates all profit for himself and explain the ta'lil that reclassifies the contract as qard.

Core Idea
All profit for mudarib = ownership of capital = qard, not mudaraba.

Mudaraba requires a known share of profit. If the mudarib demands all profit, he effectively owns the capital. The Hanafi school holds that such a stipulation nullifies the mudaraba and transforms it into a qard (loan). This brief passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the reasoning using the analogy of fruit and tree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the stipulation
The mudarib conditions that all profit from the venture goes to him. This is the key fact.
The stipulation is made by the mudarib, not the rabb al-mal.
2
Apply the Hanafi principle: profit follows capital
Recall that in Hanafi fiqh, profit is considered a branch (far') of capital (asl). One cannot claim all profit without owning the capital itself.
Analogy: fruit belongs to the tree's owner.
3
Recognize ownership implication
By stipulating all profit, the mudarib has effectively taken ownership of the entire capital, because profit cannot be separated from capital ownership.
This is the logical outcome of the principle.
4
Reclassify the contract
Since the mudarib owns the capital, the arrangement is no longer mudaraba but a loan (qard). The mudarib is a borrower (mustaqrid) who must return an equivalent amount.
Qard transfers ownership of the capital to the borrower, who is liable for its return.
5
Note the practical consequence
The original capital provider (rabb al-mal) is now a lender. He cannot claim any profit; he can only demand repayment of the principal. Any actual profit belongs entirely to the mudarib as owner.
This contrasts with a valid mudaraba where profit is shared.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وباشتراط إلخ أي باشتراط المضارب بأن يكون كل الربح له مستقرض أي طالب قرض يقال : استقرض من فلان إذا طلب منه القرض؛ لأنه لا يستحق الربح كله إلا إذا صار المال كله ملكاً له؛ لأن الربح فرع المال كالثمر للشجر، فإذا شرط أن يكون جميع الربح له، فقد ملك جميع رأس المال، فلا يكون هذا إلا بطريق القرض
And with the stipulation of all the profit for him [means] the mudarib is mustaqrid (one seeking a loan); because he is not entitled to all profit unless he owns all the capital; therefore profit is a branch of capital like fruit from a tree; so if he stipulates all profit for himself, he has owned all the capital, so this is only by way of a loan (qard).
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage explains the matn phrase 'وباشتراط كل الربح له مستقرض'. The ruling is that if the mudarib stipulates that all profit from the venture goes to him, the contract is not a mudaraba but rather a qard (loan). The reasoning (ta'lil) is that profit is considered a branch (far') of capital (asl), like fruit to a tree. Therefore, one cannot be entitled to all the profit without owning all the capital. If the mudarib takes all profit, he effectively owns the entire capital, which is the nature of a loan: the borrower takes ownership of the capital and is only obligated to return its equivalent. Hence, the contract is reclassified as a qard, not a mudaraba. The term 'mustaqrid' is derived from 'istiqrad' (seeking a loan).

Key Terms
مستقرض (mustaqrid): One who seeks a loan; here, the mudarib who stipulates all profit is considered to be requesting a loan.
قرض (qard): Loan; a contract where the lender gives property to the borrower with the obligation to return its equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does stipulating all profit for the mudarib make the contract a qard?
A) Because profit must be divided equally in mudaraba
B) Because profit is a branch of capital, so all profit implies ownership of capital
C) Because the mudarib is not entitled to any profit
D) Because the capital provider must guarantee the principal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: mudaraba requires shared profit; stipulating all profit for the mudarib reclassifies the contract into a qard (loan).

Stipulating All Profit for Rabb al-Mal: The Ruling of Bida'a
Definition of mustabdi' and bida'a when all profit is stipulated to rabb al-mal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the rabb al-mal stipulates all profit for himself, distinguish between mudaraba and bida'a, and identify the legal implications for the mudarib.

Core Idea
If the rabb al-mal claims all profit, the mudarib works for free — it becomes a bida'a, not a mudaraba.

In the previous lesson, we learned about the basic structure of mudaraba where profit is shared. But what happens if the capital owner (rabb al-mal) stipulates that all profit belongs to him? This passage explains that such a contract is no longer a mudaraba but a bida'a — a voluntary commodity investment. The worker becomes a volunteer with no claim to profit. Understanding this distinction is crucial because it changes the legal rights and obligations of both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act is making a mudaraba contract with the condition that all profit goes to rabb al-mal.
This condition contradicts the essence of mudaraba (profit-sharing).
2
State the ruling
The contract is not a valid mudaraba but a bida'a (voluntary commodity investment).
The ruling is based on the absence of consideration for the worker.
3
Define the key terms: mustabdi' and bida'a
The rabb al-mal is called 'mustabdi'' (one who seeks a bida'a). The worker is 'mutabarri'' (volunteer). Bida'a means the worker trades the capital as a favor.
These terms are specific to the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the consequence for the worker
The worker receives no profit and works voluntarily; he has no claim to compensation.
The worker is not a mudarib; he is a gratuitous agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستبضع أي طالب بضاعة، وهي أن يعمل له متبرعاً؛ لأنه لم يطلب لعمله بدلاً فكان متبرعاً، فهذا معنى البضاعة، فكأنه نص عليها.
Mustabdi': meaning one who seeks a bida'a (commodity investment), and it is that he works for him voluntarily; because he did not request a compensation for his work, so he is a volunteer. This is the meaning of bida'a, and it is as if he mentioned it.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage explains the matn phrase 'وباشتراطه لرب المال مستبضع'. The ruling is that if the rabb al-mal stipulates all profit for himself, the contract is not a mudaraba but rather a bida'a (a form of voluntary commodity investment). The mudarib becomes a mutabarri' (volunteer) who works without any claim to profit. He is called 'mustabdi'' (seeking to place a bida'a). The term 'bida'a' refers to a transaction where one party gives goods to another to trade, with the understanding that the worker receives no profit and works solely as a favor. The passage simply states this as a fact without further elaboration.

Key Terms
مستبضع (mustabdi'): One who seeks a bida'a; the rabb al-mal who gives capital with the condition that all profit goes to him.
بضاعة (bida'a): A voluntary commodity investment where the worker receives no share of profit; acts as a favor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the owner of capital stipulates all profit for himself, what type of contract does it become?
A) Mudaraba
B) Qard
C) Bida'a
D) Ijara

Key Takeaway
Stipulating all profit for the rabb al-mal transforms the contract into a bida'a, where the worker is a volunteer with no profit share.

Valid Capital for Mudaraba: Dirhams, Dinars, and the Fulus Dispute
Ruling on the validity of capital for mudaraba; dispute on fulus and commodities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on valid capital for mudaraba and evaluate the objections of Malik and Ibn Abi Layla.

Core Idea
Mudaraba capital must be something the mudarib guarantees — only currency (or fulus per Muhammad) qualifies.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a fundamental condition of mudaraba: the type of capital. The Hanafi school restricts valid capital to dirhams and dinars (gold and silver currency), with a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement on copper coins (fulus). Beyond the school, Ibn Abi Layla and Malik allow commodities, but the Hanafis respond with a hadith-based argument. Understanding this dispute reveals the school's rigorous approach to liability and profit allocation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi consensus and divergence
State the ruling that mudaraba is valid only with what makes shirkah valid — dirhams and dinars according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and also fulus according to Muhammad. Recognize that this is a ruling-with-proof with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The matn implicitly endorses Muhammad's view by stating 'with what makes shirkah valid'.
2
Work through the commodity example
Analyze the scenario: a person gives a commodity (عرض) and says 'sell it and use the price as mudaraba capital.' Note that some Hanafi sources (Mulla Miskin) rule it valid if the sale occurs, but others (al-Fath) call it invalid. Trace the reasoning to the hadith 'لا ربح ما لم يضمن'.
The dispute hinges on whether the mudarib's liability attaches at the moment of sale or earlier.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof (dalil)
Recite the hadith 'نهى عن ربح ما لم يضمن' and explain its implications: profit is only allowed from property that has entered one's liability (daman). In mudaraba with commodities, the mudarib holds the goods as amana, so profit from their sale would be profit from unguaranteed property.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in the school.
4
Contrast the opposing schools
Identify the positions of Ibn Abi Layla (measurable/weighable goods allowed) and Malik (all commodities allowed). For each, note their proof: commodities are valuable (muttaqawwima) and analogous to currency.
These views are rejected in the Hanafi school due to the specific prohibition.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Summarize how the dispute affects real mudaraba contracts: in Hanafi, giving a car as capital is invalid; in Maliki, it is valid. Even within Hanafi, giving fulus as capital is valid only according to Muhammad.
The mufta bihi position in the text follows the matn, i.e., allowing fulus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما تصح إلخ : أي وإنما تصح المضاربة بما تصح به الشركة الدراهم والدنانير عندهما، وعند محمد بهما وبالفلوس الرائجة، ولو دفع إليه عرضاً، وقال له: بعه واعمل به مضاربة في ثمنه، فباع بدراهم أو بدنانير فتصرف صح (ملا مسكين) وقال في "الفتح": لا يصح؛ لنهيه عليه عن ربح ما لم يضمن، والمضاربة بغير النقود تؤدي إليه؛ لأنها أمانة في يد المضارب، وربما زادت قيمتها بعد العقد، فإذا باعها شركه في الربح فحصل ربح ما لم يضمن؛ إذ المضارب يستحق نصيبه من غير أن يدخل شيء في ضمانه؛ بخلاف النقود؛ فإنه عند الشراء بها يجب الثمن في ذمته؛ لأنها لا تتعين بالتعيين، فما يحصل له بذلك فهو ربح ما ضمن والمكيل والموزون عروض. (زيلعي) بما تصح به الشركة إلخ وهي الدراهم والدنانير لا غير عندهما، والفلوس النافقة عند محمد مثلهما، وقد مر في الشركة، وقال ابن أبي ليلى تصح المضاربة في المكيل والموزون؛ لأنهما من ذوات الأمثال، فيمكن تقدير -  - يكون الربح بينهما مشاعا، فإن شرط لأحدهما زيادة عشر، فله أجر مثله، من الربح فللمضارب ولا يجاوز عن المشروط، وكل شرط يوجب جهالة الربح يفسده، وإلا لا، الأجر عقد المضاربة - رأس المال بمثل المقبوض ، وقال مالك تجوز بالعروض؛ لأنها متقومة، فصار كالنقدين، ولنا: ما روي أنه عليا نهى عن ربح ما لم يضمن، والمضاربة بغير النقود تؤدي إليه؛ لأنها أمانة في يد المضارب، وربما زادت قيمتها بعد العقد، فإذا باعها شاركه في الربح، فحصل ربح ما لم يضمن؛ إذ المضارب يستحق نصيبه من غير أن يدخل شيء في ضمانه، بخلاف النقود؛ فإنه عند الشراء بها يجب الثمن في ذمته؛ لأنها لا تتعين بالتعيين، فما يحصل له بذلك، فهو ربح ما ضمن [رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۹/۲]
And it is valid [i.e., mudaraba] only with what makes partnership (shirkah) valid, i.e., dirhams and dinars according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? Actually 'indahuma refers to the two: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf? Or the two refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, while Muhammad adds fulus). And according to Muhammad, with both of them and with current fulus (coins). And if he hands over [a commodity] and says: sell it and work with its price as mudaraba, then he sells it for dirhams or dinars and transacts properly. (Mulla Miskin) And it is said in al-Fath: it is not valid, because of the prohibition of profit from what one has not guaranteed (i.e., the hadith). And mudaraba with non-silver/gold items leads to that, because it is an amana in the hands of the mudarib, and its value may increase after the contract; if he sells it, [the mudarib] shares the profit, so profit is obtained from what was not guaranteed. Since the mudarib becomes entitled to his share without anything entering his liability. Unlike silver/gold dirhams/dinars, because when he purchases with them, the price is a debt in his liability, since they are not determined by specification (la tata'ayyunu bi al-ta'yin). So what he gains thereby is profit from what he guaranteed. And measurable and weighable goods are commodities ('urud). (Zayla'i) 'Valid only with what makes partnership valid' etc., i.e., dirhams and dinars only according to the two, and current fulus according to Muhammad are like them. This has passed in the chapter of shirkah. And Ibn Abi Layla said: mudaraba is valid with measurable and weighable goods, because they are of comparable types (dhawat al-amthal), so they can be estimated. [Page 92] The profit is shared between them proportionally (musha'an). If one stipulates an additional ten, he gets ajr al-mithl from the profit, but does not exceed the stipulated amount. And every condition that causes uncertainty (jahala) in profit invalidates it, otherwise not. The ajr for the mudaraba contract: the capital is like its equivalent received. And Malik said: it is permissible with 'urud (commodities) because they are valuable (muttaqawwima), so they become like currency. And we have: what is narrated that 'Ali (r) forbade profit from what is not guaranteed. And mudaraba with non-silver/gold items leads to that, because it is an amana in the hands of the mudarib, and its value may increase after the contract; if he sells it, [the mudarib] shares the profit, so profit is obtained from what was not guaranteed. Since the mudarib becomes entitled to his share without anything entering his liability. Unlike silver/gold dirhams/dinars, because with them when he purchases, the price is a debt in his liability, since they are not determined by specification. So what he gains thereby is profit from what he guaranteed. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/239]
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage discusses the valid capital for mudaraba. It begins by stating that mudaraba is valid only with the same type of capital that makes shirkah (partnership) valid, namely dirhams (silver coins) and dinars (gold coins) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf ('indahuma). According to Imam Muhammad, current fulus (copper coins) are also valid like dirhams and dinars. The text then gives an example: if someone hands over a commodity ('ard) and says 'sell it and use its price as mudaraba capital,' and the mudarib sells for dirhams or dinars and trades, it is valid according to Mulla Miskin, but al-Fath says it is not valid because of the prohibition of 'profit from what one has not guaranteed' (a hadith). The reasoning is that commodities are amana in the mudarib's hands; their value may increase after the contract, so if the mudarib sells and shares profit, he would profit from something he never guaranteed to return equivalent of. In contrast, with dirhams/dinars, when the mudarib buys, the price becomes a debt on his liability (dhimma), so any profit is from what he guaranteed. The text then mentions the view of Ibn Abi Layla (allowing mudaraba with measurable and weighable goods) and Malik (allowing with any commodity because they are valuable). The Hanafi response is the same: the hadith prohibits profiting from unguaranteed items, and mudaraba with commodities leads to that. The passage concludes with the ruling that profit must be shared proportionally, etc. This is clearly an inter-madhhab dispute with Hanafi, Ibn Abi Layla, and Malik.

Key Terms
عروض (urud): Commodities other than gold and silver; goods for trade that are not currency.
الفلوس الرائجة (fulus al-ra'ija): Current copper coins; token money in circulation.
ضمان (daman): Liability; guarantee to return an equivalent of what was taken.
ثمن (thaman): Currency; price paid in gold/silver (or their equivalent).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject commodities (عروض) as capital for mudaraba?
A) Because commodities are not valuable enough
B) Because the mudarib cannot guarantee them
C) Because the mudarib would profit from unguaranteed property
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Mudaraba capital must be from a type that enters the mudarib's liability, ensuring profit is from guaranteed property.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Profit Must Be Proportional (Musha')
Ruling on profit sharing ratio

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that profit in mudaraba must be musha' and identify the consequence of stipulating a fixed sum.

Core Idea
A mudaraba contract is invalid if the profit share is a fixed sum; it must be a proportional share (musha').

This lesson examines the fundamental rule that profit in a mudaraba must be shared proportionally between the rabb al-mal and the mudarib. We will explore why a fixed-sum stipulation invalidates the contract, and what compensation the mudarib receives in that case, including the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the details.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (mudaraba contract) and the ruling regarding profit sharing: profit must be musha' (common share). A fixed sum invalidates the contract.
2
Identify the dalil
The proof is that partnership (shirkah) is not realized without common ownership. Stipulating a fixed sum cuts the partnership, as profit may only equal that amount, leaving nothing to share.
This is an implicit dalil from the nature of partnership.
3
Analyze the consequence of invalidity
When the contract is invalid (fasid), the mudarib gets ajr al-mithl (market rate), not the stipulated amount. The profit belongs to the rabb al-mal.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that the ajr cannot exceed the stipulated amount; Muhammad says it can be more. Also, in the original riwaya, ajr is due even without profit, but Abu Yusuf says no profit means no ajr.
This ikhtilaf affects the mudarib's compensation in practice.
5
Apply the ruling
In a modern mudaraba, if the contract stipulates a fixed salary for the mudarib from the profit, the contract becomes fasid and the mudarib is entitled to ajr al-mithl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكون الربح بينهما مشاعا، معناه لا تصح المضاربة حتى يكون الربح مشاعاً بينهما؛ لأن الشركة لا تتحقق إلا به، حتى لو شرط لأحدهما دراهم مسماة من الربح تبطل المضاربة. رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] فإن شرط إلخ أي إن شرط لأحدهما زيادة عشرة دراهم قبل أن يكون الربح بينهما، فسدت المضاربة؛ لأن اشتراط ذلك مما يقطع الشركة بينهما؛ لأنه ربما لا يربح إلا هذا القدر. [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] فله أجر إلخ: أي فللمضارب أجر المثل؛ لأنه لم يرض بالعمل مجاناً، ولا سبيل إلى المشروط للفساد، والربح لرب المال؛ لأنه نماء ملكه. (فتح) ولا يجاوز إلخ أي لا يجاوز الأجر عن القدر المشروط عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد: يجاوز ويبلغ بالغاً ما بلغ، ويجب الأجر في المضاربة الفاسدة وإن لم يربح في رواية الأصل، وعن أبي يوسف محله: أنه إذا لم يربح فلا أجر له. (مسكين) وكل شرط إلخ: أي كل شرط يوجب جهالة الربح كشرط رب المال على المضارب أن يدفع إليه أرضه ليزرعها سنة، أو داره ليسكنها سنة، يفسد المضاربة؛ لأنه جعل بعض الربح عوضاً عن عمله، والبعض أجرة داره أو أرضه ولا يعلم حصة العمل حتى يجب حصته، ويسقط ما أصاب منفعة الدار [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] وقال في "الزيلعي" وغيره كما في "الفتح": إن كل شرط يوجب الجهالة في الربح أو قطع الشركة يفسد عقد المضاربة وما لا فلا انتهى قال الأكمل: شرط العمل على رب المال يفسدها وليس بواحد منهما فلم يطرد، والجواب أن الفساد يراد به ما يشمل عدم وجود المضاربة؛ إذ شرط العمل على رب العقد المال يخرج عن المضاربة؛ إذ حقيقة المضاربة أن يكون العمل فيها من طرف المضارب، فكان هذا من قبيل سلب الشيء عن المعدوم وهو يجوز كـ"زيد المعدوم ليس ببصير" كذا في "الحموي" عن "المقدسي". (فتح) وإلا لا: أي وإن لم يوجب الشرط جهالة الربح لا يفسد العقد، ولكن يبطل الشرط.(مسكين) وقال في "العيني": لأنه لا يفضي إلى جهالة حصة العمل؛ إذ نصيبه من الربح مقابل بعمله لا غير، ولا جهالة في نصيبه. [٢٤٠/٢]
And the profit is shared between them proportionally (musha'an); its meaning is that mudaraba is not valid until the profit is in common between them, because partnership (shirkah) is not realized except with that. So if one of them stipulates a specific number of dirhams from the profit, the mudaraba becomes invalid. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/240] 'Then if he stipulates' etc.: meaning, if one of them stipulates an extra ten dirhams before the profit is between them, the mudaraba becomes invalid; because stipulating that cuts the partnership between them; because perhaps he will only earn that amount. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/240] 'So he gets ajr' etc.: meaning, the mudarib gets ajr al-mithl; because he did not agree to work for free, and there is no way to [give] what was stipulated due to invalidity, and the profit is for the owner because it is the growth of his property. (Fath) 'And does not exceed' etc.: i.e., the ajr does not exceed the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf; and according to Muhammad, it exceeds and reaches whatever it may be. And the ajr is obligatory in invalid mudaraba even if there is no profit in the original version (riwaya al-asl); and from Abu Yusuf in his place: if there is no profit, he gets no ajr. (Miskin) 'And every condition' etc.: i.e., every condition that causes uncertainty (jahala) regarding the profit, such as the owner's condition that the mudarib give him his land to cultivate for a year, or his house to live in for a year, invalidates the mudaraba; because he makes part of the profit in exchange for his work, and part as rent for his house or land, and the portion for work is unknown, so his share is unknown, and what corresponds to the benefit of the house is dropped. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/240] And it is stated in al-Zayla'i and others as in al-Fath: every condition that causes uncertainty in the profit or cuts the partnership invalidates the mudaraba contract; and what does not [cause that] does not [invalidate]. He said al-Akmal: the condition that the work is upon the owner invalidates it, and it is not one of them [i.e., does not cause jahala or cut partnership], so the rule is not universal. The answer is that invalidity here is intended to include the non-existence of mudaraba; because stipulating work on the owner removes it from being a mudaraba, since the reality of mudaraba is that the work is from the mudarib's side. So this is like negating a thing from what does not exist, which is permissible, like 'Zaid who does not exist is not seeing'. This is from al-Hamawi from al-Maqdisi. (Fath) 'Otherwise not': i.e., if the condition does not cause uncertainty in the profit, it does not invalidate the contract, but the condition becomes void. (Miskin) And it is said in al-Ayni: because it does not lead to uncertainty in the portion of work; since his share of profit is in exchange for his work only, and there is no uncertainty in his share. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/240]
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage discusses essential rules for profit-sharing in mudaraba. First, profit must be a common share (musha') between the parties; a fixed sum invalidates the contract because it nullifies partnership. If a fixed extra amount (e.g., ten dirhams) is stipulated before the profit is distributed, the contract becomes invalid (fasid). The mudarib then gets ajr al-mithl, not the stipulated amount, and the profit belongs to the rabb al-mal. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf says ajr cannot exceed the fixed amount; Muhammad says it can be any amount. Also, in the original riwaya, ajr is due even if no profit; but in a narration from Abu Yusuf, no profit means no ajr. Next, any condition that causes jahala (uncertainty) regarding the profit invalidates the contract, e.g., requiring the mudarib to let the owner use his land or house for free—since that mixes unknown compensation. However, some conditions that do not cause jahala do not invalidate the contract, but the condition itself is void. A special case: if the condition is that the owner does the work, this invalidates because it negates the essence of mudaraba (work by mudarib), not due to jahala but due to the absence of a required element. The passage ends with a clarification from al-Ayni.

Key Terms
مشاع (musha'): Shared proportionally; the profit is divided by percentage, e.g., half, third, not a fixed sum.
جهالة (jahala): Uncertainty that leads to dispute; here, any condition that makes the profit unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if one party stipulates a fixed 10 dirhams from the profit before distribution?
A) The contract is valid, but the stipulation is void.
B) The contract is invalid (fasid).
C) The contract remains valid and the stipulation is enforceable.
D) The mudarib gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
A mudaraba is only valid if the profit share is proportional (musha'); a fixed sum invalidates the contract, and the mudarib receives ajr al-mithl.

Conditions That Cause Jahala Invalidate Mudaraba
Ruling on conditions causing uncertainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions that cause jahala (uncertainty) in the profit share and those that do not, and state the ruling for each.

Core Idea
Conditions that create uncertainty in the profit share invalidate the mudaraba; harmless conditions are void but the contract remains valid.

This lesson explores the second major rule from the passage: any condition that leads to jahala (uncertainty) in the profit share invalidates the mudaraba contract. We will examine examples such as requiring the mudarib to provide free use of property, and the special case where the condition negates the very essence of mudaraba.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Every condition that causes jahala (uncertainty) regarding the profit invalidates the mudaraba. The text gives examples: requiring the mudarib to let the owner use his land for cultivation or his house for residence for a year.
2
Understand why jahala invalidates
Such conditions mix compensation for work with compensation for other services, making the profit share unknown. The mudarib's share of profit is partly in return for his work and partly as rent, and the allocation is unclear.
3
Identify the boundary
If a condition does not cause jahala in the profit, it does not invalidate the contract, but the condition itself is void (batil). Example: a condition that does not affect the profit share's certainty.
4
Analyze the special case
A condition that the owner does the work invalidates the contract, not due to jahala but because it removes the essence of mudaraba (work by mudarib). This is like negating a non-existent property.
This shows the rule is not purely about jahala but also about the fundamental nature of mudaraba.
5
Apply the rule
In a modern mudaraba, if the contract requires the mudarib to also act as a consultant for free, it creates jahala and invalidates. If the condition is irrelevant (e.g., the mudarib must wear a certain color), it is void but the contract stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكون الربح بينهما مشاعا، معناه لا تصح المضاربة حتى يكون الربح مشاعاً بينهما؛ لأن الشركة لا تتحقق إلا به، حتى لو شرط لأحدهما دراهم مسماة من الربح تبطل المضاربة. رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] فإن شرط إلخ أي إن شرط لأحدهما زيادة عشرة دراهم قبل أن يكون الربح بينهما، فسدت المضاربة؛ لأن اشتراط ذلك مما يقطع الشركة بينهما؛ لأنه ربما لا يربح إلا هذا القدر. [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] فله أجر إلخ: أي فللمضارب أجر المثل؛ لأنه لم يرض بالعمل مجاناً، ولا سبيل إلى المشروط للفساد، والربح لرب المال؛ لأنه نماء ملكه. (فتح) ولا يجاوز إلخ أي لا يجاوز الأجر عن القدر المشروط عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد: يجاوز ويبلغ بالغاً ما بلغ، ويجب الأجر في المضاربة الفاسدة وإن لم يربح في رواية الأصل، وعن أبي يوسف محله: أنه إذا لم يربح فلا أجر له. (مسكين) وكل شرط إلخ: أي كل شرط يوجب جهالة الربح كشرط رب المال على المضارب أن يدفع إليه أرضه ليزرعها سنة، أو داره ليسكنها سنة، يفسد المضاربة؛ لأنه جعل بعض الربح عوضاً عن عمله، والبعض أجرة داره أو أرضه ولا يعلم حصة العمل حتى يجب حصته، ويسقط ما أصاب منفعة الدار [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] وقال في "الزيلعي" وغيره كما في "الفتح": إن كل شرط يوجب الجهالة في الربح أو قطع الشركة يفسد عقد المضاربة وما لا فلا انتهى قال الأكمل: شرط العمل على رب المال يفسدها وليس بواحد منهما فلم يطرد، والجواب أن الفساد يراد به ما يشمل عدم وجود المضاربة؛ إذ شرط العمل على رب العقد المال يخرج عن المضاربة؛ إذ حقيقة المضاربة أن يكون العمل فيها من طرف المضارب، فكان هذا من قبيل سلب الشيء عن المعدوم وهو يجوز كـ"زيد المعدوم ليس ببصير" كذا في "الحموي" عن "المقدسي". (فتح) وإلا لا: أي وإن لم يوجب الشرط جهالة الربح لا يفسد العقد، ولكن يبطل الشرط.(مسكين) وقال في "العيني": لأنه لا يفضي إلى جهالة حصة العمل؛ إذ نصيبه من الربح مقابل بعمله لا غير، ولا جهالة في نصيبه. [٢٤٠/٢]
And the profit is shared between them proportionally (musha'an); its meaning is that mudaraba is not valid until the profit is in common between them, because partnership (shirkah) is not realized except with that. So if one of them stipulates a specific number of dirhams from the profit, the mudaraba becomes invalid. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/240] 'Then if he stipulates' etc.: meaning, if one of them stipulates an extra ten dirhams before the profit is between them, the mudaraba becomes invalid; because stipulating that cuts the partnership between them; because perhaps he will only earn that amount. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/240] 'So he gets ajr' etc.: meaning, the mudarib gets ajr al-mithl; because he did not agree to work for free, and there is no way to [give] what was stipulated due to invalidity, and the profit is for the owner because it is the growth of his property. (Fath) 'And does not exceed' etc.: i.e., the ajr does not exceed the stipulated amount according to Abu Yusuf; and according to Muhammad, it exceeds and reaches whatever it may be. And the ajr is obligatory in invalid mudaraba even if there is no profit in the original version (riwaya al-asl); and from Abu Yusuf in his place: if there is no profit, he gets no ajr. (Miskin) 'And every condition' etc.: i.e., every condition that causes uncertainty (jahala) regarding the profit, such as the owner's condition that the mudarib give him his land to cultivate for a year, or his house to live in for a year, invalidates the mudaraba; because he makes part of the profit in exchange for his work, and part as rent for his house or land, and the portion for work is unknown, so his share is unknown, and what corresponds to the benefit of the house is dropped. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/240] And it is stated in al-Zayla'i and others as in al-Fath: every condition that causes uncertainty in the profit or cuts the partnership invalidates the mudaraba contract; and what does not [cause that] does not [invalidate]. He said al-Akmal: the condition that the work is upon the owner invalidates it, and it is not one of them [i.e., does not cause jahala or cut partnership], so the rule is not universal. The answer is that invalidity here is intended to include the non-existence of mudaraba; because stipulating work on the owner removes it from being a mudaraba, since the reality of mudaraba is that the work is from the mudarib's side. So this is like negating a thing from what does not exist, which is permissible, like 'Zaid who does not exist is not seeing'. This is from al-Hamawi from al-Maqdisi. (Fath) 'Otherwise not': i.e., if the condition does not cause uncertainty in the profit, it does not invalidate the contract, but the condition becomes void. (Miskin) And it is said in al-Ayni: because it does not lead to uncertainty in the portion of work; since his share of profit is in exchange for his work only, and there is no uncertainty in his share. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/240]
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage discusses essential rules for profit-sharing in mudaraba. First, profit must be a common share (musha') between the parties; a fixed sum invalidates the contract because it nullifies partnership. If a fixed extra amount (e.g., ten dirhams) is stipulated before the profit is distributed, the contract becomes invalid (fasid). The mudarib then gets ajr al-mithl, not the stipulated amount, and the profit belongs to the rabb al-mal. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf says ajr cannot exceed the fixed amount; Muhammad says it can be any amount. Also, in the original riwaya, ajr is due even if no profit; but in a narration from Abu Yusuf, no profit means no ajr. Next, any condition that causes jahala (uncertainty) regarding the profit invalidates the contract, e.g., requiring the mudarib to let the owner use his land or house for free—since that mixes unknown compensation. However, some conditions that do not cause jahala do not invalidate the contract, but the condition itself is void. A special case: if the condition is that the owner does the work, this invalidates because it negates the essence of mudaraba (work by mudarib), not due to jahala but due to the absence of a required element. The passage ends with a clarification from al-Ayni.

Key Terms
مشاع (musha'): Shared proportionally; the profit is divided by percentage, e.g., half, third, not a fixed sum.
جهالة (jahala): Uncertainty that leads to dispute; here, any condition that makes the profit unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The mudarib must submit audited financial statements.
D) The mudarib must not invest in real estate.

Key Takeaway
Conditions that cause uncertainty (jahala) in the profit share invalidate the mudaraba; harmless conditions are void but do not affect the contract.

Capital of Mudarabah Must Be in Coins
Dispute with Malik regarding capital cash vs goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires mudarabah capital to be in coins and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the principle of 'ribh ma lam yudman'.

Core Idea
Profit without liability is forbidden; thus mudarabah capital must be coins, not goods.

The capital in a mudarabah contract must be clearly defined to avoid prohibited uncertainty and ensure that profit is earned only after bearing liability. The Hanafi school, relying on a hadith of Imam Ali (ra), insists that capital be in the form of coins (nuqud). Imam Malik permits goods ('urud) based on analogy. In this lesson, we examine the proofs of each school and the reasoning that leads the Hanafis to require coins.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: capital must be in coins (nuqud). Mudarabah with goods is fasid (void).
This is the established position of the three Hanafi imams.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam Malik holds that goods are valid because they are valuable (mutaqawwimah) and thus analogous to cash.
Opposing school is Maliki.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The hadith of Ali forbids profit from what is not guaranteed (ribh ma lam yudman). In mudarabah with goods, the mudarib does not guarantee the goods (they are an amanah), so profit from selling them would fall under this prohibition.
The hadith is ahad, but it is relied upon in this context.
4
Analyze the Maliki proof and the Hanafi response
Malik uses qiyas: goods are valuable like cash. Hanafis respond that the analogy fails because cash creates a liability (thaman fi dhimmah) at purchase, whereas goods remain an amanah. Thus the risk of liability is fundamentally different.
This is a classic example of qiyas with a difference in the effective cause (illah).
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis require the capital to be cash; Malikis allow goods. In practice, a contract structured with goods as capital would be invalid in a Hanafi court.
This affects product structuring in Islamic finance today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عقد المضاربة - رأس المال بمثل المقبوض ، وقال مالك تجوز بالعروض؛ لأنها متقومة، فصار كالنقدين، ولنا: ما روي أنه عليا نهى عن ربح ما لم يضمن، والمضاربة بغير النقود تؤدي إليه؛ لأنها أمانة في يد المضارب، وربما زادت قيمتها بعد العقد، فإذا باعها شاركه في الربح، فحصل ربح ما لم يضمن؛ إذ المضارب يستحق نصيبه من غير أن يدخل شيء في ضمانه، بخلاف النقود؛ فإنه عند الشراء بها يجب الثمن في ذمته؛ لأنها لا تتعين بالتعيين، فما يحصل له بذلك، فهو ربح ما ضمن [رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۹/۲]
The contract of mudarabah - the capital is like the received amount (i.e., must be in coins). Malik said: it is permissible with goods because they are valuable, so they become like cash. Our proof: it is narrated that Ali (ra) forbade profit from what is not guaranteed, and mudarabah with other than cash leads to that because it is an amanah in the mudarib's hand, and its value might increase after the contract; if he sells it, he shares profit, so profit is obtained from what was not guaranteed, since the mudarib deserves his share without anything entering his liability, unlike cash, because when purchasing with it, the price becomes a debt in his liability since it is not specified by specification, so what he gains thereby is profit from what he guaranteed.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding the nature of capital in a mudarabah contract. The matn states that the capital must be 'like the received amount' (i.e., in the form of coins, nuqud). Imam Malik holds that the capital may also be in the form of goods ('urud) because goods are valuable (mutaqawwimah) and thus analogous to cash. The Hanafi school responds with a proof: the hadith of Imam Ali (ra) that forbids profit from what is not guaranteed (ribh ma lam yudman). Mudarabah with goods leads to this forbidden profit because the goods are an amanah in the mudarib's hand; if their value increases after the contract and he sells them, he shares in the profit even though he never bore any liability (damān) for the goods. In contrast, when the capital is cash, the mudarib incurs liability at the time of purchase because the price becomes a debt in his dhimmah; thus any profit earned is profit from what he guaranteed. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that the capital must be in coins to avoid the prohibited category of earning profit without liability. The authority weight of this ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is expressed in the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-mudārabah): A contract of profit-sharing between capital provider (rabb al-māl) and worker (muḍārib).
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The party who provides the capital in a mudarabah contract.
المضارب (al-muḍārib): The worker/entrepreneur who invests the capital in trade.
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Liability for loss; in this context, the obligation to bear the risk of capital loss.
ربح ما لم يضمن (ribḥ mā lam yuḍman): Profit earned from something for which the earner does not bear liability or risk of loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is mudarabah with goods ('urud) as capital invalid?
A) Goods are not valuable enough.
B) Goods lead to profit without liability, which is prohibited.
C) There is a consensus among all schools against it.
D) The mudarib cannot sell goods.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi mudarabah, capital must be in coins to ensure profit is earned only after bearing liability; goods as capital lead to the forbidden category of ribh ma lam yudman.
