Mudarib's Authority in Absolute Mudarabah
Rulings on delivery of capital and mudarib's authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid mudarabah and identify which customary trade actions the mudarib may undertake in an absolute mudarabah.

Core Idea
In absolute mudarabah, the mudarib may do all customary trade acts unless restrictions are specified.

This lesson examines the conditions of a valid mudarabah and the scope of the mudarib's authority when no restrictions are placed. We'll explore the essential delivery of capital, the analogy to ijarah, and debate over travel and credit sales. The text is from Kanz al-Daqaiq with commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of capital delivery
Recognize that delivering the capital to the mudarib is a condition for the contract's validity, analogous to hire (ijarah).
This distinguishes mudarabah from shirkah, where both partners work.
2
Understand the analogy to ijarah
The text likens mudarabah to ijarah in that the capital is the subject matter, hence delivery is obligatory for the mudarib to work.
This qiyas supports the ruling.
3
Define absolute mudarabah
Absolute mudarabah is when no restrictions are placed on time, place, or type of trade; the mudarib then follows trade custom.
Custom is the benchmark, as per the text.
4
Examine each permission: sales and travel
The text grants sale for cash and credit (but credit requires permission), travel (with dispute), and ibda' (giving capital as bida'ah).
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on travel.
5
Apply the custom restriction
Actions must be customary (e.g., not selling with a 20-year term); non-customary acts exceed the mudarib's authority.
The mufta bihi position allows travel unless forbidden.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدفع المال إلخ : عطف على قوله: "ويكون الربح بينهما" أي من شرط صحة المضاربة أن يدفع المال إلى المضارب؛ ليتمكن من الاسترباح؛ ولأنها في معنى الإجارة، والمال محل، فيجب تسليمه ليعمل بخلاف الشركة لانعقادها على العمل منهما، وسواء عقدها المالك أو غيره كولي الصغير، وكذا لو دفع أحد الشريكين بشرط عمل الآخر ولو بشرط عمل عاقد غير مالك، فإن لم يكن أهلاً للمضاربة فيه تفسد كمأذون دفع بشرط عمل نفسه أو مولاه، ولا دين عليه ولو مديوناً صح . أبي حنيفة، ولو دفع مكاتب بشرط عمل مولاه صح مطلقاً، كذا في الحموي. [ تبيين الحقائق ٥٢٤/٥] واحترز بالمعتاد عما لم يعهد كالبيع إلى عشرين سنة كما في الدر، وفي "الدراية" : يملك البيع ولو فاسداً، و لم يرد به جواز مباشرة البيع الفاسد بل أشار به إلى أنه بالبيع فاسداً لا يكون مخالفاً، فلا يكون غاصباً، فلا يخرج من أن يكون المال في يده أمانة. (فتح المعين ونسيئة: أي إلى أجل وعند الثلاثة لا يبيع بنسيئة إلا بإذنه رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] وقال في "الخزانة": لأن كلاً منهما أي من النقد والنسيئة صنيع التجارة، والغرض من هذا العقد الاسترباح، وهو بالتجارة، وإنما قال في مطلقها"؛ إذ لو شرط عليه البيع بالنقد لا يجوز له أن يبيع نسيئة، أما لو شرط عليه البيع نسيئة، فيجوز له أن بالنقد إذا باع بمقدار ما لا يتغابن الناس فيه، هو الصحيح. ويسافر إلخ أي يسافر المضارب بمال المضاربة براً وبحراً في الروايات الظاهرة عن الإمام، كما في "الخانية"، وفي "الظهيرية": له السفر بمال المضاربة مطلقاً على الأصح إلا أن ينهاه نصاً، كذا في "الحموي"، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه ليس له أن يسافر بلا إذنه، وهو خلاف الظاهر، وكذا ما روى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة من التفصيل بأنه إن دفع المال إليه في مصر، وهو من أهل ذلك المصر، فليس له أن يسافر به، وإن دفع المال إليه في غير مصره، فله أن يسافر به إلى بلده، خلاف الظاهر أيضاً، قال في "البحر" [۳۷۹/۷]: ويسافر براً وبحراً، ولو دفع إليه في بلده على الظاهر، انتهى، والكلام في المضاربة المطلقة التي لم تقيد بمكان أو زمان أو نوع (فتح، ملا مسكين بتصرف من المحشي) ويبضع إلخ من الإبضاع أي يدفع المال بضاعة، ولو لرب المال ولا تبطل به المضاربة كذا في "الدرر"، قال العيني: وهو أن يدفع إلى غيره مالا يعمل فيه، ويكون الربح للعامل؛ لأن هذا من صنيع التجار. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢] قال في "الفتح": وقول العيني: "ويكون الربح للعامل صوابه ولا يكون، أو يحمل العامل على المضارب الذي .
And the payment of capital... appended to His saying: 'And the profit is between them' meaning from the conditions of validity of mudarabah is that the capital be paid to the mudarib so that he can profit, and because it is similar to hire (ijarah), and the capital is the subject matter, so its delivery is obligatory for him to work, unlike partnership (shirkah) because it is based on work from both. Whether the contract is made by the owner or another like the guardian of a minor, and likewise if one of the partners pays with the condition of work by the other, even if the condition is of work by the non-owner contractor; if he is not eligible for mudarabah, it becomes void, like a ma'dhun (slave permitted to trade) who pays with condition of work by himself or his master, and there is no debt on him, and if he is indebted it is valid according to Abu Hanifa. If a mukatib (slave with contract of manumission) pays with condition of work by his master, it is valid absolutely. And he sells... meaning if the mudarabah is valid and absolute (mulaqah), i.e., he gave him mudarabah in halves for example, and nothing more, because the absolute includes all types, so he may do what is customary among merchants. He restricts 'customary' to exclude that which is not customary, like selling with a term of twenty years. And in al-Dirayah: he possesses the sale even if invalid (fasid), and by this he did not mean permission to directly perform an invalid sale but indicated that by selling invalidly he is not negligent, so he is not a usurper, and the capital does not cease to be an amanah in his hand. And credit: meaning to a term, and according to the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) he may not sell on credit without permission. And he said in al-Khazanah: because each of them, i.e., cash and credit, are trade practices, and the purpose of this contract is profit, which is through trade. He only said this in an absolute mudarabah; because if he stipulated on him sale for cash, it is not permissible for him to sell on credit; but if he stipulated on him sale on credit, it is permissible for him to sell for cash if he sells for an amount that people do not consider a significant discrepancy, this is the correct view. And he travels... meaning the mudarib travels with mudarabah capital by land and sea in the apparent narrations from the Imam, as in al-Khaniyyah, and in al-Zahiriyyah: he may travel with mudarabah capital absolutely according to the most correct view unless he explicitly forbids him. And from Abu Yusuf: he may not travel without his permission, which is contrary to the apparent position. And similarly what Abu Yusuf narrated from Abu Hanifa of detail: that if he gave him the capital in a city and he is from that city, he may not travel with it; but if he gave him the capital outside his city, he may travel with it to his town—also contrary to the apparent. He said in al-Bahr: he travels by land and sea even if given in his town according to the apparent view. End. And the discussion is about the absolute mudarabah that is not restricted by place, time, or type. And he gives as a bida'ah... from ibda' meaning he gives the capital as a commodity, even to the owner of the capital, and the mudarabah does not become void because that is trade practice.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissions and conditions of the mudarib in an absolute mudarabah (unrestricted). First, the delivery of capital to the mudarib is a condition for the contract's effectiveness, similar to leasing (ijarah). The contract can be made by the owner or his representative, such as a guardian. Various cases are discussed: a slave with trade permission (ma'dhun) or a mukatib. The main ruling is that in an absolute mudarabah, the mudarib may engage in all customary trade practices: selling for cash or credit, traveling by land or sea, appointing agents, and even giving the capital as a bida'ah (a consignment) to another trader. However, credit sales require explicit permission according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). There is a dispute regarding travel: the apparent narrations from Abu Hanifa allow travel without permission, while Abu Yusuf restricts it. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that the mudarib may travel unless explicitly forbidden. The passage ends with a note on ibda' (giving the capital as a bida'ah to a third party). The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, with some reports from Nawadir.

Key Terms
المضاربة المطلقة (al-muḍārabah al-muṭlaqah): An unrestricted mudarabah where the mudarib is not limited by time, place, or specific type of trade.
الإبضاع (al-ibḍāʿ): Giving capital as a bida'ah (commodity) to a third party for trade; the mudarib may do so without voiding mudarabah.
النسيئة (al-nasī’ah): Credit sale; sale with deferred payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an absolute mudarabah, if the mudarib sells goods on credit without permission from the capital owner, the sale is:
A) Valid and the mudarib acted per custom.
B) Invalid because credit sales always require permission.
C) Valid only if the term is short.
D) The mudarib becomes a guarantor for the price.

Key Takeaway
In absolute mudarabah, the mudarib's authority is broad but bounded by trade custom and the requirement of permission for credit sales; travel is generally allowed unless forbidden.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Invalid Stipulations and Conditions of Validity in Mudarabah
Commentary on invalid stipulations and conditions of validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a condition placing loss on the mudarib and list the conditions for a valid mudarabah contract.

Core Idea
A void stipulation does not invalidate mudarabah; loss is always on the capital owner.

The passage begins by addressing an invalid condition: the owner stipulating that the mudarib bears any loss. This contradicts the nature of mudarabah where the mudarib is a trustee. The commentary then explains that handing over the capital is a condition of validity, with details on who may contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the invalid condition
Find the condition that is void and state what it is (shart al-wadi'ah on mudarib).
The text uses 'bati! al-shart' meaning the condition is void.
2
Analyze the effect of the void condition
Determine whether the condition invalidates the contract. The text says it does not, because it does not cut profit or cause ignorance.
The contract remains valid; loss stays on the owner.
3
Extract the condition of validity for mudarabah
Note that handing over the capital is a condition (shart) for validity, enabling the mudarib to work. The commentary compares to ijarah.
This is unlike partnership (shirkah) which does not require handover.
4
List additional conditions related to parties
The text discusses who may contract: owner, guardian, one of partners, etc. Identify the conditions of capacity for mudarib.
A non-qualified person (e.g., a minor's guardian's agent) may cause invalidity.

أحكام المضاربة
ويبطل الشرط كشرط الوضيعة على المضارب، ويدفع المال إلى المضارب، ويبيع بنقد ونسيئة، ويشتري ويوكل ويسافر ويبضع
كشرط الوضيعة إلخ وهي الخسران على المضارب؛ فإنه شرط زائد لا يوجب قطع الشرط في الربح، ولا جهالة فيه، فلا يكون مفسدا، وتكون الوضيعة على رب المال؛ لأن ما فات جزء من المال بالهلاك يلزم صاحب المال دون غيره، والمضارب أمين فيه، فلا يلزمه الشرط [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] ويدفع المال إلخ : عطف على قوله: "ويكون الربح بينهما" أي من شرط صحة المضاربة أن يدفع المال إلى المضارب؛ ليتمكن من الاسترباح؛ ولأنها في معنى الإجارة، والمال محل، فيجب تسليمه ليعمل بخلاف الشركة لانعقادها على العمل منهما، وسواء عقدها المالك أو غيره كولي الصغير، وكذا لو دفع أحد الشريكين بشرط عمل الآخر ولو بشرط عمل عاقد غير مالك، فإن لم يكن أهلاً للمضاربة فيه تفسد كمأذون دفع بشرط عمل نفسه أو مولاه، ولا دين عليه ولو مديوناً صح . أبي حنيفة، ولو دفع مكاتب بشرط عمل مولاه صح مطلقاً، كذا في الحموي. (فتح بقدر الحاجة) ويبيع إلخ: أي إذا كانت المضاربة صحيحة مطلقة بأن دفع إليه مضاربة بالنصف مثلاً، ولم يزد عليه؛ لأن المطلق يتناول الأنواع كلها، فله أن يفعل ما هو معتاد بين التجار. [ تبيين الحقائق ٥٢٤/٥] واحترز بالمعتاد عما لم يعهد كالبيع إلى عشرين سنة كما في الدر، وفي "الدراية" : يملك البيع ولو فاسداً، و لم يرد به جواز مباشرة البيع الفاسد بل أشار به إلى أنه بالبيع فاسداً لا يكون مخالفاً، فلا يكون غاصباً، فلا يخرج من أن يكون المال في يده أمانة. (فتح المعين ونسيئة: أي إلى أجل وعند الثلاثة لا يبيع بنسيئة إلا بإذنه رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] وقال في "الخزانة": لأن كلاً منهما أي من النقد والنسيئة صنيع التجارة، والغرض من هذا العقد الاسترباح، وهو بالتجارة، وإنما قال في مطلقها"؛ إذ لو شرط عليه البيع بالنقد لا يجوز له أن يبيع نسيئة، أما لو شرط عليه البيع نسيئة، فيجوز له أن بالنقد إذا باع بمقدار ما لا يتغابن الناس فيه، هو الصحيح. ويسافر إلخ أي يسافر المضارب بمال المضاربة براً وبحراً في الروايات الظاهرة عن الإمام، كما في "الخانية"، وفي "الظهيرية": له السفر بمال المضاربة مطلقاً على الأصح إلا أن ينهاه نصاً، كذا في "الحموي"، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه ليس له أن يسافر بلا إذنه، وهو خلاف الظاهر، وكذا ما روى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة من التفصيل بأنه إن دفع المال إليه في مصر، وهو من أهل ذلك المصر، فليس له أن يسافر به، وإن دفع المال إليه في غير مصره، فله أن يسافر به إلى بلده، خلاف الظاهر أيضاً، قال في "البحر" [۳۷۹/۷]: ويسافر براً وبحراً، ولو دفع إليه في بلده على الظاهر، يبيع انتهى، والكلام في المضاربة المطلقة التي لم تقيد بمكان أو زمان أو نوع (فتح، ملا مسكين بتصرف من المحشي) ويبضع إلخ من الإبضاع أي يدفع المال بضاعة، ولو لرب المال ولا تبطل به المضاربة كذا في "الدرر"، قال العيني: وهو أن يدفع إلى غيره مالا يعمل فيه، ويكون الربح للعامل؛ لأن هذا من صنيع التجار. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢] قال في "الفتح": وقول العيني: "ويكون الربح للعامل صوابه ولا يكون، أو يحمل العامل على المضارب الذي .
ويودع ولا يزوج عبدا ولا أمة، ولا يضارب إلا بإذن أو بـ"اعمل برأيك" ولم يتعدّ أي من مال المضاربة
وجد منه
أي لا يعطي المال مضاربة من رب المال بقوله
الإبضاع، وإن لم يعمل بالفعل كذا ذكره الشيخ شاهين وليس المراد بالربح الذي يكون للمضارب
في كلام الشيخ شاهين دون رب المال إذا دفع إليه المال بضاعة أصل الربح بل ما يخصه منه، فتنبه. ويودع: [ أي المضارب عند أحد مال المضاربة ] قال في "البحر الرائق: وله الإبضاع والإيداع واستئجار العمال للأعمال، واستئجار المنازل لحفظ الأموال، واستئجار السفن والدواب وله أن يرهن، ويرتهن لها، وله أن يستأجر أرضاً بيضاء، ويشتري ببعض المال طعاماً ليزرعها أو ليغرس فيها نخلا أو شجرا، ولو أخذ نخلا أو شجرا معاملة على أن ينفق في تلقيحها أو تأبيرها من المال لم يجز عليها، وإن قال له اعمل برأيك، ولا يملك الاستدانة، فإن رهن شيئاً من المضاربة ضمن ولو أذنه رب المال في ذلك كان الدين عليهما نصفين، ولو أخر المضارب الثمن جاز على رب المال، ولا يضمن بخلاف الوكيل الخاص، ولو حط بعض الثمن إن كان لعيب طعن فيه المشتري، وكان ما حط حصته أو أكثر يسيراً جاز، وإن كان لا يتغابن الناس في الزيادة يصح، ويضمن ذلك. من ماله لرب المال، وكان رأس المال ما بقي على المشتري. [٣٧٩/٧] ولا يزوج إلخ: أي ليس للمضارب أن يزوج من مال المضاربة عبداً ولا أمة، وعن أبي يوسف له أنه أمة؛ لأنه من باب الاكتساب؛ إذ يستفيد به المهر، وسقوط النفقة من مال المضاربة ولهما: أنه ليس من التجارة، والعقد لا يتضمن إلا التوكيل بالتجارة، فلا يملكه وإن كان اكتساباً كالكتابة والإعتاق على ضعف القيمة، كذا في "الدرر". (فتح) ولا يضارب إلخ لأنه يجعل بعض ربح ماله لغيره، وهو أي رب المال لم يرض به، ولأن الشيء لا يستتبع مثله. (إلياس) إلا بإذن إلخ : أي إلا بإذن من رب المال أو بقوله: "اعمل" برأيك؛ لأن الشيء لا يتضمن مثله إلا بالتنصيص عليه، أو التفويض المطلق إليه رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢] ولم يتعد إلخ: [شروع في المضاربة الخاصة] أي لم يجاوز المضارب عما عينه أي رب المال من بلد بعينه بأن قال له: لا تعمل إلا في مصر مثلا، سلعة بعينها بأن قال له لاتبع ولا تشتر إلا في الحرير مثلاً، ومن وقت بعينه بأن قال له: لا تبع ولا تشتر إلا في وقت كذا، ومن معامل بعينه بأن قال له: لا تعمل إلا مع زيد بن فلان مثلاً، فإن ضامناً، ولو لم يشتر شيئاً حتى رد المال إلى البلد الذي عينه له، برئ من الضمان كالمودع إذا خالف خالف صار ومن يزوج في الوديعة، ثم رجع إلى الوفاق، وعاد المال مضاربة حتى إذا اشترى في ذلك البلد كان للمضاربة. وهذا بخلاف ما إذا قيده في سوق معين من المصر، حيث لا يتقيد به؛ لأن المصر الواحد قلما يتفاوت جوانبه وأسواقه؛ لأنه كبقعة واحدة، فلا يفيد التقييد، إلا إذا صرح بالنهي بأن قال: اعمل في هذا السوق ولا تعمل في غيره، فحينئذ يتقيد به؛ لأن المال له، وولاية التصرف إليه بخلاف ما إذا قال له: بع نسيئة، ولا تبع عدم اختلاف السعر بينهما؛ لأنه مخالفة إلى خير بيقين، كمن وكل شخصاً ببيع عبده بألف درهم، ولهاه عن البيع بالزيادة، فباعه الوكيل بألفين، فإنه يجوز؛ لما قلنا رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢]
Book of Mudarabah. Rulings of Mudarabah. The condition is invalidated like the condition of loss on the mudarib, and the capital is handed over to the mudarib, and he sells for cash and credit, and buys, and appoints agents, and travels, and sends as bida'ah. 'Like the condition of loss etc.' that is, loss on the mudarib; it is an extra condition that does not necessitate cutting the condition in profit, and there is no ignorance in it, so it is not corrupting, and the loss is upon the owner of the capital; because what is lost is part of the capital by destruction, it is binding on the owner of the capital not on others, and the mudarib is a trustee in it, so the condition is not binding on him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/240] 'And hands over the capital etc.' is a conjunction to his saying 'and the profit is between them' i.e., from the conditions of validity of mudarabah is that the capital is handed over to the mudarib so that he can make profit; and because it is akin to a hire contract, and capital is the locus, so it must be handed over for him to work, unlike partnership because it is concluded on work from both of them. It is the same whether the owner of the contract or someone else like the guardian of a minor, and likewise if one of the partners hands over (capital) with the condition of work of the other, even if with the condition of work of a non-owner contractor, then if he is not qualified for mudarabah, it becomes invalid, like a permitted slave who hands over with the condition of his own work or his master's work. And there is no debt upon him, and even if he is in debt it is valid according to Abu Hanifa. And if a mukatab hands over with the condition of his master's work, it is valid absolutely, as in al-Hamawi. (Fath bi-qadr al-haja) 'And sells etc.': i.e., if the mudarabah is valid and absolute, that he handed over to him a mudarabah with half for example, and did not add more; because the absolute includes all types, so he may do what is customary among merchants. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 5/524] And he restricted by 'customary' what is not customary like selling with a term of twenty years as in al-Durr. And in al-Diraya: he owns the sale even if corrupt, and he did not intend by it the permissibility of conducting a corrupt sale, rather he indicated that by a corrupt sale he is not violating, so he is not a usurper, so the capital does not cease to be an amanah in his hand. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'and credit': i.e., with a term, and according to the three, he does not sell on credit except with his permission. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/240] And it is said in al-Khazanah: because each of them, i.e., cash and credit, is a practice of trade, and the purpose of this contract is profit-making, which is by trade. And he only said 'in absolute (mudarabah)' because if he stipulated upon him sale for cash, it is not permissible for him to sell on credit; but if he stipulated upon him sale on credit, it is permissible for him to sell for cash if he sells for an amount that people do not dispute over, that is the correct view. 'And travels etc.': i.e., the mudarib travels with the mudarabah capital by land and sea according to the apparent narrations from the Imam, as in al-Khaniyah, and in al-Zahiriyyah: he may travel with mudarabah capital absolutely according to the most correct view unless he prohibits him explicitly, as in al-Hamawi. And from Abu Yusuf: that he may not travel without his permission, and that is contrary to the apparent. And likewise what Abu Yusuf narrated from Abu Hanifa of the detail that if he handed over the capital to him in a city, and he is from that city's people, then he may not travel with it; but if he handed over the capital to him outside his city, then he may travel with it to his city, that is also contrary to the apparent. He said in al-Bahr [7/379]: he travels by land and sea, even if he handed over to him in his city according to the apparent. The discussion is in absolute mudarabah which is not restricted to place, time, or type. (Fath, Mulla Miskeen with adaptation from the commenter). 'And sends as bida'ah etc.' from ibda' i.e., he hands over the capital as goods (bida'ah), even to the owner of the capital, and the mudarabah is not invalidated by it, as in al-Durar. Al-Ayni said: it is that he gives to someone else wealth to work with, and the profit is for the worker; because this is among the practices of merchants. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/241] He said in al-Fath: al-Ayni's saying 'and the profit is for the worker' – the correct is 'and it is not', or the worker is interpreted as the mudarib who... 'And deposits, and does not marry a slave or slave-girl, and does not give as mudarabah except with permission or by saying 'act according to your opinion', and he has not exceeded (the limits) i.e., from the mudarabah capital.' 'i.e., he does not give the capital as mudarabah from the owner of the capital by saying 'ibda'', even if he did not work physically, as mentioned by Shaykh Shahin. And what is meant by the profit that is for the mudarib in Shaykh Shahin's statement is not the original profit without the owner of the capital when he handed over the capital as bida'ah, but rather his portion from it, so be mindful. 'And deposits': [i.e., the mudarib with someone the mudarabah capital] He said in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: he may do ibda', deposit, hire workers for tasks, hire houses to protect wealth, hire ships and mounts, he may give and take collateral, he may lease white land, and buy with some of the capital food to cultivate it or to plant date palms or trees in it, but if he took date palms or trees on a mu'amalah basis to spend on their pollination or fertilization from the capital, that is not permissible for him. And if he says to him 'act according to your opinion', he does not own taking a loan. If he pledges something from the mudarabah, he is liable. And if the owner of the capital authorized him in that, the debt is on both of them half and half. If the mudarib delays the price, it is valid upon the owner of the capital, and he is not liable, unlike a specific agent. If he reduces some of the price, if it is due to a defect that the buyer complained about, and the reduction was his share or a little more, it is valid. If it is an amount over which people would not dispute, it is valid, and he is liable for that from his wealth to the owner of the capital, and the capital is what remains on the buyer. [7/379] 'And does not marry etc.': i.e., it is not for the mudarib to marry a slave or slave-girl from the mudarabah capital. And from Abu Yusuf that he may, for the slave-girl [because] it is a means of acquisition; as he benefits from the dower and the dropping of maintenance from the mudarabah capital. And for the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): it is not trade, and the contract only includes agency for trade, so he does not own it even if it is acquisition, like kitabah and manumission upon weak value, as in al-Durar. (Fath) 'And does not give as mudarabah etc.' because he makes some of the profit of his wealth for someone else, and the owner of the capital did not consent to that, and because a thing does not follow its like. (Ilyas) 'Except with permission etc.': i.e., except with permission from the owner of the capital or by his saying 'act according to your opinion'; because a thing does not include its like except by explicit specification or absolute delegation to him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/241] 'And he has not exceeded etc.': [Beginning of special mudarabah] i.e., the mudarib did not violate what the owner of the capital specified: a specific city, by saying to him 'only work in Egypt for example'; a specific commodity, by saying 'do not buy or sell except silk for example'; a specific time, by saying 'do not buy or sell except at such time'; a specific person, by saying 'do not deal except with Zayd ibn so-and-so for example'. If he violates, he becomes a guarantor. And if he did not buy anything until he returned the capital to the city specified for him, he is free from guarantee like a depositor who violated in the deposit, then returned to compliance, and the capital becomes mudarabah again, so that if he buys in that city, it is for the mudarabah. And this is contrary to if he restricted him to a specific market in the city, where he is not restricted by it; because a single city rarely differs in its sides and markets; because it is like one area, so the restriction is of no benefit, unless he explicitly forbids by saying: 'work in this market and do not work in another', then he is restricted by it; because the capital is his, and the authority of disposal is his. Contrary to if he said to him: 'sell on credit and do not sell for cash' when there is no difference in price between them; because it is a violation to a clearly better action, like one who appointed an agent to sell his slave for 1000 dirhams and forbade him from selling for more, and the agent sold for 2000, then it is valid; because of what we said. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/241]
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the rights and restrictions of the mudarib in a mudarabah contract. The author, Imam Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, explains the conditions for a valid mudarabah and the scope of the mudarib's authority. The passage can be divided into several sections. First, it addresses invalid stipulations: if the owner stipulates that any loss (wadi'ah) falls on the mudarib, the condition is void but does not invalidate the contract. The loss remains on the owner because the mudarib is a trustee (amin), and loss due to destruction is akin to loss of the owner's property. Second, the handover of capital is a condition of validity, as the mudarib needs physical possession to trade. This is likened to an ijarah contract where the subject matter must be delivered. Third, in an absolute mudarabah (no restrictions), the mudarib has broad authority to do what is customary among merchants: sell for cash or credit, buy, appoint agents, travel, and send goods as bida'ah (giving goods to another to trade, with profit for the worker). There is an intra-madhhab dispute on traveling: the apparent narrations from Abu Hanifa allow it absolutely, while Abu Yusuf requires permission. There is also a detail attributed to Abu Hanifa about traveling from the same or different city, but the commentary says the relied-upon view is that he may travel absolutely unless explicitly prohibited. The mudarib may also deposit the capital, hire workers, lease property, and give/accept collateral, but he may not take loans (except with permission) nor marry slaves from the mudarabah capital. On marrying slaves, Abu Yusuf allows it as a form of acquisition, but Abu Hanifa and Muhammad forbid it as it is not trade. The mudarib may not give the capital to another mudarib without the owner's explicit authorization or a general delegation. Finally, if the owner specifies restrictions (e.g., a particular city, commodity, time, or person), the mudarib must adhere; violation makes him a guarantor. However, if the restriction is on a market within the same city, it is not binding unless explicitly phrased as a prohibition, because a city is considered a single location. The commentary uses qiyas and istihsan to derive these rulings, emphasizing that the mudarib's authority is defined by the contract and customary trade practices.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-mudarabah): A partnership contract where one party (rabb al-mal) provides capital and the other (mudarib) provides labor, with profit shared according to agreement.
الوضيعة (al-wadi'ah): Loss or deficiency in the capital. In this context, a stipulation that the mudarib bears any loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an absolute mudarabah, if the owner stipulates that any loss is on the mudarib, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The condition is valid and binding.
B) The condition is void but the mudarabah is valid, and loss is on the owner.
C) The condition voids the entire mudarabah.
D) The condition is void and the mudarib must still bear the loss.

Key Takeaway
A void condition in mudarabah does not invalidate the contract if it does not cut profit or cause ignorance; loss always remains on the capital owner.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
12 min
The Mudarib's Authority in Absolute Mudarabah
Commentary on mudarib's permissions in absolute mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the scope of the mudarib's authority in an absolute mudarabah and resolve intra-Hanafi disputes on traveling and credit sales.

Core Idea
In an absolute mudarabah, the mudarib may do what is customary among merchants, including traveling, credit sales, and ibda'.

The passage now details the mudarib's permissions in an unrestricted (mutlaq) mudarabah. The author explains that the mudarib can sell for cash or credit, buy, appoint agents, travel, and send goods as bida'ah. There are disputes on traveling and credit sales, and the commentary clarifies the relied-upon positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of mudarabah
Recognize that the discussion is about absolute (mutlaq) mudarabah with no restrictions on place, time, or type.
The text says 'al-mutlaq yatanaawalu anwaa'a kullaha'.
2
List the permissible actions
Extract the actions: sell cash and credit, buy, appoint agents, travel, ibda' (give goods to another to trade).
These are customary (mu'tad) among merchants.
3
Analyze the dispute on traveling
Compare Abu Hanifa's apparent position (allows travel absolutely) with Abu Yusuf's (requires permission). Note the detail about traveling from same city.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) is that travel is allowed unless explicitly prohibited.
4
Analyze the dispute on credit sales
The three (probably Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) require permission for credit; Hanafi allows it in absolute mudarabah unless cash-only stipulated.
The text mentions 'عند الثلاثة لا يبيع بنسيئة إلا بإذنه'.
5
Understand ibda' (bida'ah)
Ibda' is permissible; the mudarib may give capital to another to trade, with profit for the worker. This is from merchant custom.
The commentary clarifies that the profit belongs to the mudarib, not the new worker.

أحكام المضاربة
ويبطل الشرط كشرط الوضيعة على المضارب، ويدفع المال إلى المضارب، ويبيع بنقد ونسيئة، ويشتري ويوكل ويسافر ويبضع
كشرط الوضيعة إلخ وهي الخسران على المضارب؛ فإنه شرط زائد لا يوجب قطع الشرط في الربح، ولا جهالة فيه، فلا يكون مفسدا، وتكون الوضيعة على رب المال؛ لأن ما فات جزء من المال بالهلاك يلزم صاحب المال دون غيره، والمضارب أمين فيه، فلا يلزمه الشرط [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] ويدفع المال إلخ : عطف على قوله: "ويكون الربح بينهما" أي من شرط صحة المضاربة أن يدفع المال إلى المضارب؛ ليتمكن من الاسترباح؛ ولأنها في معنى الإجارة، والمال محل، فيجب تسليمه ليعمل بخلاف الشركة لانعقادها على العمل منهما، وسواء عقدها المالك أو غيره كولي الصغير، وكذا لو دفع أحد الشريكين بشرط عمل الآخر ولو بشرط عمل عاقد غير مالك، فإن لم يكن أهلاً للمضاربة فيه تفسد كمأذون دفع بشرط عمل نفسه أو مولاه، ولا دين عليه ولو مديوناً صح . أبي حنيفة، ولو دفع مكاتب بشرط عمل مولاه صح مطلقاً، كذا في الحموي. (فتح بقدر الحاجة) ويبيع إلخ: أي إذا كانت المضاربة صحيحة مطلقة بأن دفع إليه مضاربة بالنصف مثلاً، ولم يزد عليه؛ لأن المطلق يتناول الأنواع كلها، فله أن يفعل ما هو معتاد بين التجار. [ تبيين الحقائق ٥٢٤/٥] واحترز بالمعتاد عما لم يعهد كالبيع إلى عشرين سنة كما في الدر، وفي "الدراية" : يملك البيع ولو فاسداً، و لم يرد به جواز مباشرة البيع الفاسد بل أشار به إلى أنه بالبيع فاسداً لا يكون مخالفاً، فلا يكون غاصباً، فلا يخرج من أن يكون المال في يده أمانة. (فتح المعين ونسيئة: أي إلى أجل وعند الثلاثة لا يبيع بنسيئة إلا بإذنه رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] وقال في "الخزانة": لأن كلاً منهما أي من النقد والنسيئة صنيع التجارة، والغرض من هذا العقد الاسترباح، وهو بالتجارة، وإنما قال في مطلقها"؛ إذ لو شرط عليه البيع بالنقد لا يجوز له أن يبيع نسيئة، أما لو شرط عليه البيع نسيئة، فيجوز له أن بالنقد إذا باع بمقدار ما لا يتغابن الناس فيه، هو الصحيح. ويسافر إلخ أي يسافر المضارب بمال المضاربة براً وبحراً في الروايات الظاهرة عن الإمام، كما في "الخانية"، وفي "الظهيرية": له السفر بمال المضاربة مطلقاً على الأصح إلا أن ينهاه نصاً، كذا في "الحموي"، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه ليس له أن يسافر بلا إذنه، وهو خلاف الظاهر، وكذا ما روى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة من التفصيل بأنه إن دفع المال إليه في مصر، وهو من أهل ذلك المصر، فليس له أن يسافر به، وإن دفع المال إليه في غير مصره، فله أن يسافر به إلى بلده، خلاف الظاهر أيضاً، قال في "البحر" [۳۷۹/۷]: ويسافر براً وبحراً، ولو دفع إليه في بلده على الظاهر، يبيع انتهى، والكلام في المضاربة المطلقة التي لم تقيد بمكان أو زمان أو نوع (فتح، ملا مسكين بتصرف من المحشي) ويبضع إلخ من الإبضاع أي يدفع المال بضاعة، ولو لرب المال ولا تبطل به المضاربة كذا في "الدرر"، قال العيني: وهو أن يدفع إلى غيره مالا يعمل فيه، ويكون الربح للعامل؛ لأن هذا من صنيع التجار. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢] قال في "الفتح": وقول العيني: "ويكون الربح للعامل صوابه ولا يكون، أو يحمل العامل على المضارب الذي .
ويودع ولا يزوج عبدا ولا أمة، ولا يضارب إلا بإذن أو بـ"اعمل برأيك" ولم يتعدّ أي من مال المضاربة
وجد منه
أي لا يعطي المال مضاربة من رب المال بقوله
الإبضاع، وإن لم يعمل بالفعل كذا ذكره الشيخ شاهين وليس المراد بالربح الذي يكون للمضارب
في كلام الشيخ شاهين دون رب المال إذا دفع إليه المال بضاعة أصل الربح بل ما يخصه منه، فتنبه. ويودع: [ أي المضارب عند أحد مال المضاربة ] قال في "البحر الرائق: وله الإبضاع والإيداع واستئجار العمال للأعمال، واستئجار المنازل لحفظ الأموال، واستئجار السفن والدواب وله أن يرهن، ويرتهن لها، وله أن يستأجر أرضاً بيضاء، ويشتري ببعض المال طعاماً ليزرعها أو ليغرس فيها نخلا أو شجرا، ولو أخذ نخلا أو شجرا معاملة على أن ينفق في تلقيحها أو تأبيرها من المال لم يجز عليها، وإن قال له اعمل برأيك، ولا يملك الاستدانة، فإن رهن شيئاً من المضاربة ضمن ولو أذنه رب المال في ذلك كان الدين عليهما نصفين، ولو أخر المضارب الثمن جاز على رب المال، ولا يضمن بخلاف الوكيل الخاص، ولو حط بعض الثمن إن كان لعيب طعن فيه المشتري، وكان ما حط حصته أو أكثر يسيراً جاز، وإن كان لا يتغابن الناس في الزيادة يصح، ويضمن ذلك. من ماله لرب المال، وكان رأس المال ما بقي على المشتري. [٣٧٩/٧] ولا يزوج إلخ: أي ليس للمضارب أن يزوج من مال المضاربة عبداً ولا أمة، وعن أبي يوسف له أنه أمة؛ لأنه من باب الاكتساب؛ إذ يستفيد به المهر، وسقوط النفقة من مال المضاربة ولهما: أنه ليس من التجارة، والعقد لا يتضمن إلا التوكيل بالتجارة، فلا يملكه وإن كان اكتساباً كالكتابة والإعتاق على ضعف القيمة، كذا في "الدرر". (فتح) ولا يضارب إلخ لأنه يجعل بعض ربح ماله لغيره، وهو أي رب المال لم يرض به، ولأن الشيء لا يستتبع مثله. (إلياس) إلا بإذن إلخ : أي إلا بإذن من رب المال أو بقوله: "اعمل" برأيك؛ لأن الشيء لا يتضمن مثله إلا بالتنصيص عليه، أو التفويض المطلق إليه رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢] ولم يتعد إلخ: [شروع في المضاربة الخاصة] أي لم يجاوز المضارب عما عينه أي رب المال من بلد بعينه بأن قال له: لا تعمل إلا في مصر مثلا، سلعة بعينها بأن قال له لاتبع ولا تشتر إلا في الحرير مثلاً، ومن وقت بعينه بأن قال له: لا تبع ولا تشتر إلا في وقت كذا، ومن معامل بعينه بأن قال له: لا تعمل إلا مع زيد بن فلان مثلاً، فإن ضامناً، ولو لم يشتر شيئاً حتى رد المال إلى البلد الذي عينه له، برئ من الضمان كالمودع إذا خالف خالف صار ومن يزوج في الوديعة، ثم رجع إلى الوفاق، وعاد المال مضاربة حتى إذا اشترى في ذلك البلد كان للمضاربة. وهذا بخلاف ما إذا قيده في سوق معين من المصر، حيث لا يتقيد به؛ لأن المصر الواحد قلما يتفاوت جوانبه وأسواقه؛ لأنه كبقعة واحدة، فلا يفيد التقييد، إلا إذا صرح بالنهي بأن قال: اعمل في هذا السوق ولا تعمل في غيره، فحينئذ يتقيد به؛ لأن المال له، وولاية التصرف إليه بخلاف ما إذا قال له: بع نسيئة، ولا تبع عدم اختلاف السعر بينهما؛ لأنه مخالفة إلى خير بيقين، كمن وكل شخصاً ببيع عبده بألف درهم، ولهاه عن البيع بالزيادة، فباعه الوكيل بألفين، فإنه يجوز؛ لما قلنا رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢]
Book of Mudarabah. Rulings of Mudarabah. The condition is invalidated like the condition of loss on the mudarib, and the capital is handed over to the mudarib, and he sells for cash and credit, and buys, and appoints agents, and travels, and sends as bida'ah. 'Like the condition of loss etc.' that is, loss on the mudarib; it is an extra condition that does not necessitate cutting the condition in profit, and there is no ignorance in it, so it is not corrupting, and the loss is upon the owner of the capital; because what is lost is part of the capital by destruction, it is binding on the owner of the capital not on others, and the mudarib is a trustee in it, so the condition is not binding on him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/240] 'And hands over the capital etc.' is a conjunction to his saying 'and the profit is between them' i.e., from the conditions of validity of mudarabah is that the capital is handed over to the mudarib so that he can make profit; and because it is akin to a hire contract, and capital is the locus, so it must be handed over for him to work, unlike partnership because it is concluded on work from both of them. It is the same whether the owner of the contract or someone else like the guardian of a minor, and likewise if one of the partners hands over (capital) with the condition of work of the other, even if with the condition of work of a non-owner contractor, then if he is not qualified for mudarabah, it becomes invalid, like a permitted slave who hands over with the condition of his own work or his master's work. And there is no debt upon him, and even if he is in debt it is valid according to Abu Hanifa. And if a mukatab hands over with the condition of his master's work, it is valid absolutely, as in al-Hamawi. (Fath bi-qadr al-haja) 'And sells etc.': i.e., if the mudarabah is valid and absolute, that he handed over to him a mudarabah with half for example, and did not add more; because the absolute includes all types, so he may do what is customary among merchants. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 5/524] And he restricted by 'customary' what is not customary like selling with a term of twenty years as in al-Durr. And in al-Diraya: he owns the sale even if corrupt, and he did not intend by it the permissibility of conducting a corrupt sale, rather he indicated that by a corrupt sale he is not violating, so he is not a usurper, so the capital does not cease to be an amanah in his hand. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'and credit': i.e., with a term, and according to the three, he does not sell on credit except with his permission. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/240] And it is said in al-Khazanah: because each of them, i.e., cash and credit, is a practice of trade, and the purpose of this contract is profit-making, which is by trade. And he only said 'in absolute (mudarabah)' because if he stipulated upon him sale for cash, it is not permissible for him to sell on credit; but if he stipulated upon him sale on credit, it is permissible for him to sell for cash if he sells for an amount that people do not dispute over, that is the correct view. 'And travels etc.': i.e., the mudarib travels with the mudarabah capital by land and sea according to the apparent narrations from the Imam, as in al-Khaniyah, and in al-Zahiriyyah: he may travel with mudarabah capital absolutely according to the most correct view unless he prohibits him explicitly, as in al-Hamawi. And from Abu Yusuf: that he may not travel without his permission, and that is contrary to the apparent. And likewise what Abu Yusuf narrated from Abu Hanifa of the detail that if he handed over the capital to him in a city, and he is from that city's people, then he may not travel with it; but if he handed over the capital to him outside his city, then he may travel with it to his city, that is also contrary to the apparent. He said in al-Bahr [7/379]: he travels by land and sea, even if he handed over to him in his city according to the apparent. The discussion is in absolute mudarabah which is not restricted to place, time, or type. (Fath, Mulla Miskeen with adaptation from the commenter). 'And sends as bida'ah etc.' from ibda' i.e., he hands over the capital as goods (bida'ah), even to the owner of the capital, and the mudarabah is not invalidated by it, as in al-Durar. Al-Ayni said: it is that he gives to someone else wealth to work with, and the profit is for the worker; because this is among the practices of merchants. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/241] He said in al-Fath: al-Ayni's saying 'and the profit is for the worker' – the correct is 'and it is not', or the worker is interpreted as the mudarib who... 'And deposits, and does not marry a slave or slave-girl, and does not give as mudarabah except with permission or by saying 'act according to your opinion', and he has not exceeded (the limits) i.e., from the mudarabah capital.' 'i.e., he does not give the capital as mudarabah from the owner of the capital by saying 'ibda'', even if he did not work physically, as mentioned by Shaykh Shahin. And what is meant by the profit that is for the mudarib in Shaykh Shahin's statement is not the original profit without the owner of the capital when he handed over the capital as bida'ah, but rather his portion from it, so be mindful. 'And deposits': [i.e., the mudarib with someone the mudarabah capital] He said in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: he may do ibda', deposit, hire workers for tasks, hire houses to protect wealth, hire ships and mounts, he may give and take collateral, he may lease white land, and buy with some of the capital food to cultivate it or to plant date palms or trees in it, but if he took date palms or trees on a mu'amalah basis to spend on their pollination or fertilization from the capital, that is not permissible for him. And if he says to him 'act according to your opinion', he does not own taking a loan. If he pledges something from the mudarabah, he is liable. And if the owner of the capital authorized him in that, the debt is on both of them half and half. If the mudarib delays the price, it is valid upon the owner of the capital, and he is not liable, unlike a specific agent. If he reduces some of the price, if it is due to a defect that the buyer complained about, and the reduction was his share or a little more, it is valid. If it is an amount over which people would not dispute, it is valid, and he is liable for that from his wealth to the owner of the capital, and the capital is what remains on the buyer. [7/379] 'And does not marry etc.': i.e., it is not for the mudarib to marry a slave or slave-girl from the mudarabah capital. And from Abu Yusuf that he may, for the slave-girl [because] it is a means of acquisition; as he benefits from the dower and the dropping of maintenance from the mudarabah capital. And for the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): it is not trade, and the contract only includes agency for trade, so he does not own it even if it is acquisition, like kitabah and manumission upon weak value, as in al-Durar. (Fath) 'And does not give as mudarabah etc.' because he makes some of the profit of his wealth for someone else, and the owner of the capital did not consent to that, and because a thing does not follow its like. (Ilyas) 'Except with permission etc.': i.e., except with permission from the owner of the capital or by his saying 'act according to your opinion'; because a thing does not include its like except by explicit specification or absolute delegation to him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/241] 'And he has not exceeded etc.': [Beginning of special mudarabah] i.e., the mudarib did not violate what the owner of the capital specified: a specific city, by saying to him 'only work in Egypt for example'; a specific commodity, by saying 'do not buy or sell except silk for example'; a specific time, by saying 'do not buy or sell except at such time'; a specific person, by saying 'do not deal except with Zayd ibn so-and-so for example'. If he violates, he becomes a guarantor. And if he did not buy anything until he returned the capital to the city specified for him, he is free from guarantee like a depositor who violated in the deposit, then returned to compliance, and the capital becomes mudarabah again, so that if he buys in that city, it is for the mudarabah. And this is contrary to if he restricted him to a specific market in the city, where he is not restricted by it; because a single city rarely differs in its sides and markets; because it is like one area, so the restriction is of no benefit, unless he explicitly forbids by saying: 'work in this market and do not work in another', then he is restricted by it; because the capital is his, and the authority of disposal is his. Contrary to if he said to him: 'sell on credit and do not sell for cash' when there is no difference in price between them; because it is a violation to a clearly better action, like one who appointed an agent to sell his slave for 1000 dirhams and forbade him from selling for more, and the agent sold for 2000, then it is valid; because of what we said. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/241]
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the rights and restrictions of the mudarib in a mudarabah contract. The author, Imam Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, explains the conditions for a valid mudarabah and the scope of the mudarib's authority. The passage can be divided into several sections. First, it addresses invalid stipulations: if the owner stipulates that any loss (wadi'ah) falls on the mudarib, the condition is void but does not invalidate the contract. The loss remains on the owner because the mudarib is a trustee (amin), and loss due to destruction is akin to loss of the owner's property. Second, the handover of capital is a condition of validity, as the mudarib needs physical possession to trade. This is likened to an ijarah contract where the subject matter must be delivered. Third, in an absolute mudarabah (no restrictions), the mudarib has broad authority to do what is customary among merchants: sell for cash or credit, buy, appoint agents, travel, and send goods as bida'ah (giving goods to another to trade, with profit for the worker). There is an intra-madhhab dispute on traveling: the apparent narrations from Abu Hanifa allow it absolutely, while Abu Yusuf requires permission. There is also a detail attributed to Abu Hanifa about traveling from the same or different city, but the commentary says the relied-upon view is that he may travel absolutely unless explicitly prohibited. The mudarib may also deposit the capital, hire workers, lease property, and give/accept collateral, but he may not take loans (except with permission) nor marry slaves from the mudarabah capital. On marrying slaves, Abu Yusuf allows it as a form of acquisition, but Abu Hanifa and Muhammad forbid it as it is not trade. The mudarib may not give the capital to another mudarib without the owner's explicit authorization or a general delegation. Finally, if the owner specifies restrictions (e.g., a particular city, commodity, time, or person), the mudarib must adhere; violation makes him a guarantor. However, if the restriction is on a market within the same city, it is not binding unless explicitly phrased as a prohibition, because a city is considered a single location. The commentary uses qiyas and istihsan to derive these rulings, emphasizing that the mudarib's authority is defined by the contract and customary trade practices.

Key Terms
مطلق (mutlaq): Absolute; unrestricted contract allowing all customary trade actions.
النسيئة (al-nasī'ah): Credit sale; sale with deferred payment.
الإبضاع (al-ibdā'): Giving mudarabah goods to another to trade, with profit for the mudarib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, can a mudarib in an absolute mudarabah sell goods on credit without the owner's permission?
A) No, because credit sales are not customary.
B) Yes, because credit is a customary trade practice and the contract is absolute.
C) Only if the mudarib also sells for cash.
D) Only if the owner is informed after the sale.

Key Takeaway
In absolute mudarabah, the mudarib's authority extends to all customary trade practices, including travel and credit sales, unless explicitly restricted.

Prohibited Acts and Restrictions in Mudarabah
Commentary on prohibitions and restrictions in mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify actions prohibited for the mudarib (marrying slaves, giving mudarabah to another, taking loans) and explain the effect of violating specified restrictions.

Core Idea
The mudarib may not marry slaves from capital, give mudarabah to another without permission, or take loans; violation of restrictions makes him a guarantor.

After discussing permissible actions, the passage turns to prohibitions and restrictions. The mudarib cannot marry a slave or slave-girl from the capital, nor give the capital to another mudarib without the owner's permission or general delegation. He also cannot take loans without authorization. If the owner specifies restrictions, the mudarib must adhere; otherwise, he becomes liable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited actions
List the actions explicitly forbidden: marrying a slave or slave-girl, giving mudarabah to another (mudarabah thaniya), and taking loans (istidāna) without permission.
The text says 'lā yuzawwiju 'abdan wa lā amatan, wa lā yudāribu illā bi-idhn'.
2
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute on marrying slaves
Abu Yusuf allows marrying a slave-girl as acquisition; Abu Hanifa and Muhammad prohibit it because it is not trade. The mufta bihi is prohibition.
The dispute is based on whether marriage is a form of acquisition benefiting the mudarabah.
3
Explain the exception for giving mudarabah to another
The mudarib may give mudarabah to another only if the owner explicitly says 'i'mal bi-ra'yik' (act according to your opinion) or gives permission.
Without such, the mudarib cannot delegate because the owner did not consent to another worker.
4
Understand restrictions (ta'yid) and violation
If the owner restricts to a specific place, commodity, time, or person, the mudarib must comply. Violation makes him a guarantor (dāmin).
There is a nuance: if restricted to a market within a city, it is not binding unless explicitly phrased as a prohibition.

أحكام المضاربة
ويبطل الشرط كشرط الوضيعة على المضارب، ويدفع المال إلى المضارب، ويبيع بنقد ونسيئة، ويشتري ويوكل ويسافر ويبضع
كشرط الوضيعة إلخ وهي الخسران على المضارب؛ فإنه شرط زائد لا يوجب قطع الشرط في الربح، ولا جهالة فيه، فلا يكون مفسدا، وتكون الوضيعة على رب المال؛ لأن ما فات جزء من المال بالهلاك يلزم صاحب المال دون غيره، والمضارب أمين فيه، فلا يلزمه الشرط [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] ويدفع المال إلخ : عطف على قوله: "ويكون الربح بينهما" أي من شرط صحة المضاربة أن يدفع المال إلى المضارب؛ ليتمكن من الاسترباح؛ ولأنها في معنى الإجارة، والمال محل، فيجب تسليمه ليعمل بخلاف الشركة لانعقادها على العمل منهما، وسواء عقدها المالك أو غيره كولي الصغير، وكذا لو دفع أحد الشريكين بشرط عمل الآخر ولو بشرط عمل عاقد غير مالك، فإن لم يكن أهلاً للمضاربة فيه تفسد كمأذون دفع بشرط عمل نفسه أو مولاه، ولا دين عليه ولو مديوناً صح . أبي حنيفة، ولو دفع مكاتب بشرط عمل مولاه صح مطلقاً، كذا في الحموي. (فتح بقدر الحاجة) ويبيع إلخ: أي إذا كانت المضاربة صحيحة مطلقة بأن دفع إليه مضاربة بالنصف مثلاً، ولم يزد عليه؛ لأن المطلق يتناول الأنواع كلها، فله أن يفعل ما هو معتاد بين التجار. [ تبيين الحقائق ٥٢٤/٥] واحترز بالمعتاد عما لم يعهد كالبيع إلى عشرين سنة كما في الدر، وفي "الدراية" : يملك البيع ولو فاسداً، و لم يرد به جواز مباشرة البيع الفاسد بل أشار به إلى أنه بالبيع فاسداً لا يكون مخالفاً، فلا يكون غاصباً، فلا يخرج من أن يكون المال في يده أمانة. (فتح المعين ونسيئة: أي إلى أجل وعند الثلاثة لا يبيع بنسيئة إلا بإذنه رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٠/٢] وقال في "الخزانة": لأن كلاً منهما أي من النقد والنسيئة صنيع التجارة، والغرض من هذا العقد الاسترباح، وهو بالتجارة، وإنما قال في مطلقها"؛ إذ لو شرط عليه البيع بالنقد لا يجوز له أن يبيع نسيئة، أما لو شرط عليه البيع نسيئة، فيجوز له أن بالنقد إذا باع بمقدار ما لا يتغابن الناس فيه، هو الصحيح. ويسافر إلخ أي يسافر المضارب بمال المضاربة براً وبحراً في الروايات الظاهرة عن الإمام، كما في "الخانية"، وفي "الظهيرية": له السفر بمال المضاربة مطلقاً على الأصح إلا أن ينهاه نصاً، كذا في "الحموي"، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه ليس له أن يسافر بلا إذنه، وهو خلاف الظاهر، وكذا ما روى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة من التفصيل بأنه إن دفع المال إليه في مصر، وهو من أهل ذلك المصر، فليس له أن يسافر به، وإن دفع المال إليه في غير مصره، فله أن يسافر به إلى بلده، خلاف الظاهر أيضاً، قال في "البحر" [۳۷۹/۷]: ويسافر براً وبحراً، ولو دفع إليه في بلده على الظاهر، يبيع انتهى، والكلام في المضاربة المطلقة التي لم تقيد بمكان أو زمان أو نوع (فتح، ملا مسكين بتصرف من المحشي) ويبضع إلخ من الإبضاع أي يدفع المال بضاعة، ولو لرب المال ولا تبطل به المضاربة كذا في "الدرر"، قال العيني: وهو أن يدفع إلى غيره مالا يعمل فيه، ويكون الربح للعامل؛ لأن هذا من صنيع التجار. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢] قال في "الفتح": وقول العيني: "ويكون الربح للعامل صوابه ولا يكون، أو يحمل العامل على المضارب الذي .
ويودع ولا يزوج عبدا ولا أمة، ولا يضارب إلا بإذن أو بـ"اعمل برأيك" ولم يتعدّ أي من مال المضاربة
وجد منه
أي لا يعطي المال مضاربة من رب المال بقوله
الإبضاع، وإن لم يعمل بالفعل كذا ذكره الشيخ شاهين وليس المراد بالربح الذي يكون للمضارب
في كلام الشيخ شاهين دون رب المال إذا دفع إليه المال بضاعة أصل الربح بل ما يخصه منه، فتنبه. ويودع: [ أي المضارب عند أحد مال المضاربة ] قال في "البحر الرائق: وله الإبضاع والإيداع واستئجار العمال للأعمال، واستئجار المنازل لحفظ الأموال، واستئجار السفن والدواب وله أن يرهن، ويرتهن لها، وله أن يستأجر أرضاً بيضاء، ويشتري ببعض المال طعاماً ليزرعها أو ليغرس فيها نخلا أو شجرا، ولو أخذ نخلا أو شجرا معاملة على أن ينفق في تلقيحها أو تأبيرها من المال لم يجز عليها، وإن قال له اعمل برأيك، ولا يملك الاستدانة، فإن رهن شيئاً من المضاربة ضمن ولو أذنه رب المال في ذلك كان الدين عليهما نصفين، ولو أخر المضارب الثمن جاز على رب المال، ولا يضمن بخلاف الوكيل الخاص، ولو حط بعض الثمن إن كان لعيب طعن فيه المشتري، وكان ما حط حصته أو أكثر يسيراً جاز، وإن كان لا يتغابن الناس في الزيادة يصح، ويضمن ذلك. من ماله لرب المال، وكان رأس المال ما بقي على المشتري. [٣٧٩/٧] ولا يزوج إلخ: أي ليس للمضارب أن يزوج من مال المضاربة عبداً ولا أمة، وعن أبي يوسف له أنه أمة؛ لأنه من باب الاكتساب؛ إذ يستفيد به المهر، وسقوط النفقة من مال المضاربة ولهما: أنه ليس من التجارة، والعقد لا يتضمن إلا التوكيل بالتجارة، فلا يملكه وإن كان اكتساباً كالكتابة والإعتاق على ضعف القيمة، كذا في "الدرر". (فتح) ولا يضارب إلخ لأنه يجعل بعض ربح ماله لغيره، وهو أي رب المال لم يرض به، ولأن الشيء لا يستتبع مثله. (إلياس) إلا بإذن إلخ : أي إلا بإذن من رب المال أو بقوله: "اعمل" برأيك؛ لأن الشيء لا يتضمن مثله إلا بالتنصيص عليه، أو التفويض المطلق إليه رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢] ولم يتعد إلخ: [شروع في المضاربة الخاصة] أي لم يجاوز المضارب عما عينه أي رب المال من بلد بعينه بأن قال له: لا تعمل إلا في مصر مثلا، سلعة بعينها بأن قال له لاتبع ولا تشتر إلا في الحرير مثلاً، ومن وقت بعينه بأن قال له: لا تبع ولا تشتر إلا في وقت كذا، ومن معامل بعينه بأن قال له: لا تعمل إلا مع زيد بن فلان مثلاً، فإن ضامناً، ولو لم يشتر شيئاً حتى رد المال إلى البلد الذي عينه له، برئ من الضمان كالمودع إذا خالف خالف صار ومن يزوج في الوديعة، ثم رجع إلى الوفاق، وعاد المال مضاربة حتى إذا اشترى في ذلك البلد كان للمضاربة. وهذا بخلاف ما إذا قيده في سوق معين من المصر، حيث لا يتقيد به؛ لأن المصر الواحد قلما يتفاوت جوانبه وأسواقه؛ لأنه كبقعة واحدة، فلا يفيد التقييد، إلا إذا صرح بالنهي بأن قال: اعمل في هذا السوق ولا تعمل في غيره، فحينئذ يتقيد به؛ لأن المال له، وولاية التصرف إليه بخلاف ما إذا قال له: بع نسيئة، ولا تبع عدم اختلاف السعر بينهما؛ لأنه مخالفة إلى خير بيقين، كمن وكل شخصاً ببيع عبده بألف درهم، ولهاه عن البيع بالزيادة، فباعه الوكيل بألفين، فإنه يجوز؛ لما قلنا رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢]
Book of Mudarabah. Rulings of Mudarabah. The condition is invalidated like the condition of loss on the mudarib, and the capital is handed over to the mudarib, and he sells for cash and credit, and buys, and appoints agents, and travels, and sends as bida'ah. 'Like the condition of loss etc.' that is, loss on the mudarib; it is an extra condition that does not necessitate cutting the condition in profit, and there is no ignorance in it, so it is not corrupting, and the loss is upon the owner of the capital; because what is lost is part of the capital by destruction, it is binding on the owner of the capital not on others, and the mudarib is a trustee in it, so the condition is not binding on him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/240] 'And hands over the capital etc.' is a conjunction to his saying 'and the profit is between them' i.e., from the conditions of validity of mudarabah is that the capital is handed over to the mudarib so that he can make profit; and because it is akin to a hire contract, and capital is the locus, so it must be handed over for him to work, unlike partnership because it is concluded on work from both of them. It is the same whether the owner of the contract or someone else like the guardian of a minor, and likewise if one of the partners hands over (capital) with the condition of work of the other, even if with the condition of work of a non-owner contractor, then if he is not qualified for mudarabah, it becomes invalid, like a permitted slave who hands over with the condition of his own work or his master's work. And there is no debt upon him, and even if he is in debt it is valid according to Abu Hanifa. And if a mukatab hands over with the condition of his master's work, it is valid absolutely, as in al-Hamawi. (Fath bi-qadr al-haja) 'And sells etc.': i.e., if the mudarabah is valid and absolute, that he handed over to him a mudarabah with half for example, and did not add more; because the absolute includes all types, so he may do what is customary among merchants. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 5/524] And he restricted by 'customary' what is not customary like selling with a term of twenty years as in al-Durr. And in al-Diraya: he owns the sale even if corrupt, and he did not intend by it the permissibility of conducting a corrupt sale, rather he indicated that by a corrupt sale he is not violating, so he is not a usurper, so the capital does not cease to be an amanah in his hand. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'and credit': i.e., with a term, and according to the three, he does not sell on credit except with his permission. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/240] And it is said in al-Khazanah: because each of them, i.e., cash and credit, is a practice of trade, and the purpose of this contract is profit-making, which is by trade. And he only said 'in absolute (mudarabah)' because if he stipulated upon him sale for cash, it is not permissible for him to sell on credit; but if he stipulated upon him sale on credit, it is permissible for him to sell for cash if he sells for an amount that people do not dispute over, that is the correct view. 'And travels etc.': i.e., the mudarib travels with the mudarabah capital by land and sea according to the apparent narrations from the Imam, as in al-Khaniyah, and in al-Zahiriyyah: he may travel with mudarabah capital absolutely according to the most correct view unless he prohibits him explicitly, as in al-Hamawi. And from Abu Yusuf: that he may not travel without his permission, and that is contrary to the apparent. And likewise what Abu Yusuf narrated from Abu Hanifa of the detail that if he handed over the capital to him in a city, and he is from that city's people, then he may not travel with it; but if he handed over the capital to him outside his city, then he may travel with it to his city, that is also contrary to the apparent. He said in al-Bahr [7/379]: he travels by land and sea, even if he handed over to him in his city according to the apparent. The discussion is in absolute mudarabah which is not restricted to place, time, or type. (Fath, Mulla Miskeen with adaptation from the commenter). 'And sends as bida'ah etc.' from ibda' i.e., he hands over the capital as goods (bida'ah), even to the owner of the capital, and the mudarabah is not invalidated by it, as in al-Durar. Al-Ayni said: it is that he gives to someone else wealth to work with, and the profit is for the worker; because this is among the practices of merchants. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/241] He said in al-Fath: al-Ayni's saying 'and the profit is for the worker' – the correct is 'and it is not', or the worker is interpreted as the mudarib who... 'And deposits, and does not marry a slave or slave-girl, and does not give as mudarabah except with permission or by saying 'act according to your opinion', and he has not exceeded (the limits) i.e., from the mudarabah capital.' 'i.e., he does not give the capital as mudarabah from the owner of the capital by saying 'ibda'', even if he did not work physically, as mentioned by Shaykh Shahin. And what is meant by the profit that is for the mudarib in Shaykh Shahin's statement is not the original profit without the owner of the capital when he handed over the capital as bida'ah, but rather his portion from it, so be mindful. 'And deposits': [i.e., the mudarib with someone the mudarabah capital] He said in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: he may do ibda', deposit, hire workers for tasks, hire houses to protect wealth, hire ships and mounts, he may give and take collateral, he may lease white land, and buy with some of the capital food to cultivate it or to plant date palms or trees in it, but if he took date palms or trees on a mu'amalah basis to spend on their pollination or fertilization from the capital, that is not permissible for him. And if he says to him 'act according to your opinion', he does not own taking a loan. If he pledges something from the mudarabah, he is liable. And if the owner of the capital authorized him in that, the debt is on both of them half and half. If the mudarib delays the price, it is valid upon the owner of the capital, and he is not liable, unlike a specific agent. If he reduces some of the price, if it is due to a defect that the buyer complained about, and the reduction was his share or a little more, it is valid. If it is an amount over which people would not dispute, it is valid, and he is liable for that from his wealth to the owner of the capital, and the capital is what remains on the buyer. [7/379] 'And does not marry etc.': i.e., it is not for the mudarib to marry a slave or slave-girl from the mudarabah capital. And from Abu Yusuf that he may, for the slave-girl [because] it is a means of acquisition; as he benefits from the dower and the dropping of maintenance from the mudarabah capital. And for the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): it is not trade, and the contract only includes agency for trade, so he does not own it even if it is acquisition, like kitabah and manumission upon weak value, as in al-Durar. (Fath) 'And does not give as mudarabah etc.' because he makes some of the profit of his wealth for someone else, and the owner of the capital did not consent to that, and because a thing does not follow its like. (Ilyas) 'Except with permission etc.': i.e., except with permission from the owner of the capital or by his saying 'act according to your opinion'; because a thing does not include its like except by explicit specification or absolute delegation to him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/241] 'And he has not exceeded etc.': [Beginning of special mudarabah] i.e., the mudarib did not violate what the owner of the capital specified: a specific city, by saying to him 'only work in Egypt for example'; a specific commodity, by saying 'do not buy or sell except silk for example'; a specific time, by saying 'do not buy or sell except at such time'; a specific person, by saying 'do not deal except with Zayd ibn so-and-so for example'. If he violates, he becomes a guarantor. And if he did not buy anything until he returned the capital to the city specified for him, he is free from guarantee like a depositor who violated in the deposit, then returned to compliance, and the capital becomes mudarabah again, so that if he buys in that city, it is for the mudarabah. And this is contrary to if he restricted him to a specific market in the city, where he is not restricted by it; because a single city rarely differs in its sides and markets; because it is like one area, so the restriction is of no benefit, unless he explicitly forbids by saying: 'work in this market and do not work in another', then he is restricted by it; because the capital is his, and the authority of disposal is his. Contrary to if he said to him: 'sell on credit and do not sell for cash' when there is no difference in price between them; because it is a violation to a clearly better action, like one who appointed an agent to sell his slave for 1000 dirhams and forbade him from selling for more, and the agent sold for 2000, then it is valid; because of what we said. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/241]
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the rights and restrictions of the mudarib in a mudarabah contract. The author, Imam Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, explains the conditions for a valid mudarabah and the scope of the mudarib's authority. The passage can be divided into several sections. First, it addresses invalid stipulations: if the owner stipulates that any loss (wadi'ah) falls on the mudarib, the condition is void but does not invalidate the contract. The loss remains on the owner because the mudarib is a trustee (amin), and loss due to destruction is akin to loss of the owner's property. Second, the handover of capital is a condition of validity, as the mudarib needs physical possession to trade. This is likened to an ijarah contract where the subject matter must be delivered. Third, in an absolute mudarabah (no restrictions), the mudarib has broad authority to do what is customary among merchants: sell for cash or credit, buy, appoint agents, travel, and send goods as bida'ah (giving goods to another to trade, with profit for the worker). There is an intra-madhhab dispute on traveling: the apparent narrations from Abu Hanifa allow it absolutely, while Abu Yusuf requires permission. There is also a detail attributed to Abu Hanifa about traveling from the same or different city, but the commentary says the relied-upon view is that he may travel absolutely unless explicitly prohibited. The mudarib may also deposit the capital, hire workers, lease property, and give/accept collateral, but he may not take loans (except with permission) nor marry slaves from the mudarabah capital. On marrying slaves, Abu Yusuf allows it as a form of acquisition, but Abu Hanifa and Muhammad forbid it as it is not trade. The mudarib may not give the capital to another mudarib without the owner's explicit authorization or a general delegation. Finally, if the owner specifies restrictions (e.g., a particular city, commodity, time, or person), the mudarib must adhere; violation makes him a guarantor. However, if the restriction is on a market within the same city, it is not binding unless explicitly phrased as a prohibition, because a city is considered a single location. The commentary uses qiyas and istihsan to derive these rulings, emphasizing that the mudarib's authority is defined by the contract and customary trade practices.

Key Terms
التقييد (al-taqyīd): Restriction; specifying limitations on the mudarib's actions (place, commodity, time, person).
الاستدانة (al-istidānah): Taking a loan from the mudarabah capital or on its credit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, can a mudarib give some of the mudarabah capital to another person to trade as a separate mudarabah without the owner's permission?
A) Yes, because it is customary among merchants.
B) No, except with the owner's permission or if the owner said 'act according to your opinion'.
C) Yes, if the mudarib retains control.
D) No, never; it always invalidates the mudarabah.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib may not marry slaves from the capital, delegate mudarabah to another without permission, or take loans; violation of specified restrictions makes him a guarantor, but a violation that clearly benefits the owner may be excused by analogy to the agent selling above price.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Mudarib's Authority: Deposit, Marriage, and Sub-Mudarabah
Rulings on mudarib's permissible acts and prohibitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the limits of a mudarib's authority in a Hanafi mudarabah contract, identify which acts are prohibited without permission, and explain the rationale based on the principle that a thing does not include its like.

Core Idea
A mudarib may not marry slaves or give sub-mudarabah unless explicitly authorized, because agency for trade does not imply agency for like contracts.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq defines the boundaries of a mudarib's authority. While the mudarib can perform many incidental acts like depositing, hiring, and leasing, there are strict prohibitions on using funds for non-commercial purposes like marrying slaves or entering a sub-mudarabah. The underlying legal principle is that the mudarabah contract only authorizes trade; it does not implicitly authorize similar contracts or non-commercial acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
The passage states: 'He may deposit' (يبضاع), 'He may not marry a slave' (لا يزوج عبدا ولا أمة), and 'He may not give mudarabah' (ولا يضارب). Recognize that deposit is allowed while marriage and sub-mudarabah are prohibited without permission.
Deposit is an incidental act necessary for trade; the other two are not.
2
Locate the dalil for prohibition
The text gives the reason: 'because a thing does not include its like' (الشيء لا يستتبع مثله). This is a rational proof (qiyas khafi) that the mudarabah contract does not imply the power to create another mudarabah or to engage in non-commercial acts.
The dalil is based on the nature of agency.
3
Examine the exception
The prohibition is lifted with explicit permission from the capital owner or by saying 'act according to your opinion' (اعمل برأيك), which constitutes absolute delegation (التفويض المطلق).
Absolute delegation allows the mudarib to act as he sees fit.
4
Note the intra-madhhab disagreement
Abu Yusuf allowed marrying a female slave because it earns dowry and saves maintenance, but the majority (Sahibayn) prohibit it, comparing it to kitabah (emancipation contract) which is also earning but not permitted. The mufta bihi is the prohibition.
This is a valid ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

[٣٧٩/٧] ولا يزوج إلخ: أي ليس للمضارب أن يزوج من مال المضاربة عبداً ولا أمة، وعن أبي يوسف له أنه أمة؛ لأنه من باب الاكتساب؛ إذ يستفيد به المهر، وسقوط النفقة من مال المضاربة ولهما: أنه ليس من التجارة، والعقد لا يتضمن إلا التوكيل بالتجارة، فلا يملكه وإن كان اكتساباً كالكتابة والإعتاق على ضعف القيمة، كذا في "الدرر". (فتح) ولا يضارب إلخ لأنه يجعل بعض ربح ماله لغيره، وهو أي رب المال لم يرض به، ولأن الشيء لا يستتبع مثله. (إلياس) إلا بإذن إلخ : أي إلا بإذن من رب المال أو بقوله: "اعمل" برأيك؛ لأن الشيء لا يتضمن مثله إلا بالتنصيص عليه، أو التفويض المطلق إليه رمز الحقائق: ٢٤١/٢]
And he may deposit, and he may not marry a male slave or female slave, and he may not give mudarabah except with permission or with 'act according to your opinion,' and he did not exceed anything from the mudarabah property. [Marginal note: 'from it is found' - meaning he does not give the property as mudarabah from the capital owner by the word of ibda' (assignment for trade?), even if he did not work practically. As such mentioned by Sheikh Shahin. And what is meant by profit that is for the mudarib in the speech of Sheikh Shahin, not the capital owner, if he gave him the property as bida'ah (investment), is the original profit, but what pertains to him from it, so be attentive.] And he may deposit: [i.e., the mudarib with someone the mudarabah property]. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq said: He has the right of ibda' (commending?), deposit, hiring workers for tasks, hiring houses for safeguarding wealth, hiring ships and animals, and he may pawn and take pawn for it, and he may lease white land, and buy with some of the property food to cultivate it or to plant palm trees or trees, and if he took palm trees or trees on a mu'amalah contract on condition that he spend on their fertilization from the property, it is not permissible upon her, and if he said to him 'act according to your opinion,' and he does not have the right to borrow, and if he pawned something from the mudarabah, he is liable, and if the capital owner authorized him in that, the debt would be upon both halves, and if the mudarib delayed the price, it is permissible upon the capital owner, and he is not liable, unlike a special agent, and if he deducted some of the price, if it was due to a defect that the buyer complained about, and what he deducted was his share or less that was little, it is permissible, and if people do not overlook each other in the increase, it is valid, and he is liable for that from his wealth to the capital owner, and the capital is what remains upon the buyer. [7/379] 'And he may not marry, etc.': i.e., it is not for the mudarib to marry from the mudarabah property a male slave or female slave, and from Abu Yusuf that he may marry a female slave because it is a means of earning, as he benefits from the dowry and the removal of maintenance from the mudarabah property, and for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that it is not from trade, and the contract does not include except agency for trade, so he does not own it even if it is earning, like kitabah and emancipation upon weak value, as in al-Durar. (Fath) 'And he may not give mudarabah, etc.' because he makes some of the profit of his wealth for someone else, and he, i.e., the capital owner, did not consent to it, and because a thing does not include its like. (Ilyas) 'Except with permission, etc.': i.e., except with permission from the capital owner or by his saying 'act according to your opinion' because a thing does not include its like except by explicit mention or absolute delegation to him. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/241]
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays out the basic limitations on the mudarib's authority in a mudarabah contract. The first ruling is that the mudarib may deposit the capital for safekeeping, but this is limited to reasonable commercial expenses. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands this to include many incidental acts: commending goods, hiring workers, storing goods, renting ships and animals, pawning and taking pawn, leasing uncultivated land, and buying provisions for cultivation. However, such cultivation must not involve a mu'amalah contract (a sharecropping-like arrangement) because that would entail a separate partnership. The mudarib may not borrow money without liability. Regarding marriage of slaves, the mudarib cannot use capital to marry a slave (for breeding purposes) because that is not commercial activity. Abu Yusuf differed, viewing it as earning through the dowry and reduced maintenance, but the majority (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict the mudarib to trade only. Similarly, the mudarib cannot enter a sub-mudarabah (give the capital to another mudarib) because that would give part of the profit to a third party without the owner's consent. An exception is made if the owner explicitly permits it or gives absolute discretion ('اعمل برأيك'). The hadith 'a thing does not include its like' means that agency for trade does not implicitly include agency for another mudarabah; it requires explicit mention.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-mudarabah): A partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit shared according to agreement.
الإبضاع (al-ibda'): Entrusting goods for trade without profit share; the agent is a trustee, not a partner.
التفويض المطلق (al-tafwid al-mutlaq): Absolute delegation of authority, allowing the mudarib to act as he sees fit.
الإيداع (al-ida'): Deposit; entrusting property for safekeeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a mudarib who enters a sub-mudarabah without permission?
A) Valid but liable
B) Invalid and liable
C) Valid with owner's permission only
D) Valid if profitable

Key Takeaway
A mudarib's authority is limited to trade; any departure, like marriage of slaves or sub-mudarabah, requires explicit permission or absolute delegation, based on the principle that a thing does not include its like.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Restrictions on Mudarib: Exceeding Specified Conditions
Detailed rules on beneficial restrictions and liability for exceeding them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify beneficial restrictions in mudarabah and determine when a mudarib becomes liable for exceeding them.

Core Idea
A mudarib who violates beneficial restrictions becomes liable; non-beneficial restrictions are ignored unless explicitly forbidden.

This lesson explains the limits of a mudarib's authority when the capital owner specifies a particular country, commodity, time, or transaction partner. We will see what constitutes a 'beneficial' restriction and when the mudarib is held liable even if he later corrects his action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of restrictions
From the text, the capital owner may restrict mudarib to a specific country (e.g., Egypt), commodity (e.g., silk), time (e.g., only in summer), or specific person (e.g., only with Zayd).
These are called 'beneficial restrictions' because they affect the nature of the trade.
2
Distinguish beneficial from non-beneficial
A restriction to a specific market within a single city is not beneficial because the city is considered one place; it is ineffective unless the owner explicitly forbids other markets.
Similarly, a restriction to 'sell on credit' when cash price is same is non-beneficial; mudarib may sell for cash if better.
3
Apply the consequence of violation
If the mudarib exceeds a beneficial restriction, he becomes liable (dhāmin) for any loss. However, if he returns to the specified country before buying, liability ceases and the mudarabah resumes.
This is analogous to a depositor who violates the terms of the deposit.
4
Check for explicit prohibition
Even for non-beneficial restrictions, if the owner explicitly forbids (e.g., 'work only in this market, not others'), then the mudarib must comply; otherwise it is not binding.
The owner's explicit negation makes it binding because the property is his.
5
Compare with agency
Analogous to an agent told to sell for 1000 but sells for 2000: the agent is not liable because it is a better deal. Similarly, if the mudarib's violation results in a better outcome (e.g., selling cash when told credit with same price), it is permissible.
This is based on the principle that violating to a certain betterment is allowed.

(فتح الله المعين) أو معامل المراد بالمعامل معامل معين؛ لأنه لو قال على أن تشتري من أهل الكوفة أو قال: على أن تعمل في الصرف وتشتري في الصيارفة، وتبيع منهم فباع بالكوفة من رجل ليس من أهل الكوفة أو من غير الصيارفة جاز؛ لأن المقصود من . هذا الكلام التقييد بالمكان أو بالنوع حتى يجوز له أن يخرج من الكوفة في الأول ويبيع فيها من أهلها أو من غير أهلها، ولا يجوز أن يعمل في غير الصرف في الثاني، ويبيع ويشتري من الصيارفة وغيرهم؛ لأن التقييد بالمكان والنوع مفيد ولا يفيد التقييد بأهل الكوفة والصيارفة؛ لأن كل واحد منهما جمع كثير لا يمكن إحصاؤه، كذا في الزيلعي.
