Mudarib Subcontracting: Share Calculations and Liability
Explaining rulings on mudarib subcontracting with profit distribution and liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the profit shares for the owner, first mudarib, and second mudarib under different owner wordings, and determine when the first mudarib becomes personally liable for the second's share.

Core Idea
In a sub-mudaraba, the first mudarib's share is residual after the owner's fixed share and the second's conditioned share; conditioning more than his share triggers personal liability.

When a mudarib subcontracts to a second mudarib, the profit distribution depends critically on the wording used by the owner. The Hanafi school provides detailed rules to resolve shares and liability. This lesson walks you through the key scenarios from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentaries, from basic distribution to the edge cases of personal liability and slave involvement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the owner's wording and its scope
The owner's statement (e.g., 'ما رزق الله' vs. 'ما رزقك الله' vs. 'ما ربحت') determines whether his share is based on total profit or only on what the first mudarib personally earns. This is the foundation for all subsequent calculations.
The key is whether the owner attributes the profit to the capital (general) or to the mudarib (personal).
2
Determine the second mudarib's conditioned share
The first mudarib conditions a share for the second mudarib (e.g., one-third, half, two-thirds). This condition is valid because it is done with the owner's implicit permission, but it may affect the first mudarib's own share.
The condition must be known; if it exceeds the first's own share, liability may arise.
3
Calculate the owner's share
Apply the owner's condition to the relevant profit base (total or personal). The owner's share is fixed and cannot be reduced by the first mudarib's actions.
The owner's share takes priority over the second mudarib's share in case of conflict.
4
Calculate the first mudarib's share and possible liability
After allocating the owner's share and the second mudarib's conditioned share, the remainder (if any) goes to the first mudarib. If the total of the owner's share and the second's share exceeds the profit, the first mudarib must pay the shortfall from his own wealth.
This liability arises from the first mudarib's implicit guarantee of the second's share.
5
Apply to the slave cases and intra-Hanafi dispute
When a share is conditioned for a slave (owner's or mudarib's), the ruling depends on whether the slave has debt and whether work is stipulated. Abu Hanifa and the two companions differ on the validity when the slave is indebted and no work condition is set.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that according to Abu Hanifa the contract is invalid, while according to the Sahibayn it is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة
المضارب يضارب من غيره
وقيل له: ما رزق الله فبيننا نصفان فللمالك النصف وللأول السدس، وللثاني للمضارب الأول لرب المال نصف الربح أي وللمضارب الأول الثلث، ولو قيل له: ما رزقك الله فبيننا نصفان فللثاني ثلثه، والباقي بين المالك للمضارب الأول للمضارب الثاني ثلث الربح والأول نصفان ولو قيل له ما ربحت فبيننا نصفان ودفع بالنصف، فللثاني والمضارب الأول للمضارب الأول النصف، واستويا فيما بقي ولو قيل له: ما رزق الله فلي نصفه . للمضارب الأول : تصر أي بنصف الربح - أي وللمضارب الأول السدس منه وللثاني أي وللمضارب الثاني الثلث منه أي من الربح؛ لأن الدفع إلى الثاني صحيح؛ لأنه بأمر المالك، وقد شرط لنفسه نصف جميع ما رزق الله تعالى، وقد جعل الأول للثاني ثلثه، فينصرف ذلك نصيبه؛ لأنه لا يقدر أن ينقص من نصيب رب المال شيئا فبقي له السدس فيطيب ذلك لكلهم؛ لأن رب المال يستحقه بالمال؛ لأنه نماء ملكه رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٥/٢] وقيل له: جملة حالية أي والحال أنه قد قيل له فللمالك: أي رف الثاني وربح فللمالك إلخ. وللثاني الثلث أي للمضارب الثاني ثلث الربح ولو قيل له إلخ : أي لو قال رب المال ذلك، والمسألة بحالها؛ لأن المشروط ما رزق الله المضارب، وهو ههنا الثلثان، فيقسم بينهما، وللثاني الثلث الباقي بالشرط، ونظيره: ما ربحت في هذا من شيء، أو ما كان لك فيه من فضل الربح، أو ما كسبت فيه من كسب، أو ما رزقت فيه من شيء، أو ما صار لك فيه من ربح، وكذا لو شرط للمضارب الثاني أكثر من الثلث، أو أقل منه، فما بقي بعد ما أخذه منه، فهو بين رب المال والأول، والفرق بينهما: أن في الأول شرط نصف الربح جميعه؛ لأنه أضاف الرزق إلى المال، وفي الثاني أضافه إلى المضارب [البحر الرائق: ٣٨٣/٧] ولو قيل له ما ربحت إلخ أي للمضارب الأول يعني لو قال له رب المال : ما ربحت فبيننا نصفان، ودفع الأول بالنصف، فللثاني النصف أي نصف الربح؛ لأن الأول شرط له ذلك، وشرطه صحيح؛ لأنه بإذن المالك، واستويا رب المال والمضارب الأول فيما بقي وهو النصف؛ لأن المالك لم يشترط ههنا لنفسه إلا نصف ما ربحه، و لم يربح الأول إلا النصف، فكان بينهما نصفان والنصف الآخر صار للثاني بشرطه، فلم يكن من ربح الأول. رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٥/٢] وقال في "البحر الرائق: لا فرق بين هذه الصورة وما قبلها إلا من حيث اشتراط المضارب للثاني، فإن في الأولى شرط له الثلث، فكان ما بقي بينهما، وفي الثانية شرط له النصف، فكان النصف الباقي بينهما . [۳۸۳/۷] ودفع بالنصف : أي المضارب الأول إلى المضارب الثاني. (مسكين) واستويا: أي استوى المالك والمضارب الأول. (مسكين) ما رزق الله: يعني لو قال له فلي نصفه، أي نصف ما رزق الله تعالى من الربح أو قال رب المال للمضارب ما كان من فضل فبيننا نصفان، فدفع أي المضارب الأول إلى آخر بالنصف، فللمالك أي فلرب المال النصف من الربح وللثاني أي وللمضارب الثاني - النصف، ولا شيء أي للمضارب الثاني أي ربح المضارب الأول أي رب المال للأول، ولو شرط للثاني ثلثيه ضمن الأول للثاني سدسا، وإن أي للمضارب الأول للمضارب الثاني المضارب الأول من ماله من الربح شرط للمالك ثلثه، ولعبده ثلثه على أن يعمل معه، ولنفسه ثلثه، صح، الربح المالك عبد المالك المضارب الشرط النصف منه، ولا شيء للأول؛ لأن قول رب المال: "ما رزق الله تعالى" أو "ما كان من فضل" ينصرف إلى جميع الربح فيكون له النصف من الجميع، وقد شرط المضارب الأول للثاني نصف جميع الربح، فيكون له النصف، فلم يبق للأول شيء من الربح، فيخرج بغير شيء. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٥/٢] ولو شرط إلخ : أي المضارب الأول للثاني ثلثيه أي ثلثي الربح، والمسألة بحالها، ضمن المضارب الأول للثاني أي للمضارب الثاني سدساً أي سدس الربح من ماله؛ لأن رب المال شرط لنفسه النصف من مطلق الربح، فله ذلك، واستحق المضارب الثاني ثلثي الربح بشرط الأول؛ لأن شرطه صحيح؛ لكونه معلوماً، لكن لا ينفذ في حق رب المال؛ إذ لا يقدر أن يغير شرطه فيغرم له قدر السدس؛ لأنه ضمن له سلامة الثلثين بالعقد؛ لأنه غره في ضمن عقد المضاربة، وهو أيضاً سبب الرجوع للثاني على الأول. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢]
وإن شرط إلخ : أي وإن شرط المضارب لرب المال ثلث الربح، وشرط لعبد رب المال ثلثه على أن يعمل العبد مع المضارب وشرط لنفسه ثلثه صح؛ فإذا تصرف المضارب وربح يكون ثلث الربح للمضارب وثلثاه لرب المال إن لم يكن على العبد دين، وإن كان عليه دين فهو للغرماء، قال في "العيني": لأن اشتراطه للعبد يكون اشتراطاً للمولى، فكأنه اشترط للمولى ثلثي الربح، واشتراط عمل العبد غير مفسد؛ لأنه من أهل أن يضارب في مال مولاه، بخلاف ما إذا شرط عمل رب المال؛ لأن بقاء يده يمنع تسليم المال إلى المضارب، فلا يجوز. ثم إن لم يكن على العبد دين فهو للمولى، سواء شرط فيها عمل العبد أو لا، وإن كان عليه دين فهو لغرمائه إن شرط عمله وإلا فهو للمولى، وكذلك إذا شرط الثلث لعبد المضارب يصح، سواء اشترط العمل أو لا إن لم يكن عليه دين وإن كان عليه دين إن شرط عليه عمله جاز، وكان المشروط لغرمائه، وإن لم يشترط عمله لا يجوز، ويكون ما شرط لرب المال عند أبي حنيفة له، وعندهما يملك المولى كسب عبده المديون، فاشتراطه له يكون اشتراطاً للمولى، فيصح. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢] على أن يعمل معه إلخ عمل العبد ليس بقيد للصحة؛ إذ لو اشترط له الثلث، و لم يشترط عمله صح، ويكون لمولاه، لكن فائدة اشتراط عمله تظهر في أخذ غرمائه ما شرطه له حينئذ وإلا فليس لهم بل للمولى، قال الزيلعي: وهذا ظاهر؛ لأنه باشتراط عمله صار مضارباً في مال مولاه فيكون كسبه له، فيأخذه غرماؤه، وإلا فهو للمولى إلخ. تبيين الحقائق ٥٤١/٥] واستفيد منه أنه إذا اشترط عمله فلم يعمل، لم يكن للغرماء، بل للمولى؛ لأنه حيث لم يعمل لم يكن من كسبه.(فتح الله المعين)
Book of Mudaraba. The mudarib contracts with someone else. And it was said to him: 'What Allah provides, half is between us' – so for the owner half, for the first one-sixth, and for the second (the first mudarib for the owner half the profit, and for the first mudarib one-third). And if it was said to him: 'What Allah provides you, half between us' - then for the second one-third of it, and the rest between the owner and the first mudarib: for the second mudarib one-third of the profit, and the first mudarib and owner half each. And if it was said to him: 'What you profit, half between us' and he gave half, then for the second (and the first mudarib) the first mudarib half, and they are equal in what remains. And if it was said to him: 'What Allah provides, half of it for me' – for the first mudarib: to act (i.e., by half the profit) – that is, for the first mudarib one-sixth of it, and for the second (i.e., for the second mudarib) one-third of it (i.e., of the profit), because the payment to the second is valid since it is by the owner's command, and he (the owner) conditioned for himself half of all that Allah provides, and the first made for the second one-third, so that (the first's share) is reduced; because he cannot reduce anything from the owner's share, so one-sixth remains for him, and that is permissible for all because the owner deserves it by his capital, as it is the growth of his property. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:245) 'And it was said to him' is a circumstantial clause meaning while it was said to him, so for the owner (i.e., the second and the profit?) ... And for the second the third, i.e., for the second mudarib one-third of the profit. 'And if it was said to him' etc., i.e., if the owner said that, and the case remains as is, because the conditioned profit is what Allah provides to the mudarib, which here is two-thirds, so it is divided between them, and for the second the remaining third by condition. And similar: 'What you profit in this from something,' or 'What you have of surplus profit,' or 'What you earn in it,' or 'What you are provided in it,' or 'What becomes for you of profit,' and likewise if he conditions for the second mudarib more than one-third or less, then what remains after what he took from it is between the owner and the first. The difference between the two: in the first he conditioned half of all profit because he attributed the provision to the capital, and in the second he attributed it to the mudarib. (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 7:383) 'And if it was said to him: What you profit' etc., i.e., for the first mudarib, meaning if the owner said to him: 'What you profit, half between us,' and the first paid half, then for the second half (i.e., half the profit) because the first conditioned that for him, and his condition is valid because it is with the owner's permission, and the owner and the first mudarib are equal in what remains, which is half, because the owner here did not condition for himself except half of what the first profited, and the first only profited half, so it is half between them, and the other half became for the second by his condition, so it was not from the first's profit. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:245) And it is said in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 'There is no difference between this case and the previous except in terms of what the mudarib conditioned for the second: in the first he conditioned one-third for him, so what remained was between them, and in the second he conditioned half for him, so the remaining half is between them.' (7:383) 'And he paid half' i.e., the first mudarib to the second mudarib. (Miskin) 'And they are equal' i.e., the owner and the first mudarib are equal. (Miskin) 'What Allah provides' means if he said to him: 'Half of it for me,' i.e., half of what Allah provides of profit, or the owner said to the mudarib: 'What is of surplus, half between us,' and the first paid to another half, then for the owner half of the profit, and for the second (i.e., the second mudarib) half, and nothing for the first (i.e., for the first mudarib) because the owner's statement 'What Allah provides' or 'What is of surplus' refers to all profit, so he gets half of all, and the first mudarib conditioned for the second half of all profit, so he gets half, so nothing remains for the first, so he exits with nothing. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:245) 'And if he conditioned for the second two-thirds' i.e., the first mudarib for the second two-thirds of the profit, the case remaining as is, then the first mudarib is liable to the second for one-sixth (i.e., one-sixth of the profit) from his own wealth, because the owner conditioned for himself half of the absolute profit, so he gets that, and the second mudarib deserves two-thirds of the profit by the first's condition because his condition is valid as it is known, but it does not take effect against the owner, because he (the owner) cannot change his condition, so the first pays him the amount of one-sixth because he guaranteed the safety of two-thirds by the contract, for he deceived him in the mudaraba contract, and that is also the basis for the second to have recourse against the first. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:246) 'And if he conditioned' etc., i.e., if the mudarib conditioned for the owner one-third of the profit, and conditioned for the owner's slave one-third on condition that the slave works with him, and conditioned for himself one-third, it is valid; when the mudarib acts and profits, one-third of the profit is for the mudarib and two-thirds for the owner if the slave has no debt, and if he has debt it goes to the creditors. It is said in al-'Ayni: 'Because his conditioning for the slave is conditioning for the master, so it is as if he conditioned for the master two-thirds of the profit, and conditioning the slave's work is not corrupting because he is fit to be a mudarib in his master's property, unlike conditioning the owner's work because the owner's continued possession prevents handing the property to the mudarib, so it is not permissible. Then if the slave has no debt, it is for the master, whether the slave's work is conditioned or not; and if he has debt, it is for his creditors if his work is conditioned, otherwise it is for the master. Similarly, if he conditions one-third for the mudarib's slave, it is valid whether work is conditioned or not if he has no debt; but if he has debt, if he conditions his work it is permissible and the conditioned goes to his creditors, and if he does not condition his work it is not permissible, and at Abu Hanifa the conditioned is for the owner (of the slave? Actually 'what is conditioned for the owner'?), and according to them (the two companions) the master owns the income of his indebted slave, so conditioning for him is conditioning for the master, so it is valid.' (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:246) 'On condition that he works with him' etc. The slave's work is not a condition for validity; for if he conditioned one-third for him and did not condition his work, it is valid and is for his master, but the benefit of conditioning his work appears in that his creditors then take what was conditioned for him; otherwise it is not for them but for the master. Al-Zayla'i said: 'This is apparent because by conditioning his work he becomes a mudarib in his master's wealth, so his income is his, so his creditors take it; otherwise it is for the master etc.' (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 5:541) And from it is understood that if he conditions his work and he does not work, it is not for the creditors but for the master, because since he did not work, it is not from his income. (Fath Allah al-Mu'in)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary (sharh) from works like Ramz al-Haqa'iq and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a series of rulings on the situation where the first mudarib (agent) enters into a second mudaraba (sub-contract) with a second mudarib. The central issue is the distribution of profit when the owner (rabb al-mal) and the first mudarib have agreed on a share, and the first mudarib then contracts with a second mudarib, conditioning a portion of the profit for him. The commentary explains the share calculations based on the specific wording used by the owner.

The first scenario: The owner says 'What Allah provides, half is between us' (meaning the profit from the entire capital). The first mudarib then gives the capital to a second mudarib, conditioning one-third of the profit for him. In this case, the owner gets half of the total profit, the second mudarib gets one-third, and the first mudarib gets one-sixth. The reasoning is that the owner has a right to half of all profit, and the first mudarib cannot reduce the owner's share, so his share for himself is effectively reduced from one-third (his own share from the first mudaraba) to one-sixth after subtracting the second mudarib's share.

Second scenario: The owner says 'What Allah provides YOU (the mudarib), half between us.' Here the owner's share is half of what the first mudarib personally earns, not half of the total profit. If the first mudarib then sub-contracts, conditioning one-third of the total profit for the second, then the second gets one-third, and the owner and first mudarib split the remaining two-thirds equally? Actually the text says 'والباقي بين المالك والأول نصفان' meaning the remainder (after the second's third) is split half between owner and first. So owner gets half of two-thirds = one-third, first gets one-third as well, and second gets one-third.

Third scenario: The owner says 'What you profit, half between us.' The first mudarib then gives half the capital to a second mudarib, conditioning half the profit for him. Here the second mudarib gets half of the total profit, and the owner and first mudarib split the remaining half equally (each gets one-quarter). The reasoning is that the owner only conditioned on what the first mudarib personally profits, but since the first mudarib only profits from the half he retains (the other half is given away), the profit is only half, so the owner gets half of that half, the first gets half, and the second gets the other half of the total.

Fourth scenario: The owner says 'What Allah provides, half of it is for me' (or 'what is of surplus, half between us'). The first mudarib then sub-contracts, conditioning half of the total profit for the second. In this case, the owner gets half, the second gets half, and the first mudarib gets nothing. This is because the owner's statement covers all profit, so he gets half, and the first mudarib conditioned the other half for the second, leaving nothing for himself.

Fifth scenario: The first mudarib conditions for the second two-thirds of the profit (while the owner condition is half). The first mudarib becomes liable (daman) to pay the second one-sixth of the profit from his own wealth. This is because the owner's right to half is fixed, and the second's right to two-thirds cannot be fulfilled from the profit (as that sums to more than the whole profit), so the first mudarib must compensate the second for the shortfall, since he guaranteed the second's share by the contract.

Sixth scenario: The first mudarib conditions one-third for the owner, one-third for the owner's slave on condition that the slave works with him, and one-third for himself. This is valid. The slave's share goes to his owner (the rabb al-mal) if the slave has no debt, but if the slave has debt, the share goes to his creditors if the slave's work was conditioned; otherwise it goes to the owner. The commentary also discusses the case where the slave is the mudarib's slave, with similar rules. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: If the slave has debt and no work condition, according to Abu Hanifa the contract is not permissible, while according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is permissible because the slave's income belongs to the master regardless.

Throughout, the commentary emphasizes that the sub-mudaraba is valid because it is done with the owner's permission (either explicitly or impliedly by the owner's general statement). The differences in distribution arise from the owner's wording and the shares conditioned.

Key Terms
مضارب (mudārib): The agent who manages the capital in a mudaraba contract. In this context, the first mudarib is the one who contracts with a second mudarib (sub-contractor).
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The owner of the capital in a mudaraba contract.
مضاربة (muḍāraba): A partnership contract where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, and profits are shared according to agreement.
ضمان (ḍamān): Guarantee or liability. In this passage, the first mudarib is liable (ḍāmin) to pay the second mudarib from his own wealth when the profit share conditioned cannot be fulfilled from the actual profit.
شرط (sharṭ): Condition stipulated in the contract regarding profit sharing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the owner says 'ما رزق الله فبيننا نصفان' and the first mudarib conditions one-third for the second, what is the first mudarib's share?
A) 1/2
B) 1/3
C) 1/6
D) 0

Key Takeaway
When a mudarib subcontracts, his own profit share is the residual after fulfilling the owner's fixed share and the second mudarib's conditioned share; if the conditioned share exceeds his own, he bears personal liability.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
beginner
6 min
The Mudarib Who Over-promises: When the First Mudarib Gets Nothing
First scenario: first mudarib gives half to second

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mudarib appoints another mudarib and gives away his entire profit share, and explain why he ends up with nothing.

Core Idea
If the first mudarib gives his entire share to a second, he ends up with no profit and no compensation.

Imagine you are a mudarib managing capital. You decide to hire another mudarib to help, promising him a share. But you must be careful: if you promise away all the profit that was meant for you, you might end up empty-handed. This lesson examines the first scenario in our text: when a mudarib contracts with a second mudarib for half of the total profit, while the owner of the capital also had a claim to half.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and initial contract
The owner (rabb al-mal) enters a mudarabah with the first mudarib, with profit shared equally ('half and half'). Then the first mudarib appoints a second mudarib, giving him half of the total profit.
The owner's statement 'whatever Allah provides' covers all profit.
2
Determine each party's entitlement
The owner gets half (from the whole). The second mudarib gets half (from the whole, by the first's stipulation). The first mudarib gets nothing because he gave away his entire share.
The first mudarib's stipulation is valid but leaves nothing for himself.
3
Analyze the legal basis
The permissibility is based on istihsan (juristic preference) due to custom and need. The first mudarib's share is essentially transferred to the second, so he has no residual claim.
The text from Rumuz al-Haqaiq states this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة
المضارب يضارب من غيره
أو ما كان من فضل فبيننا نصفان فدفع بالنصف، فللمالك النصف، وللثاني النصف، ولا شيء أي للمضارب الثاني أي ربح المضارب الأول أي رب المال للأول، ولو شرط للثاني ثلثيه ضمن الأول للثاني سدسا، وإن أي للمضارب الأول للمضارب الثاني المضارب الأول من ماله من الربح شرط للمالك ثلثه، ولعبده ثلثه على أن يعمل معه، ولنفسه ثلثه، صح، الربح المالك عبد المالك المضارب الشرط النصف منه، ولا شيء للأول؛ لأن قول رب المال: "ما رزق الله تعالى" أو "ما كان من فضل" ينصرف إلى جميع الربح فيكون له النصف من الجميع، وقد شرط المضارب الأول للثاني نصف جميع الربح، فيكون له النصف، فلم يبق للأول شيء من الربح، فيخرج بغير شيء. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٥/٢] ولو شرط إلخ : أي المضارب الأول للثاني ثلثيه أي ثلثي الربح، والمسألة بحالها، ضمن المضارب الأول للثاني أي للمضارب الثاني سدساً أي سدس الربح من ماله؛ لأن رب المال شرط لنفسه النصف من مطلق الربح، فله ذلك، واستحق المضارب الثاني ثلثي الربح بشرط الأول؛ لأن شرطه صحيح؛ لكونه معلوماً، لكن لا ينفذ في حق رب المال؛ إذ لا يقدر أن يغير شرطه فيغرم له قدر السدس؛ لأنه ضمن له سلامة الثلثين بالعقد؛ لأنه غره في ضمن عقد المضاربة، وهو أيضاً سبب الرجوع للثاني على الأول. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢]
وإن شرط إلخ : أي وإن شرط المضارب لرب المال ثلث الربح، وشرط لعبد رب المال ثلثه على أن يعمل العبد مع المضارب وشرط لنفسه ثلثه صح؛ فإذا تصرف المضارب وربح يكون ثلث الربح للمضارب وثلثاه لرب المال إن لم يكن على العبد دين، وإن كان عليه دين فهو للغرماء، قال في "العيني": لأن اشتراطه للعبد يكون اشتراطاً للمولى، فكأنه اشترط للمولى ثلثي الربح، واشتراط عمل العبد غير مفسد؛ لأنه من أهل أن يضارب في مال مولاه، بخلاف ما إذا شرط عمل رب المال؛ لأن بقاء يده يمنع تسليم المال إلى المضارب، فلا يجوز. ثم إن لم يكن على العبد دين فهو للمولى، سواء شرط فيها عمل العبد أو لا، وإن كان عليه دين فهو لغرمائه إن شرط عمله وإلا فهو للمولى، وكذلك إذا شرط الثلث لعبد المضارب يصح، سواء اشترط العمل أو لا إن لم يكن عليه دين وإن كان عليه دين إن شرط عليه عمله جاز، وكان المشروط لغرمائه، وإن لم يشترط عمله لا يجوز، ويكون ما شرط لرب المال عند أبي حنيفة له، وعندهما يملك المولى كسب عبده المديون، فاشتراطه له يكون اشتراطاً للمولى، فيصح. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢] على أن يعمل معه إلخ عمل العبد ليس بقيد للصحة؛ إذ لو اشترط له الثلث، و لم يشترط عمله صح، ويكون لمولاه، لكن فائدة اشتراط عمله تظهر في أخذ غرمائه ما شرطه له حينئذ وإلا فليس لهم بل للمولى، قال الزيلعي: وهذا ظاهر؛ لأنه باشتراط عمله صار مضارباً في مال مولاه فيكون كسبه له، فيأخذه غرماؤه، وإلا فهو للمولى إلخ. تبيين الحقائق ٥٤١/٥] واستفيد منه أنه إذا اشترط عمله فلم يعمل، لم يكن للغرماء، بل للمولى؛ لأنه حيث لم يعمل لم يكن من كسبه.(فتح الله المعين)
Book of Mudarabah. The mudarib enters into a mudarabah with another. Or 'whatever surplus occurs, it is half between us,' so he gave half, then the owner gets half, the second gets half, and nothing for the first mudarib. And if he stipulated for the second two-thirds, the first mudarib guarantees for the second one-sixth from his own property of the profit. And if he stipulated for the owner one-third, and for his slave one-third on condition that the slave works with him, and for himself one-third, it is valid. The profit: the owner gets half of it, and nothing for the first; because the owner's statement 'whatever Allah provides' or 'whatever surplus occurs' applies to all profit, so he gets half of all, and the first mudarib stipulated for the second half of all profit, so the second gets half, leaving nothing for the first. [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 2:245] And if he stipulated etc.: meaning the first mudarib stipulated for the second two-thirds of the profit, the case remains as before; the first mudarib guarantees for the second one-sixth of the profit from his own property; because the owner stipulated half of the absolute profit for himself, so he gets that, and the second mudarib becomes entitled to two-thirds by the first's stipulation; because his stipulation is valid as it is known, but it is not enforceable against the owner's right, so he pays him the amount of one-sixth because he guaranteed him the two-thirds by the contract, and because he deceived him within the contract of mudarabah, and this is also a cause for the second to recourse against the first. [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 2:246] And if he stipulated etc.: meaning if the mudarib stipulated for the owner one-third of the profit, and for the owner's slave one-third on condition that the slave works with the mudarib, and for himself one-third, it is valid. Then when the mudarib transacts and makes profit, one-third of the profit is for the mudarib and two-thirds for the owner if the slave has no debt; if he has debt, it is for the creditors. Al-'Ayni said: because stipulating for the slave is stipulating for the master, so it is as if he stipulated for the master two-thirds. Stipulating the slave's work is not corrupting because he is eligible to act as mudarib in his master's wealth, unlike stipulating the owner's work because his hand remaining prevents delivery of capital to the mudarib, so it is not permissible. Then if the slave has no debt, it goes to the master, whether he stipulated the slave's work or not. If he has debt, it goes to his creditors if he stipulated his work; otherwise it goes to the master. Similarly, if he stipulated one-third for the mudarib's slave, it is valid whether he stipulated work or not if the slave has no debt; if he has debt and he stipulated his work, it is valid and the stipulated amount goes to his creditors; if he did not stipulate his work, it is not valid, and what he stipulated goes to the owner according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two disciples the master owns his debtor slave's earnings, so stipulating for him is stipulating for the master, thus valid. [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 2:246] 'On condition that he works with him' etc.: the slave's work is not a condition for validity; because if he stipulated one-third for him and did not stipulate work, it is valid and goes to his master, but the benefit of stipulating work appears in the creditors taking what was stipulated for him then, otherwise it is not for them but for the master. Al-Zayla'i said: This is apparent because by stipulating his work, he becomes a mudarib in his master's wealth, so his earnings belong to him, so his creditors take them; otherwise it is for the master. From Tabyin al-Haqaiq 5:541. It is derived from this that if he stipulated his work but he did not work, it is not for the creditors but for the master, because since he did not work, it is not his earnings. (Fath Allah al-Mu'in)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the rules of a mudarib appointing another mudarib. It presents three scenarios under the same heading. In the first scenario, the owner of capital says the profit is shared equally, but the first mudarib contracts with a second mudarib giving him half of the total profit. As a result, the owner gets his half (from the whole), the second gets his half (from the whole), and the first gets nothing because he gave away all his share. In the second scenario, the first mudarib gives the second two-thirds of the profit. Here, he must compensate the second out of his own pocket for the shortfall because the owner's right to his half cannot be overridden. The third scenario involves stipulating shares for the owner, a slave of the owner, and the mudarib himself. The slave's work may be stipulated or not. The key point is that stipulating for the slave is effectively stipulating for the master. If the slave has creditors, the profit goes to them if work was stipulated; otherwise to the master. Similar rules apply when the mudarib stipulates for his own slave. Throughout, the Hanafi position is that the validity of stipulations depends on knowledge and the absence of harm to the owner's rights, and the mudarib bears liability if he guarantees a share that conflicts with the owner's stipulated share.

Key Terms
المضارب (al-mudarib): The person who invests the capital; here, the first mudarib who appoints a second mudarib.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The owner of the capital.
شرط (shart): A condition stipulating profit shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first scenario, what is the first mudarib's profit share?
A) Half
B) Nothing
C) One-quarter
D) Depends on the owner's permission

Key Takeaway
A mudarib must not promise more profit to a second mudarib than his own share, lest he end up with no profit.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
7 min
Guaranteeing Another's Share: Mudarib's Liability for Over-commitment
Second scenario: mudarib guarantees two-thirds, must pay 1/6

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the compensation due when a mudarib promises a second mudarib a share exceeding his own profit entitlement, and explain why he must pay from his own wealth.

Core Idea
If the first mudarib promises more than his share, he must compensate the shortfall from his own property.

What happens if a mudarib gets overambitious and promises a second mudarib a larger share than he himself is entitled to? The Hanafi school holds that the first mudarib becomes a guarantor (damin) and must pay the difference from his own pocket. This lesson focuses on the second scenario from our text, where the first mudarib stipulates two-thirds for the second while the owner claimed half.

Guided Path
1
Set up the scenario
Owner and first mudarib: profit half and half. First mudarib promises second mudarib two-thirds of total profit.
The owner's half is fixed: he gets 50% of the total.
2
Identify the conflict
The second mudarib is promised 2/3 (≈66.67%) but the owner takes 1/2 (50%). The total exceeds 100%? Actually, the owner's 50% leaves 50% for the first mudarib, but he promised 66.67%, so there is a shortfall of 16.67% (1/6).
The first mudarib's promise exceeds his own share.
3
Determine the compensation
The first mudarib must pay the second mudarib 1/6 of the total profit from his own property, because his stipulation is valid but does not bind the owner. He guaranteed the second's share by contract, so he must make it good.
The text says 'dhamina al-awwal lil-thalithi sudasan'.
4
Understand the legal reason (talil)
The first mudarib 'deceived' the second within the contract by guaranteeing a share he could not deliver, so he is liable. This is a form of istihsan based on custom and protecting the second's reliance.
The second can recourse against the first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة
المضارب يضارب من غيره
أو ما كان من فضل فبيننا نصفان فدفع بالنصف، فللمالك النصف، وللثاني النصف، ولا شيء أي للمضارب الثاني أي ربح المضارب الأول أي رب المال للأول، ولو شرط للثاني ثلثيه ضمن الأول للثاني سدسا، وإن أي للمضارب الأول للمضارب الثاني المضارب الأول من ماله من الربح شرط للمالك ثلثه، ولعبده ثلثه على أن يعمل معه، ولنفسه ثلثه، صح، الربح المالك عبد المالك المضارب الشرط النصف منه، ولا شيء للأول؛ لأن قول رب المال: "ما رزق الله تعالى" أو "ما كان من فضل" ينصرف إلى جميع الربح فيكون له النصف من الجميع، وقد شرط المضارب الأول للثاني نصف جميع الربح، فيكون له النصف، فلم يبق للأول شيء من الربح، فيخرج بغير شيء. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٥/٢] ولو شرط إلخ : أي المضارب الأول للثاني ثلثيه أي ثلثي الربح، والمسألة بحالها، ضمن المضارب الأول للثاني أي للمضارب الثاني سدساً أي سدس الربح من ماله؛ لأن رب المال شرط لنفسه النصف من مطلق الربح، فله ذلك، واستحق المضارب الثاني ثلثي الربح بشرط الأول؛ لأن شرطه صحيح؛ لكونه معلوماً، لكن لا ينفذ في حق رب المال؛ إذ لا يقدر أن يغير شرطه فيغرم له قدر السدس؛ لأنه ضمن له سلامة الثلثين بالعقد؛ لأنه غره في ضمن عقد المضاربة، وهو أيضاً سبب الرجوع للثاني على الأول. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢]
وإن شرط إلخ : أي وإن شرط المضارب لرب المال ثلث الربح، وشرط لعبد رب المال ثلثه على أن يعمل العبد مع المضارب وشرط لنفسه ثلثه صح؛ فإذا تصرف المضارب وربح يكون ثلث الربح للمضارب وثلثاه لرب المال إن لم يكن على العبد دين، وإن كان عليه دين فهو للغرماء، قال في "العيني": لأن اشتراطه للعبد يكون اشتراطاً للمولى، فكأنه اشترط للمولى ثلثي الربح، واشتراط عمل العبد غير مفسد؛ لأنه من أهل أن يضارب في مال مولاه، بخلاف ما إذا شرط عمل رب المال؛ لأن بقاء يده يمنع تسليم المال إلى المضارب، فلا يجوز. ثم إن لم يكن على العبد دين فهو للمولى، سواء شرط فيها عمل العبد أو لا، وإن كان عليه دين فهو لغرمائه إن شرط عمله وإلا فهو للمولى، وكذلك إذا شرط الثلث لعبد المضارب يصح، سواء اشترط العمل أو لا إن لم يكن عليه دين وإن كان عليه دين إن شرط عليه عمله جاز، وكان المشروط لغرمائه، وإن لم يشترط عمله لا يجوز، ويكون ما شرط لرب المال عند أبي حنيفة له، وعندهما يملك المولى كسب عبده المديون، فاشتراطه له يكون اشتراطاً للمولى، فيصح. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢] على أن يعمل معه إلخ عمل العبد ليس بقيد للصحة؛ إذ لو اشترط له الثلث، و لم يشترط عمله صح، ويكون لمولاه، لكن فائدة اشتراط عمله تظهر في أخذ غرمائه ما شرطه له حينئذ وإلا فليس لهم بل للمولى، قال الزيلعي: وهذا ظاهر؛ لأنه باشتراط عمله صار مضارباً في مال مولاه فيكون كسبه له، فيأخذه غرماؤه، وإلا فهو للمولى إلخ. تبيين الحقائق ٥٤١/٥] واستفيد منه أنه إذا اشترط عمله فلم يعمل، لم يكن للغرماء، بل للمولى؛ لأنه حيث لم يعمل لم يكن من كسبه.(فتح الله المعين)
Book of Mudarabah. The mudarib enters into a mudarabah with another. Or 'whatever surplus occurs, it is half between us,' so he gave half, then the owner gets half, the second gets half, and nothing for the first mudarib. And if he stipulated for the second two-thirds, the first mudarib guarantees for the second one-sixth from his own property of the profit. And if he stipulated for the owner one-third, and for his slave one-third on condition that the slave works with him, and for himself one-third, it is valid. The profit: the owner gets half of it, and nothing for the first; because the owner's statement 'whatever Allah provides' or 'whatever surplus occurs' applies to all profit, so he gets half of all, and the first mudarib stipulated for the second half of all profit, so the second gets half, leaving nothing for the first. [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 2:245] And if he stipulated etc.: meaning the first mudarib stipulated for the second two-thirds of the profit, the case remains as before; the first mudarib guarantees for the second one-sixth of the profit from his own property; because the owner stipulated half of the absolute profit for himself, so he gets that, and the second mudarib becomes entitled to two-thirds by the first's stipulation; because his stipulation is valid as it is known, but it is not enforceable against the owner's right, so he pays him the amount of one-sixth because he guaranteed him the two-thirds by the contract, and because he deceived him within the contract of mudarabah, and this is also a cause for the second to recourse against the first. [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 2:246] And if he stipulated etc.: meaning if the mudarib stipulated for the owner one-third of the profit, and for the owner's slave one-third on condition that the slave works with the mudarib, and for himself one-third, it is valid. Then when the mudarib transacts and makes profit, one-third of the profit is for the mudarib and two-thirds for the owner if the slave has no debt; if he has debt, it is for the creditors. Al-'Ayni said: because stipulating for the slave is stipulating for the master, so it is as if he stipulated for the master two-thirds. Stipulating the slave's work is not corrupting because he is eligible to act as mudarib in his master's wealth, unlike stipulating the owner's work because his hand remaining prevents delivery of capital to the mudarib, so it is not permissible. Then if the slave has no debt, it goes to the master, whether he stipulated the slave's work or not. If he has debt, it goes to his creditors if he stipulated his work; otherwise it goes to the master. Similarly, if he stipulated one-third for the mudarib's slave, it is valid whether he stipulated work or not if the slave has no debt; if he has debt and he stipulated his work, it is valid and the stipulated amount goes to his creditors; if he did not stipulate his work, it is not valid, and what he stipulated goes to the owner according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two disciples the master owns his debtor slave's earnings, so stipulating for him is stipulating for the master, thus valid. [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 2:246] 'On condition that he works with him' etc.: the slave's work is not a condition for validity; because if he stipulated one-third for him and did not stipulate work, it is valid and goes to his master, but the benefit of stipulating work appears in the creditors taking what was stipulated for him then, otherwise it is not for them but for the master. Al-Zayla'i said: This is apparent because by stipulating his work, he becomes a mudarib in his master's wealth, so his earnings belong to him, so his creditors take them; otherwise it is for the master. From Tabyin al-Haqaiq 5:541. It is derived from this that if he stipulated his work but he did not work, it is not for the creditors but for the master, because since he did not work, it is not his earnings. (Fath Allah al-Mu'in)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the rules of a mudarib appointing another mudarib. It presents three scenarios under the same heading. In the first scenario, the owner of capital says the profit is shared equally, but the first mudarib contracts with a second mudarib giving him half of the total profit. As a result, the owner gets his half (from the whole), the second gets his half (from the whole), and the first gets nothing because he gave away all his share. In the second scenario, the first mudarib gives the second two-thirds of the profit. Here, he must compensate the second out of his own pocket for the shortfall because the owner's right to his half cannot be overridden. The third scenario involves stipulating shares for the owner, a slave of the owner, and the mudarib himself. The slave's work may be stipulated or not. The key point is that stipulating for the slave is effectively stipulating for the master. If the slave has creditors, the profit goes to them if work was stipulated; otherwise to the master. Similar rules apply when the mudarib stipulates for his own slave. Throughout, the Hanafi position is that the validity of stipulations depends on knowledge and the absence of harm to the owner's rights, and the mudarib bears liability if he guarantees a share that conflicts with the owner's stipulated share.

Key Terms
ضمن (damin): The first mudarib becomes a guarantor (damin) for the second mudarib's share when he overpromises.
سدس (sudus): One-sixth; the amount of compensation paid by the first mudarib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the first mudarib promises the second two-thirds while the owner is entitled to half, how much must the first mudarib pay from his own pocket?
A) One-half of the profit
B) One-sixth of the profit
C) One-third of the profit
D) Nothing, the second bears the loss

Key Takeaway
A mudarib who promises more than his own profit share becomes personally liable for the difference.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
advanced
9 min
Stipulations for a Slave: Work, Debt, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Third scenario: stipulating for slaves, work, debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on stipulating profit shares for a slave (of the owner or the mudarib) considering debt and work conditions, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a debtor slave's earnings.

Core Idea
Stipulating a share for a slave is essentially for the master, but debt changes entitlement if work is stipulated.

This third scenario from our text involves more complexity: the mudarib stipulates profit shares for the owner, a slave of the owner, and himself. The slave's work may or may not be required, and the slave may have creditors. The rulings differ based on these conditions, and there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement about who owns the earnings of a debtor slave.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic scenario
Mudarib stipulates: owner gets 1/3, owner's slave gets 1/3 (with condition to work with the mudarib), and the mudarib gets 1/3. The contract is valid.
The slave's share is effectively the master's, because the slave cannot own property in Hanafi law.
2
Analyze the effect of debt on the slave
If the slave has no debt, the profit goes to the master. If the slave has debt, and work was stipulated, the profit goes to the slave's creditors; if work was not stipulated, it goes to the master.
The work condition makes the earnings belong to the slave (as mudarib), so creditors can take it.
3
Examine similar rule for the mudarib's own slave
If the mudarib stipulates 1/3 for his own slave, the same rules apply. But if the slave is indebted and no work stipulated, Abu Hanifa says the stipulation is invalid and the share goes to the owner (mudarib's master? Actually the text says 'to the owner' - but careful: the mudarib's slave's master is the mudarib? In Hanafi, a slave cannot own, so what is stipulated for the mudarib's slave ultimately goes to the mudarib? The text says: 'it is not valid, and what he stipulated goes to the owner according to Abu Hanifa' - probably meaning the owner of the capital? Need to check commentary. Let's rely on the translation: 'if he did not stipulate his work, it is not valid, and what he stipulated goes to the owner according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two disciples the master owns his debtor slave's earnings, so stipulating for him is stipulating for the master, thus valid.' So the dispute is about the validity of the stipulation when the slave has debt and no work condition.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the stipulation is invalid if the slave has debt and no work condition, so the share goes to the owner of capital? Actually the text says 'it is not valid, and what he stipulated goes to the owner at Abu Hanifa' - likely meaning the owner of the capital (rabb al-mal). Under the two disciples, it is valid and goes to the master (the mudarib).
Practical difference: whether the share is taken by the owner of capital (Abu Hanifa) or by the mudarib (disciples).
5
Synthesize the work condition's role
Stipulating work is not a condition for validity, but it affects who gets the profit when the slave has debt. If work is stipulated, the slave is like a mudarib, so his earnings go to his creditors. Without work, the share is simply a gift to the master.
This is clarified by al-Zayla'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة
المضارب يضارب من غيره
أو ما كان من فضل فبيننا نصفان فدفع بالنصف، فللمالك النصف، وللثاني النصف، ولا شيء أي للمضارب الثاني أي ربح المضارب الأول أي رب المال للأول، ولو شرط للثاني ثلثيه ضمن الأول للثاني سدسا، وإن أي للمضارب الأول للمضارب الثاني المضارب الأول من ماله من الربح شرط للمالك ثلثه، ولعبده ثلثه على أن يعمل معه، ولنفسه ثلثه، صح، الربح المالك عبد المالك المضارب الشرط النصف منه، ولا شيء للأول؛ لأن قول رب المال: "ما رزق الله تعالى" أو "ما كان من فضل" ينصرف إلى جميع الربح فيكون له النصف من الجميع، وقد شرط المضارب الأول للثاني نصف جميع الربح، فيكون له النصف، فلم يبق للأول شيء من الربح، فيخرج بغير شيء. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٥/٢] ولو شرط إلخ : أي المضارب الأول للثاني ثلثيه أي ثلثي الربح، والمسألة بحالها، ضمن المضارب الأول للثاني أي للمضارب الثاني سدساً أي سدس الربح من ماله؛ لأن رب المال شرط لنفسه النصف من مطلق الربح، فله ذلك، واستحق المضارب الثاني ثلثي الربح بشرط الأول؛ لأن شرطه صحيح؛ لكونه معلوماً، لكن لا ينفذ في حق رب المال؛ إذ لا يقدر أن يغير شرطه فيغرم له قدر السدس؛ لأنه ضمن له سلامة الثلثين بالعقد؛ لأنه غره في ضمن عقد المضاربة، وهو أيضاً سبب الرجوع للثاني على الأول. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢]
وإن شرط إلخ : أي وإن شرط المضارب لرب المال ثلث الربح، وشرط لعبد رب المال ثلثه على أن يعمل العبد مع المضارب وشرط لنفسه ثلثه صح؛ فإذا تصرف المضارب وربح يكون ثلث الربح للمضارب وثلثاه لرب المال إن لم يكن على العبد دين، وإن كان عليه دين فهو للغرماء، قال في "العيني": لأن اشتراطه للعبد يكون اشتراطاً للمولى، فكأنه اشترط للمولى ثلثي الربح، واشتراط عمل العبد غير مفسد؛ لأنه من أهل أن يضارب في مال مولاه، بخلاف ما إذا شرط عمل رب المال؛ لأن بقاء يده يمنع تسليم المال إلى المضارب، فلا يجوز. ثم إن لم يكن على العبد دين فهو للمولى، سواء شرط فيها عمل العبد أو لا، وإن كان عليه دين فهو لغرمائه إن شرط عمله وإلا فهو للمولى، وكذلك إذا شرط الثلث لعبد المضارب يصح، سواء اشترط العمل أو لا إن لم يكن عليه دين وإن كان عليه دين إن شرط عليه عمله جاز، وكان المشروط لغرمائه، وإن لم يشترط عمله لا يجوز، ويكون ما شرط لرب المال عند أبي حنيفة له، وعندهما يملك المولى كسب عبده المديون، فاشتراطه له يكون اشتراطاً للمولى، فيصح. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢] على أن يعمل معه إلخ عمل العبد ليس بقيد للصحة؛ إذ لو اشترط له الثلث، و لم يشترط عمله صح، ويكون لمولاه، لكن فائدة اشتراط عمله تظهر في أخذ غرمائه ما شرطه له حينئذ وإلا فليس لهم بل للمولى، قال الزيلعي: وهذا ظاهر؛ لأنه باشتراط عمله صار مضارباً في مال مولاه فيكون كسبه له، فيأخذه غرماؤه، وإلا فهو للمولى إلخ. تبيين الحقائق ٥٤١/٥] واستفيد منه أنه إذا اشترط عمله فلم يعمل، لم يكن للغرماء، بل للمولى؛ لأنه حيث لم يعمل لم يكن من كسبه.(فتح الله المعين)

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the rules of a mudarib appointing another mudarib. It presents three scenarios under the same heading. In the first scenario, the owner of capital says the profit is shared equally, but the first mudarib contracts with a second mudarib giving him half of the total profit. Key Terms
عبد (abd): A slave; in this context, either the owner's slave or the mudarib's slave.
غرماء (ghurama): Creditors of the slave.
اشتراط العمل (ishtirat al-ʿamal): Stipulating that the slave works alongside the mudarib.

If a mudarib stipulates 1/3 for the owner's slave with work condition, and the slave has debts, where does that 1/3 go?

Key Takeaway
Conditions like work and debt status significantly affect profit distribution when stipulating for a slave in mudarabah.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
8 min
Termination by Death and Apostasy of the Owner
Rulings on what terminates a mudarabah and effects of dismissal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on when a mudarabah becomes void upon death or apostasy of the owner, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability after apostasy.

Core Idea
Mudarabah ends by death of either party; apostasy of the owner with joining suspends the mudarib's actions pending fate.

This lesson examines how a mudarabah contract terminates. The classical Hanafi texts discuss death, apostasy, and other events. A key point is the suspension of the mudarib's authority after the owner's apostasy, and the difference between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples on who bears liability for post-apostasy transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify events that void mudarabah immediately
Death of either party, killing, interdiction, and continuous insanity void the contract because mudarabah is an agency, which ends with death or incapacity.
The text cites Rumuz al-Haqaiq and al-Fath for this ruling.
2
Understand the effect of owner's apostasy with joining
The mudarib's actions are suspended until the owner's fate is known. If the owner returns to Islam, actions are valid; if he dies or is killed as an apostate, they are void.
Joining dar al-harb is considered like death.
3
Analyze the liability dispute after apostasy
Abu Hanifa: liability for transactions after apostasy is on the owner, as the mudarib is like a restricted minor. The two disciples: liability is on the mudarib with recourse to the owner.
Thamarah al-khilaf: if the mudarib cannot recover, Abu Hanifa's view protects the third party.
4
Distinguish the case of the mudarib's apostasy
If the mudarib apostatizes, the mudarabah continues because he has no ownership in the capital; his capacity to act remains intact.
This contrasts with the owner's apostasy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتبطل بموت أحدهما أو بلحوق المالك مرتدا، وينعزل بعزله إن علم، وإن علم أي المضاربة المالك أو المضارب أي دار الحرب المضارب بعزله بيعه وتبطل بموت أحدهما: أي تبطل المضاربة بموت رب المال أو المضارب؛ لأن المضاربة وكالة، وهي تبطل به، ولا تورث. رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢] وقال في "الفتح": لكونها وكالة وكذا بقتله، وحجر يطرء على أحدهما، وبجنون أحدهما مطبقاً، در عن القهستاني) وفيه عن البزازية: مات المضارب والمال عروض باعها وصيه، ولو مات رب المال والمال نقد تبطل في حق التصرف، ولو عروضاً تبطل في حق المسافرة، لا التصرف، فله بعرض ونقد. (فتح) أو بلحوق إلخ : أي تبطل أيضاً بلحوق المالك بدار الحرب حال كونه مرتداً؛ لأنه بمنزلة الموت، ولهذا يورث ماله وتعتق أمهات أولاده ومدبروه وقبل لحوقه أي الحكم بلحوقه يتوقف تصرف مضاربه عند أبي حنيفة، إن أسلم نفذ وإن مات أو قتل على الارتداد بطل، قال في "ملا مسكين": وقيد بالمالك؛ لأنه لو ارتد المضارب ولحق فالمضاربة على حالها عندهم. رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢] قال في "الفتح" : هذا مخالف لما نقله الحموي عن "الولوالجية"، وجه كون المضاربة على حالها: أن تصرفاته إنما توقفت لمكان توقفه في ملكه ولا ملك له هنا في مال المضاربة وله عبارة صحيحة؛ لأن صحتها بالآدمية والتمييز، ولا خلل في ذلك، والعبارة الصحيحة مبنى صحة الوكالة، ولا توقف في ملك رب المال؛ لأن توقف تصرف المرتد لتعلق حق الوارث ولا تعلق لورثة المضارب بملك رب المال، فبقيت المضاربة على حالها، خلا أن ما يلحقه العهدة فيما باع واشترى يكون على رب المال في قول أبي حنيفة؛ لان حكم العهدة يتوقف بردته؟ من لأنه لو لزمته لقضى من ماله ولا تصرف له فيه فكان كالصبي المحجور إذا توكل عن غيره بالبيع والشراء، وفي قولهما حاله في التصرف بعد الردة كهي فيه قبلها، فالعهدة عليه ويرجع على رب المال، كذا في "الزيلعي" عن "العناية". (عيني، ملا مسكين، فتح) يستفاد بلحوق المالك إلخ : لأن اللحوق بمنزلة الموت، والمراد بالمالك خصوص الرجل، ولهذا قال في "غاية البيان": ولو كان رب المال امرأة فارتدت فهي بمنزلة المسلمة؛ لأنها لا تقتل فلم تنعقد الردة سبب التلف في حقهما. (فتح) وينعزل إلخ: أي ينعزل المضارب بعزل رب المال إن علم به؛ لأنه وكيل وإن لم يعلم لا، والمراد بالعلم ما خبر رجلين مطلقاً، أو واحد عدل إن كان فضولياً، وإلا فخبر مميز. [البحر الرائق: ٣٨٥/٧] من إن علم إلخ: لا فرق في اشتراط العلم بالعزل بين العزل الحكمي وغيره في المضاربة، بخلاف الوكيل، فإنه ينعزل في الحكمي وإن لم يعلم كذا في "البحر" و"الزيلعي" . (فتح) وإن علم إلخ أي وإن علم المضارب بعزله والمال عروض باعها ولو نسيئة ولو نهاه ولا يملك فسخها في هذه الحالة ولا تخصيص الإذن؛ لأنه عزل من وجه، بخلاف أحد الشريكين إذا فسخها ومالها أمتعة، ولا يمنع المضارب العزل عن بيعها؛ لأن له حقاً في الربح، ولا يظهر إلا بالنقد، فثبت له حق البيع؛ ليظهر ذلك، وموته وارتداده مع اللحوق وجنونه مطبقاً والمال عروض كعزله والمال عروض كذا في "الزيلعي [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢]
And it becomes void by death of either of them or by the owner joining dar al-harb as an apostate, and the mudarib is dismissed by his dismissal if he knows. And it becomes void by death of either: meaning the mudarabah becomes void by death of the owner of capital or the mudarib, because mudarabah is an agency, and it becomes void by death, and it is not inherited. [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 2:246] And in al-Fath: because it is an agency, and likewise by killing, or by an interdiction that occurs on one of them, or by continuous insanity of one of them. And from al-Bazzaziyya: if the mudarib dies and the capital is goods, his executor sells them; and if the owner of capital dies and the capital is cash, it becomes void regarding disposition; if goods, it becomes void regarding traveling, not regarding disposition, so he may sell goods and cash. (Fath) Or by joining etc.: meaning it also becomes void by the owner joining dar al-harb while being an apostate, because it is like death, and for this his wealth is inherited and his umm walad and mudabbars become free. Before his joining, i.e., the ruling of his joining, the disposition of his mudarib is suspended according to Abu Hanifa; if he becomes Muslim it is effective, if he dies or is killed on apostasy it is void. Mulla Miskin said: and he restricted to the owner; because if the mudarib apostatizes and joins, the mudarabah remains as it was according to them. [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 2:246] In al-Fath: this contradicts what al-Hamawi transmitted from al-Walwaljiyya. The reason that the mudarabah remains as it was: his dispositions were suspended because of suspension in his ownership, but he has no ownership here in the mudarabah capital, and he has valid speech; because its validity is based on humanity and discernment, and there is no defect in that, and valid speech is the basis for the validity of agency, and there is no suspension in the owner's ownership; because the suspension of the apostate's disposition is due to the right of heirs, and there is no connection of the mudarib's heirs to the owner's capital, so the mudarabah remains as it was, except that the liability for what he sold and bought is on the owner according to Abu Hanifa? because the ruling of liability depends on his apostasy? Because if it were upon him, it would be paid from his wealth, and he has no disposition over it, so he is like a restricted minor if he acts as agent for another in sale and purchase. According to them (the two disciples), his status in disposition after apostasy is like before it, so liability is upon him and he recourses to the owner. Thus in al-Zayla'i from al-‘Inaya. (Ayni, Mulla Miskin, Fath) It is derived from the owner's joining etc.: because joining is like death, and by 'owner' specifically a man is meant; for this it is said in Ghayat al-Bayan: if the owner was a woman and she apostatizes, she is like a Muslim woman because she is not killed, so apostasy does not become a cause of loss regarding both. (Fath) And he is dismissed etc.: meaning the mudarib is dismissed by the owner's dismissal if he knows it; because he is an agent, and if he does not know, he is not dismissed. What is meant by knowledge is the report of two men absolutely, or one just man if the mudarib is a volunteer, otherwise the report of a discerning person. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 7:385] From 'if he knows' etc.: there is no difference in requiring knowledge of dismissal between constructive dismissal and others in mudarabah, unlike the agent, who is dismissed by constructive dismissal even if he does not know, thus in al-Bahr and al-Zayla'i. (Fath) And if he knows etc.: meaning if the mudarib knows of his dismissal and the capital is goods, he sells them even on credit and even if he is prohibited, and he does not have the power to annul them in this case nor to restrict permission; because it is dismissal from one aspect, unlike one of the partners when he dissolves and the capital is goods, and the dismissal does not prevent the mudarib from selling them; because he has a right in the profit, and it only appears through cash, so he is given the right to sell to make it appear. And his death, apostasy with joining, continuous insanity while the capital is goods, is like his dismissal while the capital is goods, thus in al-Zayla'i [Rumuz al-Haqaiq 2:246]
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage discusses the termination of a mudarabah contract. It begins by stating that mudarabah is voided by the death of either the capital owner or the mudarib because it is a form of agency, which ends with death. Similarly, it ends if either party is killed, becomes interdicted, or suffers continuous insanity. Special rules apply if the capital is goods as opposed to cash. The passage then addresses the case where the owner apostatizes and joins dar al-harb. According to Abu Hanifa, the mudarib's actions are suspended pending the owner's fate: if he returns to Islam, the actions are valid; if he dies or is killed as an apostate, they are void. However, if the mudarib himself apostatizes, the mudarabah continues, as he has no ownership in the capital. The liability for transactions after apostasy differs: Abu Hanifa holds the owner liable, while the two disciples hold the mudarib liable with recourse to the owner. The passage also covers the dismissal of the mudarib by the owner. Dismissal is effective only if the mudarib knows of it. The type of knowledge required is specified. Interestingly, in mudarabah, constructive dismissal does not take effect without knowledge, unlike regular agency. Finally, if the mudarib knows he is dismissed but the capital is goods, he still has the right to sell them to realize the profit, even if the owner forbids it, because his right to profit can only be realized through cash.

Key Terms
تبطل (tabtul): Becomes void; the mudarabah contract is annulled from the moment of death or apostasy.
لحوق (luhuq): Joining dar al-harb after apostasy, considered like death in effect.
عهدة (uhdah): Liability or responsibility for debts arising from transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to a mudarib's transactions after the owner apostatizes and joins dar al-harb, if the owner subsequently dies on apostasy?
A) All transactions are valid
B) Transactions are void ab initio
C) Transactions are suspended and become void upon death
D) Transactions continue as before

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is voided by death and certain incapacities; apostasy of the owner with joining suspends the contract, with a valid intra-Hanafi dispute on liability.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate
7 min
Dismissal of the Mudarib: Knowledge and Right to Sell
Rulings on dismissal of the mudarib and his right to sell after knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule that dismissal of a mudarib requires his knowledge, and describe the exceptional right of a dismissed mudarib to sell goods to realize profit.

Core Idea
A mudarib is dismissed only upon knowledge; if dismissed while goods remain, he may still sell to extract his profit share.

This lesson focuses on the dismissal of the mudarib. Unlike regular agency, constructive dismissal does not suffice; the mudarib must actually know. Furthermore, if he knows and the capital is goods, he retains the right to sell them to realize his profit share, even if the owner prohibits it.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule of dismissal
The mudarib is dismissed by the owner's dismissal if he knows; if he does not know, he is not dismissed. This is because he is an agent.
The text cites al-Bahr al-Raiq for the definition of knowledge.
2
Define the required knowledge
Knowledge means a report of two men absolutely, or one just man if the mudarib is a volunteer (fuduli), otherwise the report of a discerning person.
This specificity ensures the mudarib has reliable information.
3
Distinguish from regular agency
In regular agency, constructive dismissal (e.g., owner's death) takes effect without knowledge. In mudarabah, even constructive dismissal requires knowledge; there is no difference in the requirement between constructive and explicit dismissal.
This is a unique Hanafi rule for mudarabah.
4
Explain the right to sell after dismissal
If the mudarib knows he is dismissed and the capital is goods, he may sell them, even on credit and even if the owner prohibits, because his right to profit only appears through cash. He does not have the power to annul the sale or restrict permission.
This right is analogous to the case of death, apostasy, or insanity of the mudarib when the capital is goods.

Source Text

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Termination of Mudarabah by Death and Apostasy
Ruling on termination of mudarabah by death and apostasy, with intra-Hanafi dispute on liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on termination of mudarabah upon death or apostasy, distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding liability, and apply the correct rule to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Mudarabah terminates by death of either party or capital owner's apostasy; mudarib's apostasy does not terminate it, but liability is disputed.

Mudarabah, being a form of agency (wakala), ends when either party dies or when the capital owner apostatises and joins enemy territory. But what if the mudarib apostatises? The school diverges: does the contract remain valid? And who bears liability for transactions during the owner's apostasy? This lesson unpacks the matn's ruling and the subsequent commentary that explores the reasoning behind each imam's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify terminating events
List the events that invalidate mudarabah: death of either party, killing, legal interdiction (hijr), continuous insanity, and apostasy of the capital owner who joins dar al-harb.
The matn explicitly states termination by death and apostasy with joining.
2
Understand the legal basis
Recognise that mudarabah is a type of wakala (agency), and wakala terminates with death. Thus, termination due to death is by analogy to wakala.
The commentator says 'li-annahā wakālah'.
3
Analyse the suspension period
Before the capital owner's apostasy is judicially established (luhūq), the mudarib's transactions are suspended according to Abu Hanifah. If the owner returns to Islam, they are effective; if he dies or is killed upon apostasy, they become void.
The suspension is due to the potential claim of the apostate's heirs.
4
Distinguish liability positions
During the suspension, if the mudarib transacts, who bears the liability (ahdah)? Abu Hanifah says the capital owner, because the mudarib is like a restricted minor. The Sahibayn say the mudarib bears it and recoups from the owner.
The Sahibayn argue the mudarib's capacity is unchanged; Abu Hanifah emphasises the heir's right over the apostate's property.
5
Apply the exception for female apostates
Notice that the ruling for the capital owner's apostasy applies only to men, because women apostates are not killed and therefore are not treated as dead.
Ghayat al-Bayan: a female owner who apostatises is like a Muslim woman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتبطل بموت أحدهما: أي تبطل المضاربة بموت رب المال أو المضارب؛ لأن المضاربة وكالة، وهي تبطل به، ولا تورث. رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٦/٢] وقال في "الفتح": لكونها وكالة وكذا بقتله، وحجر يطرء على أحدهما، وبجنون أحدهما مطبقاً، در عن القهستاني) وفيه عن البزازية: مات المضارب والمال عروض باعها وصيه، ولو مات رب المال والمال نقد تبطل في حق التصرف، ولو عروضاً تبطل في حق المسافرة، لا التصرف، فله بعرض ونقد. (عيني، ملا مسكين، فتح) يستفاد بلحوق المالك إلخ : لأن اللحوق بمنزلة الموت، والمراد بالمالك خصوص الرجل، ولهذا قال في "غاية البيان": ولو كان رب المال امرأة فارتدت فهي بمنزلة المسلمة؛ لأنها لا تقتل فلم تنعقد الردة سبب التلف في حقهما. (فتح)
And it invalidates by the death of either of them: meaning the mudarabah invalidates by the death of the owner of capital or the mudarib, because mudarabah is a wakala, and it invalidates by it, and it is not inherited. [Rumuz al-Haqa'iq 2:246] And it is said in al-Fath: because it is a wakala, and similarly by his killing, and by a hijr (interdiction) that befalls one of them, and by the insane insanity of one of them continuously, from al-Qahistani. And in it from al-Bazzaziyyah: If the mudarib died and the capital is goods, his executor sells them; and if the owner of capital died and the capital is cash, it invalidates regarding disposal; and if it is goods, it invalidates regarding travel, not disposal, so he can sell goods and cash. (Fath) Or by joining etc.: meaning it also invalidates by the owner joining dar al-harb while being an apostate, because it is like death, and therefore his property is inherited and his umm walad and mudabbars become free; and before his joining (i.e., the ruling on his joining), the disposal of his mudarib is suspended according to Abu Hanifah; if he becomes Muslim it is effective, and if he dies or is killed upon apostasy it becomes invalid. He said in "Mila Miskin": And he restricted it to the owner, because if the mudarib apostatizes and joins, the mudarabah remains as it was according to them. [Rumuz al-Haqa'iq 2:246] He said in al-Fath: This contradicts what al-Hamawi transmitted from al-Walwaljiyyah. The reason that the mudarabah remains as it is: that his disposal was only suspended due to his suspension in his ownership, and he has no ownership here in the mudarabah property, and he has a valid expression (statement) because its validity is by humanity and discernment, and there is no defect in that; and the valid expression is the basis for the validity of wakala, and there is no suspension in the ownership of the owner of capital, because the suspension of the apostate's disposal is due to the affiliation of the heir's right, and the heirs of the mudarib have no affiliation with the ownership of the owner of capital, so the mudarabah remains as it was, except that the liability (ahdah) for what he sold and bought is upon the owner of capital according to Abu Hanifah's saying, because the ruling of liability is suspended upon his apostasy? Because if it were binding on him, it would be paid from his property, and he has no disposal in it, so he is like a restricted minor if he acts as an agent for someone else in buying and selling. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), his state in disposal after apostasy is like it was before, so the liability is on him and he can recourse on the owner of capital. Thus in al-Zaylai from al-Inayah. (Ayni, Mila Miskin, Fath) It is derived from the joining of the owner etc.: because joining is like death, and by the owner is meant specifically the man, and therefore it is said in Ghayat al-Bayan: If the owner of capital was a woman and she apostatized, she is like a Muslim woman because she is not killed, so the apostasy does not become a cause of destruction in their regard. (Fath)
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on termination of mudarabah, with commentary from multiple sources. The matn states that mudarabah becomes invalid (batal) by the death of either the capital owner or the mudarib. The commentator explains this is because mudarabah is a type of wakala (agency), which by its nature terminates with death. The ruling is extended to killing, legal interdiction (hijr), and continuous insanity. Detailed sub-rulings are given: if the mudarib dies and the capital is goods, the executor may sell them; if the capital owner dies and the capital is cash, the mudarib's power to dispose ends; if it is goods, only travel is prohibited but sale is still allowed. Then the passage discusses termination if the capital owner becomes an apostate and joins dar al-harb (enemy territory). This is treated like death: his property is inherited, his umm walad and mudabbars become free. Before the joining is judicially established, the mudarib's transactions are suspended according to Abu Hanifah: if the owner returns to Islam, they are valid; if he dies or is killed on apostasy, they become void. An intra-Hanafi dispute follows: if it is the mudarib who apostatizes and joins, the mudarabah remains in effect according to the early authorities, because the mudarib has no ownership in the mudarabah property and his agency is based on his capacity as a human with valid speech. The suspension of his disposal due to apostasy is linked to the potential claims of his heirs, but since the mudarabah property is not his, his transactions are not suspended. However, there is a difference between Abu Hanifah and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding who bears the liability (ahdah) for sales: Abu Hanifah says the capital owner bears it, because the mudarib is like a restricted minor who cannot own property; the two say the mudarib bears it and then recoups from the capital owner. The passage ends with the clarification that 'owner' here means specifically a man, because a woman apostate is not killed and therefore does not cause termination.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudārabah): A partnership contract where one party provides capital and the other provides labor/professional skill for profit-sharing.
وكالة (wakālah): Agency; a contract where one person delegates authority to another to act on their behalf. Mudarabah is considered a type of wakala.
مرتد (murtadd): An apostate; one who leaves Islam. In this context, an apostate who joins dar al-harb (enemy territory) is treated as if dead regarding property and family.
لحوق بدار الحرب (luhūq bi-dār al-ḥarb): Joining enemy territory; an apostate who physically goes to enemy lands is legally considered dead for certain purposes.
عهدة (ahdah): Liability or responsibility for a debt arising from a transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following does NOT cause mudarabah to become invalid (batil) according to the matn and commentary?
A) Death of the capital owner.
B) The mudarib's apostasy without joining dar al-harb.
C) Continuous insanity of the mudarib.
D) Legal interdiction (hijr) of the capital owner.

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah terminates by death of either party or the capital owner's apostasy with joining dar al-harb; the mudarib's apostasy does not terminate it, but creates a dispute on liability.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
